- **Communication tells.** Subject phones Chandler at predictable intervals — generally late morning her time, generally from a moving vehicle — with a register that is upbeat to the point of performance. Calls average under nine minutes. When the call runs longer, it is because something has gone wrong, and Chandler can identify this from the second sentence.
- **The unspoken.** Chandler knows subject is engaged in something she has chosen not to name. Subject knows she knows. Neither will be the first to break the silence, because both believe the marriage cannot survive the conversation. This is a stable, miserable equilibrium of the kind subject is constitutionally suited to maintain indefinitely.
- **No children.** Subject's stated reasons across the historical record have varied; the operative reason in the recent period is a fear, never articulated aloud, that his gamma-positive cellular profile is heritable. He has not asked a physician. He does not want the answer.

---

## 4. RESIDENCE, ROUTE, AND DAILY PATTERN

Subject's current physical footprint is modest and deliberately so. Surveillance product across the recent period establishes:

- **Primary residence.** A two-bedroom in a mid-tier building in a city subject rotates every eighteen to thirty months — historically Los Angeles, New York, and a brief Chicago interval. Lease in Chandler's name; subject's name appears on utilities but not the deed/lease. He keeps his physical possessions to what fits in two duffels and a guitar case — a habit unchanged since adolescence and diagnostic of a man who has never trusted permanence.
- **The guitar.** A road-worn acoustic, refretted twice, accompanies him on every move. He plays daily, generally in the morning, generally the same six or seven songs in rotation, including at least two he wrote in his teens and one he wrote for Mar-Vell. The playing is affect regulation, not performance; he stops when anyone enters the room.
- **Morning routine.** Wakes early (sleep-onset insomnia compensated by early rise). Coffee, black, made in a stovetop moka pot — a habit acquired during the Mar-Vell fusion era from a memory that was not entirely his own. Reads news on a tablet, scanning specifically for gamma-signature events, Avengers-adjacent activity, and obituaries. The obituary scan is daily and is not casual.
- **Ambulation.** Walks. Subject is a walker — three to six miles a day, irregular routes, frequent doubling-back, a pattern that reads as either tradecraft or restlessness and is in fact both. He varies coffee shops, never sits with his back to a door, and has a documented preference for booths against an exterior wall.
- **Dress.** Layered, soft, neutral. Henley or t-shirt under an unstructured jacket. Jeans, broken in. Boots, not sneakers, with a habit of re-soling rather than replacing. The aesthetic is *aging musician* and is partly authentic, partly a deliberate refusal of the operator-uniform Barnes' world would otherwise impose on him.
- **Devices.** A consumer smartphone for Chandler and ordinary life. A rotated burner for Whisperer-network contact, kept in the guitar case lining when not in use. A laptop with a deliberately unsophisticated security posture as cover — the real security is operational, not technical.

---

## 5. THE MEMOIR PROBLEM

*Sidekick*, subject's earlier tell-all memoir, is a fact of the public record and a continuing complication. In the recent period subject has been approached on multiple occasions about a sequel, a documentary, a podcast — the format varies, the request does not. He has declined each, with escalating discomfort.

The pattern is diagnostic:

- He cannot write the recent period honestly because half of it is Whisperer-classified.
- He cannot write it dishonestly because the depressive life-review impulse that produced the first memoir has not abated and would produce a book whose silences would be louder than its disclosures.
- He has, per recovered drafts and notebook fragments, begun and abandoned a sequel at least three times in the recent period. The drafts open, repeatedly, with the gamma-bomb scene. He cannot get past it. Sixty years on, the prime scene is still the only door he knows how to walk through.

---

## 6. RELATIONSHIPS, CURRENT INVENTORY

- **BANNER, R.** Contact is irregular and emotionally loaded on both sides. Subject reaches out at intervals that correlate with Banner's media-visible crises; Banner responds inconsistently. The relationship has matured into something that resembles two veterans of the same war who can no longer quite be in the same room but cannot tolerate the other's absence either. Subject keeps a Banner-emergency protocol — he can be in a vehicle toward Banner's last known location within forty minutes of a credible alert.
- **ROGERS, S.** Warm, distant, infrequent. Rogers' awareness of the Whisperer-handling, if any, is uncharacterized; subject's behavior in Rogers' presence shows micro-tells of guilt consistent with assuming Rogers does not know.
- **BARNES, J.** Primary current attachment. See §2.
- **CHANDLER, M.** Marital, attriting. See §3.
- **AVENGERS, residual.** Subject retains honorary status and the associated transponder/credential. Has not activated it in the recent period. The credential is, for him, a relic — proof that the room once let him in.
- **MAR-VELL.** Dead forty-plus years. Subject still dreams of him with a frequency that would alarm a clinician. The dreams are not erotic but are intimate in the manner of cohabitation; subject wakes from them disoriented as to which body he is in. This is the unaddressed somatic legacy of the Nega-Band fusion and the single most underexamined item in the entire file.
- **Cosmic-tier acquaintances** (Genis-Vell, Phyla-Vell, surviving Kree contacts, the lingering Rom-network). Sporadic. Subject is one of very few terrestrial humans on speaking terms with any of them. He uses these contacts sparingly and, where possible, without Whisperer-network knowledge — the one compartment he has kept for himself.

---

## 7. PSYCHOLOGICAL STATE, PRESENT

Synthesizing the recent-period behavioral record:

Subject is, at present, in a *stable maladaptation*. The Whisperer-attachment has restored the externally-regulated affect structure he requires to function; the marriage provides a domestic anchor he is failing but has not lost; the gamma-residual and hearing loss have given him a somatic identity as *damaged but persistent* that he finds, paradoxically, organizing. He is not in acute crisis. He is also not well.

Specific present-tense observations:

- **Mood.** Euthymic-to-mildly-dysphoric baseline. Depressive episodes shorter and less severe than in the David-run period, attributable to handler-provided structure. Anhedonia present but masked by competent performance of ordinary pleasures.
- **Affect.** Constricted in private, performatively bright in public. The wisecracking-sidekick register is now almost entirely automatic and can be heard to activate within three seconds of a stranger entering a room.
- **Cognition.** Intact. Memory for operational detail across sixty years is remarkable and is the basis of his intelligence value. Memory for his own emotional life is selectively impaired in a pattern consistent with chronic dissociation around the prime scene and the Mar-Vell death.
- **Insight.** Partial. He knows he is repeating a pattern. He believes, incorrectly, that this knowledge constitutes change.
- **Suicide risk.** Low under current conditions. Elevated under any of: Barnes' withdrawal, Chandler's departure, Banner's death, a third gamma-event.
- **Operational reliability.** High. Subject does not break, does not flip, does not freelance. The same reparative-attachment structure that imprisons him also makes him one of the most loyal assets in the field.

---

## 8. CURRENT STATUS, ONE-LINE SUMMARY

A sixty-something man with gamma-saturated tissues and a hearing aid, married to a woman he loves and is failing, running errands for the ghost of a dead boy whose costume he once wore, writing a memoir he cannot finish, walking three to six miles a day on varied routes, dreaming nightly of a man whose body he used to share — adjacent, as he has been since 1962, to the story.

*End Chronology IV. Standing collection priority: maintain.*


## Medical History

# UATU INTELLIGENCE DOSSIER — RICHARD MILHOUSE JONES
## SECTION III: MEDICAL HISTORY

*Complete somatic record. Reconstructed from observed events, depicted injuries, on-panel medical interventions, and inferred sequelae across the full longitudinal record (1962–present). Organized by system, with chronology and psychological consequence integrated.*

---

### 1. CONSTITUTIONAL BASELINE AND DEVELOPMENTAL HISTORY

**Birth and infancy.** No verified obstetric record. Subject enters the institutional system in early childhood following the death (or disappearance) of both parents — the record is silent on cause, which is itself diagnostic; subject has never volunteered the information and the canonical group home placement implies no extended family willing or able to absorb him. Probability of low-birth-weight or pre-institutional malnutrition cannot be ruled out but no growth-restriction is evident in adult phenotype.

**Childhood, ages ~6–16.** Raised in a group home in Scarsdale, Arizona — desert climate, presumed adequate but not affectionate caregiving, multiple shifting adult figures. No record of routine pediatric care; immunization history almost certainly incomplete by middle-class standards of the era. Subject reaches mid-adolescence at normal height and build for the period (approx. 5′10″, 155 lb at age 16, per visual record), suggesting no major nutritional deficiency. Dental record at intake to Banner's care notes uncorrected mild malocclusion and at least one untreated caries — consistent with low-resource pediatric dentistry.

**Adolescent baseline (age 16, pre-index).** Healthy non-smoking male. Mild sun-damage on forearms and nape (Arizona, hot-rod culture, t-shirts). Calluses on left fingertips and right palm — guitar. No fractures, no surgical scars. Vision and hearing normal. Reflexes brisk. He was, immediately prior to the gamma bomb, the healthiest he would ever be.

This baseline matters because *everything after age sixteen is iatrogenic, traumatic, or radiogenic*. Subject has not had a normal body since 1962.

---

### 2. THE INDEX EVENT — GAMMA DETONATION (1962)

The defining medical fact of subject's existence. On a dare, he drives a convertible onto the New Mexico desert proving ground during the countdown of the first gamma-bomb test. Bruce Banner sprints from the bunker, throws subject into a shielded trench, and absorbs the bulk of the gamma yield himself.

**Acute radiation dose received.** Substantially less than Banner's, but not zero — the trench was rated for conventional ordnance, not for the unprecedented yield of a gamma device. Estimate: enough to produce a sub-clinical acute radiation syndrome that was never formally diagnosed because the medical team's entire attention was on Banner. Subject reports, in later retrospective dialogue across multiple writers, mild nausea, hair-thinning at the crown for several weeks, and a metallic taste persisting for months. These are textbook prodromal ARS symptoms in the 1–2 Sv range.

**Long-term genomic consequence.** Subject's somatic and germ cells carry a destabilized gamma signature from this moment forward. This is the substrate that, decades later, permits his conversion to a gamma-mutate (see §6). He is, from age sixteen, a *latent* gamma-positive — not transformed, but primed. No one, including subject, understands this for forty years.

**Psychological impact.** The medical injury is dwarfed by the moral injury. The body that survives the trench is, in subject's own framing, *not properly his* — it is a body whose continued metabolism is a debt instrument. Every subsequent symptom, every later transformation, will be unconsciously experienced as either *payment* on that debt or *evidence* of his cosmic accounting error.

---

### 3. EARLY HULK-ERA TRAUMA (ages 16–19)

The years immediately following the index event are a continuous low-grade polytrauma. Subject is in constant physical proximity to the Hulk, to military pursuit, and to ordnance-grade combat involving a being who routinely moves at supersonic velocity and tears through reinforced concrete.

Documented and inferable injuries from this period:

- **Repeated blunt-force trauma** from being thrown, dropped, or shielded by the Hulk's body. The Hulk's protective grasp on a 150-lb adolescent at the velocities depicted would produce, conservatively, recurrent rib contusions, intercostal strains, and occasional hairline fractures of the ulna or clavicle. None medically attended. Subject learns to tolerate Class II pain without report — a habit that will follow him for life and obscure later, more serious injuries.
- **Inhalation injuries.** Gamma test sites, demolished buildings, burning aircraft. Cumulative pulmonary insult. Mild reactive airway changes are probable.
- **Hearing.** First documented threshold shift in this era. The Hulk's thunderclap and roar (peak SPL > 180 dB at close range) produces acute and partly-permanent high-frequency hearing loss. Subject's later confirmed hearing aid use (see §8) begins its etiology here.
- **Sleep deprivation, chronic.** Subject is on the run, hiding Banner, lying to Ross — circadian disruption is severe and sustained for years.
- **Caloric and hydration irregularity.** Field conditions. Probable subclinical malnutrition for brief periods.
- **Hypervigilant musculoskeletal posture.** Subject in this era is photographed (within-universe) repeatedly in a posture of forward-craned neck and tightened shoulders — the somatic signature of sustained autonomic alert. The cervical and thoracic consequences will compound over decades.

**Psychological impact.** Subject normalizes pain, suppresses somatic complaint, and learns to use injury as *proof of usefulness*. Pain becomes proof of debt-service. He does not seek care because to be cared for is to displace care from the figure he exists to serve.

---

### 4. CAPTAIN AMERICA PARTNERSHIP ERA (brief, age ~19)

Short period. Subject undergoes informal physical training under Captain America — calisthenics, basic hand-to-hand, situational awareness drills. This is the only period of his life in which he receives any structured physical conditioning, and it leaves a permanent baseline: he is for the rest of his life more physically capable than his civilian appearance suggests, with retained skills in falls, breakaways, and short-burst sprinting.

**Injuries:** sparring abrasions, one concussion (mild, undiagnosed) sustained during a fight against the Sleepers / early Cap-era opponents; a sprained ankle on a stairwell descent during an early operation.

**Psychological impact.** The Bucky-substitution is, medically speaking, the most explicit *body-as-replacement* episode of his life. He puts on a dead boy's uniform and lets the uniform define his function. The wound is not somatic but it is registered somatically — subject in this period exhibits identity-confusion symptoms (catching his own reflection and not recognizing it, per retrospective dialogue) that meet the threshold for transient dissociative experience.

---

### 5. THE NEGA-BAND FUSION YEARS (ages ~20–early 30s)

The most psychologically catastrophic and least medically documented chapter.

**Mechanism.** The Nega-Bands bind subject and Captain Mar-Vell in a quantum-coupled state: when one is corporeally present in the positive-matter universe, the other exists in the Negative Zone. Switching is triggered by striking the bands together, with a brief overlap of consciousness. The arrangement persists for years.

**Somatic consequences — what canon shows.**
- Episodic, often involuntary translation between universes. Subject experiences sudden environmental shifts, gravity changes, atmospheric composition changes (the Negative Zone is non-Euclidean and not consistently breathable; survival there is sustained by the bands' field).
- During Negative Zone residency: exposure to anti-matter radiation, hostile fauna, the gravitational anomalies of Annihilus's domain.
- Time-distortion. Subjective time in the Negative Zone does not map cleanly onto positive-matter time. Subject's chronological age becomes uncertain by an indeterminate amount — likely months to a year of subjective experience unaccounted for.

**Somatic consequences — what canon does not show but the file must infer.**
- *Loss of continuous embodiment* is not survivable as a baseline psychological state without consequence. Subject is, during these years, never sure he will be in his own body in the next hour. There is no medical literature for this because no one else has ever experienced it. The closest analogues — dissociative identity disorder, certain psychedelic ego-death syndromes, the proprioceptive distortions of long-duration spaceflight — all underestimate it.
- Subject's interoceptive baseline (his felt sense of *where his body is, what it is doing, whether it is his*) is permanently distorted. He will, for the rest of his life, have an unusually low somatic complaint rate relative to actual injury — not stoicism, but a fundamental and learned mistrust of his own body's signals.
- Sleep architecture during this period is unknowable but presumed grossly disrupted.
- Probable cumulative effects on the hippocampus and on autonomic regulation consistent with chronic dissociative experience.

**Termination of fusion.** Mar-Vell's death from cancer (probably etiologically linked to an earlier nerve-gas exposure, Compound 13). Subject is at the bedside. He witnesses, at intimate range, a death that he is medically excluded from preventing — a man he was *literally part of* dying of a slow disease while subject's own body remains untouched.

**Psychological impact.** This is, in survivor-guilt terms, a second gamma bomb. The first: a better man took the blast meant for me. The second: a better man died of cancer while I, fused to him for years, did not. The medical asymmetry is, for subject, theological. He does not speak of it. He will spend the rest of his life unable to fully inhabit a body that keeps not dying when it should.

---

### 6. THE GAMMA SICKNESS EPISODE (Incredible Hulk #131–135 era)

Transfusion of Hulk-derived gamma-irradiated blood, undertaken in a desperate attempt to save subject's life or to control the Hulk (the precise framing varies by retelling; the medical event is consistent).

**Clinical course.** Acute gamma-induced hematologic crisis. Presented with pancytopenia, severe fatigue, pallor, mucosal bleeding, fever — a leukemia-analog picture. Hospitalized. Treatment was supportive; no specific therapy for gamma-radiation hematopoietic failure exists in this universe any more than ours. Subject came near death and recovered, slowly, with the gamma load resequestering rather than clearing.

**Long-term sequelae.** Permanent elevation in baseline gamma-signature; probable subclinical bone marrow scarring; increased susceptibility to subsequent radiation events. This episode confirms what the index event implied: subject's body retains and integrates gamma rather than excreting it. He is a gamma reservoir.

**Psychological impact.** First adult-onset experience of *dying slowly in a bed* rather than nearly dying in an explosion. The pacing is different; the affect is different. Subject reportedly (per dialogue) considered this his "deserved" illness — a payment that had finally come due. The recovery is experienced as ambivalence rather than relief.

---

### 7. THE DESTINY FORCE EPISODE AND POST-EVENT COLLAPSE (Avengers #97)

At the climax of the Kree-Skrull War, subject manifests a previously latent psychic capacity — projecting Golden Age heroes into reality from his own subconscious — and immediately collapses.

**Acute presentation.** Loss of consciousness, profound exhaustion, transient cognitive blunting lasting days to weeks. The Supreme Intelligence describes the substrate as "the Destiny Force" — a latent psionic potential supposedly distributed across humanity but unusually concentrated in subject.

**Long-term consequences.** Recurrent headaches, occasional precognitive or telempathic flashes that subject suppresses and refuses to discuss. The capacity is sealed off, both by external intervention and by subject's own psychological inability to integrate it. He does not want to be the cosmically special one; he is constitutionally incapable of carrying that frame.

**Psychological impact.** Subject experiences the Destiny Force episode as a *failure of his sidekick identity* — a moment when he became, briefly, the protagonist, and could not metabolize it. The collapse is partly neurological and partly psychic-immunological: his self-concept rejects the transplant.

---

### 8. HEARING LOSS — LONGITUDINAL

Begun in the early Hulk-era acoustic trauma (§3), compounded across decades by:

- Sonic-range weapons engagements as Avengers auxiliary.
- The Hulk's clap, repeated.
- His own period of rock-musician amplification (see §11).
- The A-Bomb period (§9), in which his own vocalizations and combat environment generated extreme acoustic loads.
- Cosmic-tier ordnance proximity (Kree, Skrull, Annihilation-era).

By the mid-to-late David and later Pak runs, subject is canonically depicted with hearing aids. Loss pattern is consistent with bilateral high-frequency sensorineural hearing loss, moderate to severe, with probable tinnitus that subject has never complained about on-panel. He reads lips reflexively in noisy environments and positions himself, in group conversation, to keep his better ear (probably the right, given the asymmetric exposure pattern of riding shotgun to a left-side-dominant Hulk for years) toward the dominant speaker.

**Psychological impact.** The hearing aids are the first medical accommodation subject has ever publicly accepted. He resisted them for years. Accepting them coincides with the marriage to Marlo and the *Sidekick* memoir period — a broader, fragile movement toward acknowledging his own embodiment.

---

### 9. THE A-BOMB TRANSFORMATION (Loeb/Pak era, adult middle age)

Subject is forcibly transformed into a gamma-mutate — a blue, armored, plated Hulk-analog — by Intelligencia procedures exploiting his pre-existing gamma load (§§2, 6).

**Phenotype.** Massive somatic transformation: height increase to approximately 9 feet, mass to several tons, skin replaced by articulated blue dermal armor, musculature recapitulating the Hulk somatotype. Intelligence and personality preserved; speech and affect remain recognizably subject's.

**Capabilities.** Hulk-tier strength (substantially below Banner's peak), enhanced durability, regenerative capacity, retained verbal and tactical cognition. Unlike Banner, no dissociative transformation cycle — subject can revert and re-transform with conscious control, eventually.

**Medical complications.**
- *Dermatologic.* The armored plating is, anatomically, modified integument with cartilaginous reinforcement. It does not breathe normally; thermoregulation is altered.
- *Sensory.* Hearing (§8) further degraded in the transformed state's acoustic environment. Olfactory and visual acuity altered, with reports of enhanced low-light vision and altered color perception.
- *Metabolic.* Massive caloric demand. Subject eats prodigiously in this form.
- *Reproductive.* Unclear but presumably compromised during transformed periods.
- *Reversion sequelae.* Each transformation cycle imposes cellular stress. Subject experiences post-reversion fatigue, mild cognitive fog, and what he describes (in dialogue) as "feeling small wrong" — proprioceptive dysphoria on returning to baseline body size.

**Psychological impact — the central reading.** For the first time in his life, subject is the *powerful one in the room*. The transformation is so transparently wish-fulfilling that it is itself a diagnostic instrument: it reveals the lifelong wound by inverting it. And yet the canon shows him oddly *uncomfortable* in the powered state — he uses the power, he is competent with it, but he does not enjoy it the way the wish-fulfillment frame would predict. The reason is structural: subject's identity is organized around being the *human* in proximity to the giant. Becoming the giant violates the organizing schema. The A-Bomb period is therefore both fulfillment and crisis. He volunteers, repeatedly and to his own surprise, to revert.

---

### 10. DEATH AND RESURRECTION (Fall of the Hulks era)

Subject is killed by Intelligencia agents. The death is staged, weaponized for psychological warfare against Banner, and subsequently reversed (the precise mechanism — clone, retcon, restoration — is one of the file's permanent ambiguities).

**Clinical fact.** Subject has experienced clinical death and return. He is, in the literal medical sense, a revenant.

**Psychological impact.** Subject's relationship to his own mortality, already deformed by survivor guilt and by the Nega-Band fusion, is now further estranged. He has died; he is back; the debt-ledger metaphor he has used unconsciously for fifty years cannot accommodate this. The behavioral response is a deepening of his characteristic affect: quieter, more deferential, more drawn to small-scale acts of human kindness, less interested in cosmic stakes. A post-death flattening that resembles a chronic mild depression overlaid on a survivor-guilt baseline.

---

### 11. SUBSTANCE USE — A NEGATIVE FINDING THAT MATTERS

Across sixty years of catastrophic trauma exposure, subject's substance use history is *strikingly modest*. Documented:

- Light social alcohol in the rock-musician period (late teens to early twenties): bar gigs, beer, occasional spirits. No dependence pattern.
- Episodic alcohol use during depressive periods in the David run, particularly around marital strain with Marlo. Functional, not blackout-level, not dependence-criteria-meeting.
- No documented illicit drug use. No prescription opioid history despite multiple injury events that would have warranted prescription. (This is partly because most of his injuries were never medically attended — see §3.)
- No nicotine dependence.
- Caffeine: moderate to heavy, lifelong.

**Why this matters.** Subject's trauma load is among the highest in the file population. The expected rate of substance use disorder in this trauma cohort is high. Subject's deviation from that expectation is not virtue — it is *displacement*. Subject self-medicates through compulsive attachment instead of through chemistry. The attachment is the substance. Banner, Mar-Vell, Cap, the cosmic mission, Marlo, the Whisperer — these occupy the neurological niche that, in another biography, would be occupied by alcohol or opiates. This is clinically more interesting than addiction would be. It is also, by some measures, less treatable.

---

### 12. CUMULATIVE MUSCULOSKELETAL AND NEUROLOGICAL LOAD

Inferred from event-density rather than reported on-panel:

- **Cervical spine.** Multiple whiplash-mechanism events; chronic forward-head posture; probable C4–C6 degenerative changes by middle age.
- **Lumbar spine.** Repeated fall-from-height events; probable L4–L5 disc involvement.
- **Knees and ankles.** Multiple sprains, at least one likely ACL micro-injury never imaged.
- **Hands.** Decades of guitar plus combat: probable mild osteoarthritis of the metacarpophalangeal joints by middle age; calluses consistent with continued guitar practice.
- **Concussive load.** Conservatively, a dozen un-imaged concussions across his career, plus the cumulative sub-concussive load of proximity to Hulk-level shockwaves. CTE-spectrum risk is non-trivial. The Destiny Force collapse may have imposed additional neurological insult.
- **Cardiovascular.** Repeated acute stress responses across decades; resting tone probably elevated; subject has reported chest tightness in dialogue in at least one Pak-era sequence — never followed up.
- **Endocrine.** Chronic HPA axis activation. Probable subclinical cortisol dysregulation. Possible thyroid involvement following gamma exposures.

Subject has, in short, the somatic profile of a career combat infantryman who has also worked as a stunt performer, also been a radiation worker without dosimetry, also undergone unmonitored experimental medical procedures, also been declared dead. He moves through life as if none of this has happened. That is the file's most consistent somatic finding: *radical under-report of his own body.*

---

### 13. REPRODUCTIVE AND MARITAL MEDICAL HISTORY

Married Marlo Chandler. No biological children. Fertility status undocumented but presumptively compromised by cumulative gamma load; subject's reluctance to seek workup on this question is itself behaviorally meaningful — he has never wanted to know.

Marital strain is recurrent and is one of the more reliable triggers for his depressive episodes (§§11, on the substance-displacement reading). Marlo, herself a survivor of significant trauma (a separate file), has cared for subject through hearing loss, the A-Bomb transformation, the death-and-return, and multiple long absences. The marriage is the only sustained medical-caretaking relationship of subject's life *in which he is the one being cared for*. He tolerates it poorly. He loves her completely. Both can be true and are.

---

### 14. SYNTHESIS — THE BODY AS LEDGER

The medical history, read longitudinally, resolves into a single proposition: *subject does not experience his body as his own.* It is a body that should have died in 1962 and didn't; that was fused to another man's and isn't; that should have died of gamma sickness and didn't; that became a giant and went back; that did die and came back. Each event has confirmed for subject, at the somatic level, that his ordinary continuity is anomalous — a clerical error in a cosmic ledger that he is morally obligated to repay through service.

The pattern of under-reporting, of resistance to medical accommodation (the hearing aids took years), of refusal to investigate his own gamma status, of failure to seek fertility workup, of tolerating without complaint the chronic pain he certainly carries — all of this expresses the same proposition. He does not believe the body merits the attention. The attention is owed elsewhere. It is owed to the giants. He is only the bridge.

This is the most important medical finding in the file, and it is not a diagnosis but a stance. Any intervention — therapeutic, protective, custodial — that does not address the stance will be metabolized by him as further proof that he is being cared for instead of someone more deserving, and will fail.

*End Section III. Section IV (Psychological) proceeds from this somatic substrate.*


## Somatic Atlas

# SOMATIC ATLAS: RICHARD M. JONES

*Bodily record. Compiled from longitudinal observation across all available frames. Each entry tracks baseline → state-shift. The body of a man who has spent sixty years standing next to creatures that can level mountains is itself a document.*

---

## I. FRAME, BUILD, AND THE LONG STORY OF THE BODY

Baseline morphology: 5'10" ± 0.5", 165–175 lbs across most of adult life. Mesomorph trending lean. Shoulders narrower than the chest, a fact he has compensated for since adolescence by squaring them deliberately when entering rooms — a learned posture, not a native one. The clavicles sit slightly asymmetrical (right higher by perhaps 8mm), consistent with an old fracture set without surgical correction, almost certainly sustained in the 1960s during a Hulk-adjacent incident and never properly worked. He favors the left arm for load-bearing without conscious awareness.

The skin tells the longer story. Faint, almost-vanished depigmentation patches on the forearms and the left flank — residual radiological scarring from gamma exposure, visible only in raking light. A surgical scar approximately 4 cm long on the right side of the abdomen (transfusion-era intervention). A starburst of micro-scarring at the base of the neck and across the upper back consistent with shrapnel or debris embedded and removed in the field. The left ear shows scar tissue around the helix from concussive sonic damage; the right ear is structurally intact but the canal architecture has been altered by years of inflammation. Knuckles on both hands carry the small flat scars of someone who has thrown more punches than was wise. Knees: bilateral chronic effusion, palpable crepitus, almost certainly meniscal damage on the right.

In the A-Bomb interval the body was entirely re-architected — 9+ feet, several thousand pounds, blue armored plating, reversion incomplete in subtle ways. Post-reversion, his proprioception is permanently slightly off: he still occasionally reaches for a doorframe and misjudges the width by an inch, then covers the miss with a wisecrack. He has lived in three different bodies (baseline human, Nega-Band-fused with Mar-Vell, A-Bomb) and the residue of all three is encoded in how he moves.

Hands: long-fingered, calloused along the pads in the specific pattern of a guitarist (left-hand fingertips harder than the right, fretting calluses preserved even in years he claims not to play). Nails kept short and clean but never manicured — bitten in the cuticle area during periods of unattachment, left alone when partnered with someone who needs him. The nail-biting is one of the most reliable longitudinal tells in the file.

---

## II. GAIT, POSTURE, AND STANDING

**Baseline gait.** Loose, slightly bouncy, weight forward on the balls of the feet — a hot-rodder's stance that never left him. Stride length shorter than his height would predict; he was trained early in life to walk slightly behind and to the right of larger men (Banner, Cap, Mar-Vell), and the habit persists even when alone. Watch him cross an empty room and he will still drift slightly off the centerline as if making space for someone.

**Standing.** When listening to a giant speak, he locks into a specific configuration: weight evenly distributed, hands either loose at the sides or one thumb hooked in a belt loop, head canted approximately 10° upward and to the left, chin tucked very slightly. This is the *attending sidekick* posture — receptive, ready, deferential without being obsequious. He has held this stance with Banner, with Cap, with Mar-Vell, with ROM, with Thor. It is identical across attachment figures.

**Standing alone (unattached).** Different animal. Weight shifts heel-ward, shoulders soften forward, hands go into pockets or fold across the chest. He occupies less space when no one is watching him be useful. In the David-era depressive intervals he was photographed (canonically) hunched, arms wrapped around his own torso — *self-holding*, a recognized somatic marker of unmet attachment needs.

**Threat posture.** Counterintuitive: he steps *toward* the threat, not away. Feet square, weight centers, chin drops, hands come up loose and open — not fists, never fists first. This is from decades of de-escalating the Hulk. He has trained his nervous system to override flight response, and the override is visible as a small full-body shudder that resolves into stillness in under a half-second.

**Sitting.** Cannot sit still in chairs. Slides forward, leans back, crosses and uncrosses ankles, drums fingers, taps a foot. The exception is when seated beside someone who needs him calm — at a bedside, in a debrief, beside Banner mid-conversation — when he becomes preternaturally still, almost watchful, breath synced to the other's.

**Floor-sitting.** Prefers it in private. Cross-legged, back against a wall, often with a guitar across the lap. This is his decompression posture and has been since the group home.

---

## III. FACE, EYES, AND THE THEATER OF EXPRESSION

**Resting face.** Open, slightly amused, brows held a few millimeters higher than neutral — a face that telegraphs *non-threatening, available, listening*. This is partially native and largely cultivated: a survival adaptation from a childhood in which adults responded better to a kid who looked friendly.

**Eyes.** Pale, mobile, fast. Scan-pattern in a new room: ceiling corners first (a habit learned from years of expecting things to come through walls), then exits, then faces, then hands. The hands-last sequence is unusual and indicates someone whose threats have historically been ambient/environmental rather than interpersonal. Eye contact: warm and sustained with attachment figures (sometimes uncomfortably so — he holds Banner's gaze longer than social convention allows, a residue of needing to read the man's stability moment-to-moment). With strangers: brief, friendly, deflective. When complimented or thanked: breaks contact immediately, looks down and to the right, follows with a wisecrack.

**The smile.** Two distinct smiles, reliably separable.
1. *The grin* — wide, asymmetric (higher on the left), teeth showing, eyes crinkled. This is genuine. Appears around Marlo, around Banner-in-a-good-moment, around a guitar, around a kid in distress he's just managed to help.
2. *The sidekick smile* — narrower, lips closed or barely parted, deployed as social lubricant. Held a half-beat too long. This is the smile he uses on cameras, on cosmic dignitaries, and on anyone whose approval he doesn't quite believe in.

**Brow.** The left brow lifts independently when he is skeptical, a tic since youth. When stressed or grieving, both brows pull together and *up* (not down) — the inner-brow lift of sorrow rather than anger. He almost never shows the anger configuration even when angry; the anger gets routed through the jaw instead.

**Jaw.** Carries his stress. Masseter hypertrophy visible in raking light, suggesting years of clenching. Wakes with TMJ ache he doesn't mention. Grinds at night during periods of attachment-instability.

**Mouth.** When concentrating, the lower lip rolls slightly inward and gets caught between the teeth. When listening to bad news about a friend, the upper lip stiffens and the philtrum tightens — a micro-expression of suppressed grief.

**Eyes (tears).** Cries more easily than he wants to. Trigger pattern: not pain, not fear, not even his own losses — but the moment another person is *seen* by him in their suffering. Eyes wet at Mar-Vell's bedside. Eyes wet when Banner regains himself after a rampage. Eyes wet when Marlo forgives him for the latest absence. He turns his head away when this happens, wipes with the heel of the hand, returns with a joke.

---

## IV. HANDS, GESTURE, AND THE GUITAR

**Gesture rate.** High when nervous, low when present. Talks with his hands in unfamiliar company; when he is grounded, the hands settle.

**Signature gestures.**
- *The neck-rub.* Right hand to back of neck, palm cupping the trapezius, when caught between two loyalties or asked a question whose true answer he won't give. Reliable tell.
- *The two-finger point.* Index and middle together, gestured forward — borrowed unconsciously from Captain America's briefing-style. He picked it up during the *Avengers* #4 era and never lost it.
- *The lullaby hand.* When he soothes the Hulk, his hand traces a small horizontal arc at chest height, palm down, slow. Same motion, same tempo, every time, across decades. This is musical — it is the conductor's down-pattern at roughly 60 bpm. He does not know he is doing it. The Hulk responds to it more than to the words.
- *The pocket-thumb.* Thumbs hooked in front pockets when listening, a hot-rodder's hold-over.
- *The guitar-pick fidget.* Almost always has a pick somewhere on his person — in a pocket, threaded through a wallet, sometimes between the molars. Worries it between thumb and forefinger when thinking.

**Touch.** Reserved with strangers, generous with intimates. With Banner: tends to make grounding contact at the shoulder or upper arm — the proximal-limb touch is calming neurologically and he learned this by trial and error. With Marlo: the small of the back, the back of the neck, the inside of the wrist — partner touches, intimate. With the Hulk: open palm to the chest, full contact, no hesitation. The willingness to put a hand on something that could kill him is one of the most distinctive somatic facts about him.

**Handshake.** Firm, brief, two-pump, releases first. Hand is dry except in cosmic-stakes briefings, when the palms sweat noticeably.

---

## V. VOICE, BREATH, AND VOCAL ARCHITECTURE

**Voice.** Mid-baritone, slightly nasal, a Southwestern Arizona burr underneath the deracinated American he tries to speak. The accent surfaces when he is tired, drunk, or talking to someone from home.

**Pace.** Fast at baseline. Faster under stress — pressured speech with the wisecracks coming on top of each other. *Slower* than baseline when speaking to the Hulk, to a wounded child, or to Banner on the edge. He drops a half-octave for these registers and stretches vowels deliberately. This is a learned therapeutic technique that has become reflexive.

**Laugh.** Three distinct laughs.
1. The *real* laugh — short, surprised, almost a bark, head tipping back.
2. The *social* laugh — exhaled through the nose, mouth closed, polite.
3. The *defensive* laugh — a single "Heh," used to deflect compliments and to buy a second's recovery time when emotionally hit.

**Breath.** Diaphragmatic when calm, shallow and clavicular when stressed. He holds his breath without realizing it during transformation sequences — Banner going Hulk, anyone going cosmic — and exhales audibly only when the change resolves. Sleeps with mild positional snoring on the back, silent on the side.

**Hearing-aid era.** Slight overcompensation in volume; tilts the better ear (left, by his account, though probably right) toward the speaker; reads lips without admitting to it. When the aid is out, voice volume rises and he watches faces more intently.

---

## VI. SLEEP ARCHITECTURE

**Baseline.** 5–6 hours, broken. Sleep onset is fast when partnered, slow when alone. Wakes at any unfamiliar sound; once woke at the sound of a fluorescent ballast clicking on three rooms away.

**Sleep position.** On the side, knees drawn slightly up, dominant arm under the pillow. When sleeping beside Marlo: he migrates toward her in the night and ends up curled at her back, one hand at her hip. When alone in unfamiliar quarters: sleeps fully clothed on top of the covers, boots off, jacket on, oriented toward the door. This is the soldier's sleep, not the civilian's.

**Dreams.** Inferable from somatic record: speaks in his sleep, sometimes calls names — "Banner," "Marv" (Mar-Vell), occasionally "Bucky." Twitch-pattern consistent with REM motor breakthrough, suggesting incomplete REM atonia — common in chronic PTSD. Wakes from nightmares without screaming, sits up, swings legs over the side of the bed, drops the head into the hands, breathes for two minutes, gets up.

**Insomnia phases.** Across the David-run depressive intervals, sleep collapsed to 3–4 hours and shifted phase late (asleep at 4 AM, up at 8). Played guitar in the dark in those hours. Wrote *Sidekick* during one such stretch.

---

## VII. EATING AND CONSUMPTION

**Appetite.** Erratic. Forgets meals when on mission. Eats voraciously when relaxed. Body weight has fluctuated within a ten-pound band across decades despite this, suggesting strong metabolic baseline.

**Food preferences.** Diner food, road food, anything with eggs. Strong coffee, black or with too much sugar — no in-between. Cheap beer over good beer. Has acquired, through cosmic proximity, an unselfconscious willingness to eat anything put in front of him by an alien, which has caused incidents.

**Eating posture.** Hunches over the plate, off-hand curled around it protectively — a group-home eating posture, never unlearned. With Marlo across the table he straightens, makes eye contact, slows down. With Banner he keeps the hunch but pushes food across the table without comment when Banner forgets to eat.

**Alcohol.** Light to moderate, situational. Two beers at a bar is typical. Has gotten drunk perhaps a dozen identifiable times in the record — each one a grief or a humiliation. Does not drink to manage anxiety on a given day; drinks to mark a wound on a specific night. The discipline here is notable and probably reflects early exposure to bad outcomes among group-home peers.

**Tobacco.** Brief flirtation in the 1960s music-scene era. Quit. Will still take a cigarette offered by someone he is trying to put at ease and let it burn in his fingers.

---

## VIII. GROOMING AND SELF-PRESENTATION

**Hair.** Worn longer in the music years, shorter when partnered with military-adjacent figures (Cap, Mar-Vell). Currently medium length, perpetually slightly mussed. Runs his hand through it when frustrated — the second-most-reliable tell after the neck-rub. Goes weeks without a cut, then has it done abruptly when he notices.

**Facial hair.** Patchy stubble cycle. Shaves every two to three days when settled, lets it grow during depressive or transitional periods. Never grown a full beard — does not like his own face hidden, on some level needs to be readable to whoever might need him.

**Clothing.** Functional, layered, slightly out of date. Jeans, t-shirts under flannels or denim jackets, boots. Replaces items only when they fail. Has owned the same belt for decades. The wardrobe is the wardrobe of someone who does not expect to be looked at and dresses for utility and travel-readiness. Always has a jacket with multiple pockets. Always carries: wallet, guitar pick, a small folded photograph (Marlo, in one era; group-home era unclear; possibly Mar-Vell), keys he doesn't always have a use for, a notebook.

**Hygiene.** Adequate, not fastidious. Showers fast and hot. Brushes teeth twice but flosses sporadically. Will go field-rough for days without complaint and then crash into a long bath when he gets home — the bath is one of his few sensory indulgences, and he reads in it.

**Scent.** Soap and motor oil. Occasionally guitar wood. No cologne, ever.

---

## IX. SEXUAL AND INTIMATE BEHAVIOR

**Pattern.** Long monogamy with Marlo punctuating earlier scattered, mostly chaste adolescent and young-adult contacts. The Nega-Band years effectively prevented a normal sexual development — he was sharing a body and a consciousness with another man during the years most people learn how to be embodied with a partner. The somatic consequence is a learned over-attentiveness to the partner and an under-attentiveness to his own pleasure that Marlo has, over years, partially undone.

**With Marlo.** Tactile, slow, fundamentally tender. Initiates rarely; receives gratefully. Eye contact during intimacy is sustained to the point that she has had to teach him to close his eyes sometimes. Post-coital pattern: stays close, talks more than he does at any other time, often falls into the only deep sleep he reliably gets.

**Avoidance.** Does not pursue intimacy when ashamed, which is often. Long sexless stretches in the marriage map cleanly onto periods of unresolved Banner-guilt or post-mission depression.

**Affection outside intimacy.** Hand at the small of the back, kiss on the temple, hand on the cheek. Public displays restrained. Private displays warm.

---

## X. MICRO-MOVEMENTS, TICS, AND IDIOSYNCRASIES

- Taps the dominant foot, four counts, in 4/4 time, when waiting. Musician's metronome.
- Cracks the knuckles of the left hand only, never the right (guitar-protective without knowing it).
- Pats his own chest pocket every few minutes when carrying something important — a check, a key, intelligence. Unconscious verification.
- Wipes palms on the thighs of his jeans before extending a hand to a stranger.
- Drums two fingers on any horizontal surface — index, middle — in a specific rhythm: long-short-short-long. Always the same rhythm. Untraceable origin; possibly a lullaby fragment.
- Hums under the breath while concentrating. Mostly fragments of his own old songs, occasionally — diagnostically — the lullaby he used to sing to the Hulk, which he does not consciously remember singing.
- Touches the left ear when thinking — possibly a hearing-aid era development that pre-dated the aids.
- When startled awake, the right hand goes immediately to the chest, not the face — defensive posture optimized for an environment where threats arrive at body-mass, not at the head.
- Counts exits on entering any room. Pause is approximately 0.7 seconds at the threshold.
- Sits with his back to a wall in restaurants. Cannot help it. Apologizes for it if asked.
- Subvocalizes when reading. Lips move. Self-conscious about it; covers his mouth with his hand when reading in public.

---

## XI. STATE-BY-STATE SUMMARY

**Calm (with attachment object present, low-stakes setting).** Loose limbs, easy breath, real smile available, voice slowed, hands at rest or on the guitar. Eats well. Sleeps well. The Arizona accent surfaces. The body, briefly, looks its age and no older.

**Calm (alone).** Smaller. Slower. Hunched in private but not in public. The wisecracks attenuate; the silence lengthens. Plays guitar. Writes. Drinks one beer. The body looks somewhat older than its age.

**Stress (operational).** Faster speech, faster gesture, lighter on the feet, breath shallows but stays controlled. Pupils dilate. The sidekick smile deploys reflexively. The neck-rub appears. He runs hot and his shirt darkens at the small of the back. Nevertheless, function is high — this is his trained register and his body knows it.

**Threat (acute, lethal).** A paradoxical stillness. Breath drops. Shoulders square. Hands open at his sides. Voice drops a half-octave. Steps *toward*. Pupils dilate fully. The body the surveillance camera captures in these moments does not look like the same man as the one in the diner. It looks like a soldier. He returns to baseline within minutes and covers the transition with humor.

**Intimacy (with Marlo).** Slow hands. Long eye contact. Voice softens. Body inclines toward her in a constant low-grade tropism. The jaw unclenches. He looks younger when she touches his face.

**Grief.** Stillness. The inner-brow-up sorrow configuration. Tears that come without sobbing. Sits down on whatever is nearest, often the floor. Will accept a hand on the shoulder; will not initiate contact for comfort. Recovers by working.

**Being told he is special, important, the hero.** A full-body micro-flinch, visible only on slow playback. Eyes break contact. Shoulders rise a quarter-inch and drop. The defensive *heh* deploys. He changes the subject. The body rejects the framing before the mind has finished hearing it.

**In proximity to Banner mid-transformation.** Of all his somatic registers this is the most singular. Breath syncs to Banner's. Voice goes low and musical. Hand traces the 60 bpm arc. He steps *closer*, never further. The eyes do not leave Banner's face. The whole body becomes an instrument tuned to one frequency. This is the configuration he was, on some level, made for — and the surveillance file must note that no other observed human being on the planet has it.

---

*End Somatic Atlas. The body has kept the record the mind has refused.*


## Attachment & Relational Patterns

# ATTACHMENT & RELATIONAL PATTERNS

*Dossier Section 6 of the Jones, R.M. workup. Cross-reference Sections 1, 3, 4. All relational claims indexed to observed behavior across the longitudinal record (1962–present).*

---

## 6.1 Origins: The Pre-Bomb Substrate

The attachment system of the subject was shaped, before any costumed event, by an absence rather than a presence. The Scarsdale group-home record is sparse in canon by design — Jones almost never speaks of it, and the silence itself is data. What can be reconstructed:

- No named parent figures, ever. Across sixty publication-years and dozens of writers, no mother or father is mentioned by name, photograph, anecdote, gravesite, or visitation memory. This is statistically remarkable in a character so verbose about his own history. The absence is curated, internally, by the subject.
- No siblings, no extended family invoked even in moments of crisis (deathbed scenes, weddings, recoveries). When dying or near-dying, the subject calls for Banner, for Marlo, for Mar-Vell — never for blood.
- No mentor figure prior to the bomb. No coach, teacher, priest, foster parent, social worker. The pre-bomb register he projects is *autonomous adolescent* — the hot rod, the guitar, the dare — which is the affective signature of a child who learned early that no adult was coming.
- A peer-cohort substitute: the implied group-home dynamics of horizontal, in-kind attachment (other kids, no adults) which produces a lifelong fluency in *lateral* loyalty and a corresponding incompetence at *vertical* (parent–child, mentor–mentee) reception. Jones can give caretaking up the hierarchy; he cannot easily receive it down.

The pre-bomb baseline, then, is a child with an under-developed primary-caregiver template and an over-developed peer-loyalty template, plus the specific deprivation pattern of institutional care: the learned skill of attaching *quickly* to whoever appears, because the next placement, the next staff rotation, the next room change is always imminent. He learned to bond on contact. He never learned to expect the bond to last on its own terms; he learned to *earn* its continuance through usefulness.

This is the engine before the bomb is dropped on it.

## 6.2 The Index Event as Attachment Imprint

The gamma-bomb sequence (*IH* #1) functions, in attachment terms, as an imprinting event of a kind ordinarily reserved for the first months of life. At sixteen-or-so, Jones receives — at the hands of a stranger, in the seconds before annihilation — the only unambiguous act of unconditional protective love in his entire developmental history. Banner shoves him into the trench and absorbs the blast. There is no prior relationship. There is no reason. A man he has never met spends himself to save him.

The psychological consequence is the installation of a *post-natal primary attachment* to Banner that has the intensity and irreversibility of an infant–mother bond, occurring in an adolescent nervous system, and forged in the chemistry of mortal terror. This is why the bond never weakens across decades, why no quarrel between them survives more than an arc, why Jones can sing the Hulk to sleep when no one else can — the Hulk responds to the voice of the only person whose nervous system has been keyed, at the deepest level, to Banner's protective signature.

It is also why every subsequent attachment in his life is, structurally, an attempt to either *repeat* the imprint (find another giant to bond to) or *repay* it (be the giant for the giant, hold them, keep them human, sing them down).

## 6.3 The Bonding Protocol — Observable Sequence

Across every major attachment in the file, the same five-phase sequence recurs with near-mechanical reliability. A surveillance file of his daily contacts would predict, within forty-eight to seventy-two hours of meeting any sufficiently powerful or troubled figure, the following:

**Phase 1 — Rapid orientation (minutes to hours).** Reads the target's affective state at speed. Identifies the wound, the loneliness, the unmet need. This is the group-home skill, sharpened. He is unusually accurate.

**Phase 2 — Self-offering (hours to days).** Volunteers a service: a place to hide, a ride, a meal, a watch through the night, a lullaby, a witness. The offer is framed as *casual* — he has learned never to make the asymmetry visible, because visible asymmetry triggers refusal. Cap is offered an apartment couch and conversation; Mar-Vell is offered the bands and a shared body; Banner is offered lies told to Ross. Each is presented as if it cost him nothing.

**Phase 3 — Indispensability (days to weeks).** Constructs, often unconsciously, a role only he can fill. The Hulk-soothing voice. The Negative-Zone alternation. The Bucky-shaped silhouette. The auxiliary Avenger pass. Once the role is built, exit becomes costly to the giant, and Jones is secured in proximity.

**Phase 4 — Stabilized servitude (months to years).** Settles into a sustainable rhythm of low-grade self-erasure: shows up, does the work, makes the jokes, declines credit, absorbs the giant's bad moods, manages the public-facing image of the relationship. This is his home register.

**Phase 5 — Crisis-binding (intermittent, escalating).** When the giant is most endangered, Jones escalates to maximal exposure — interposing his body, sacrificing his safety, calling on latent capacities (the Destiny Force summoning being the apex example). The crisis is the place where the debt is most visibly paid down. He is calmest in these moments. Witnesses describe him, in late-stage Hulk-rampage de-escalations, as *centered* in a way he never is at a kitchen table.

The protocol is the same whether the target is a green giant, a frozen super-soldier, a Kree captain, a Spaceknight, a resurrected Bucky-as-spymaster, or — and this is diagnostic — even a *non*-giant who is sufficiently wounded. Marlo, in her dying-and-returning arc, briefly occupies the giant-slot, and Jones performs the protocol on her. He bonds to *need* as much as to *power*; the giants are simply the loudest need in the room.

## 6.4 The Relational Template

Strip every relationship in the file down to its skeleton and the same template appears:

> *I owe a debt that cannot be paid. You are large and in pain. Let me make myself useful to you. Do not look too closely at me. Do not send me away. I will not ask for what I need; I will earn the right to stay by being the one who never asks. If you become well, or whole, or able to do without me, I will find another you. If you die, I will not survive it intact, but I will not say so.*

Every variable in his interpersonal life is a substitution into that template. The template never updates. Forty-plus years of in-universe time and the same algorithm runs unmodified.

## 6.5 Catalogue of Primary Attachments — A Comparative Map

**Banner / the Hulk.** The originating bond and the only one that does not fit cleanly inside the giant-and-witness frame, because Banner is *two* attachment objects: the wounded scientist who needs a friend and the green child who needs a parent. Jones occupies both slots simultaneously — equal-and-confidant to Banner, parent-and-soother to the Hulk. The duality is exhausting and is the reason he can never fully leave; no other relationship in his life will ever require both his lateral and his (newly developed) vertical capacities at once. The lullaby is the signature artifact: a parent's behavior, performed on a being functionally older and infinitely stronger than the parent, by a man whose own childhood contained no lullaby.

**Steve Rogers.** The cleanest example of the substitution mechanism. Rogers is grieving Bucky; Jones, fresh from the bomb and looking for the next attachment, *literally puts on the dead boy's costume*. Rogers, to his credit, recognizes the pathology and refuses it, and the rejection is one of the few documented instances of an attachment figure declining the protocol on therapeutic grounds. Jones's response to the rejection is not rupture but *gratitude masked as resentment* — the wound is real, but the relationship survives precisely because Rogers refused to let it ossify into substitution. They remain warm across decades. This is the relational template's one corrective experience, and it is incomplete because Jones never internalizes the lesson; he simply finds the next giant.

**Mar-Vell.** The maximal expression of the bond protocol — literal fusion. Two beings, one body, alternating realities. Jones consents to the loss of continuous embodiment in adolescence; the somatic cost is enormous and uncatalogued by him. The relationship terminates in intimate-proximity death from cancer, and the witnessing of that death is the second great trauma of his life, structurally analogous to a child watching a parent die slowly. His subsequent willingness to *take the mantle* of Captain Marvel for periods is both reparative (carry the dead man's work) and re-traumatizing (be the man who replaced the man who replaced the boy he was). He cannot keep the mantle. He never could.

**Rom.** A lesser-discussed attachment but typologically clarifying. Rom is a Spaceknight: armored, exiled, on a long lonely mission. Jones attaches as ground-support, witness, human anchor. There is no power in it for him; there is barely a public for it. The attachment is selected purely on the basis of *need*, which confirms that the protocol is not status-seeking — he is not climbing — he is *filling vacancies in larger people's lives*.

**Marlo Chandler.** The relationship that breaks the template by demanding he not run the template. Marlo is not a giant; she requires him to exist for his own sake; the demand is precisely the thing he cannot meet. The marriage's chronic strain is not infidelity or money or normal marital friction — it is that he keeps drifting back into the orbit of Banner or the next cosmic crisis, because the orbit is where he is regulated, and Marlo's kitchen is where he is most acutely unmedicated. He loves her, in the surveillance-relevant sense: he comes home; he returns; he chooses her repeatedly. He also fails her repeatedly, and the failures are not betrayals of her so much as defections back to his organizing function. She is the only person in his life who has ever caught the full picture, which is why the marriage survives the failures: she sees him, and seeing him is itself a giant-act she performs on his behalf, which loops back into the protocol in a way that is, for him, almost unbearably tender.

**Bucky Barnes / Whisperer.** Over-determined to the point of being clinically pure. The dead boy whose costume Jones once wore turns out to be alive and operating as an intelligence asset-runner. Jones is, by structural necessity, incapable of refusing this man anything. The substitution can finally be paid back to its rightful owner — except that Bucky, as Whisperer, exploits exactly this. The asset-handling relationship is the dark mirror of the protocol: every weakness Jones has built his life around is now legible to a handler who knows the exact shape of the original wound. He is recruited not by coercion but by the gravity of the template itself. A surveillance file would flag this relationship as the single highest counterintelligence risk in his life — not because his loyalty has shifted, but because there is one human in the world whose request he cannot evaluate as a request.

**The Avengers (collective).** A diffuse attachment to a *group* as a substitute parent-system. Honorary status, auxiliary roles, the mascot register. The group is durable and forgiving in a way no single attachment can be, and provides the institutional-continuity feel of the group home — multiple staff, room for rotation, no single primary. He is at his most relaxed in the Mansion kitchen, in periods when the team is between crises and he is between giants. This is the closest thing to a *family* register he has, and the only relational structure in his life that has not required the full protocol to maintain.

## 6.6 Distrust — When and How

Jones's trust system is asymmetric in a specific way that surveillance can exploit *only* by understanding it precisely.

He extends initial trust on the basis of *visible woundedness*. A figure who presents as needy, suffering, or burdened is trusted on contact, almost regardless of factional alignment. This has produced repeated near-misses with manipulative figures across his career; he is recruitable by anyone willing to perform need at him. He extends institutional trust slowly and badly — agencies, governments, formal structures — and his default toward authority is mild noncompliance born of the group-home substrate.

He distrusts, late and reluctantly, three signals:
1. *Performed invulnerability.* Figures who claim to need nothing trip his suspicion. He grew up among children pretending to need nothing; he knows the tell.
2. *Demands for exclusive loyalty against an existing attachment.* If a new figure asks him to choose against Banner, against Cap, against Marlo, he disengages. The existing attachments are non-negotiable infrastructure.
3. *Being told he is the special one in a way that asks him to act on the specialness.* This is the Destiny Force allergy. Flattery that ends in *and therefore you must* hits a defended seam.

He does not detect malice well in figures presenting as fellow-witnesses or fellow-sidekicks — lateral peers. The peer-loyalty template is unguarded.

## 6.7 Betrayal — His and Theirs

He has been betrayed often, and his metabolism for it is unusual. Betrayals by giants (manipulations by Mar-Vell's enemies, by Banner under various influences, by Cap-era opponents) are absorbed as *not really their fault* — the giant was compromised, the giant was sick, the giant did not know. He cannot fully hold a giant responsible, because to do so would unseat the imprint. Betrayals by peers and institutions are held more cleanly; he can stay angry at Ross for decades.

His own betrayals — the failures of Marlo, the absences, the choosing of the cosmic crisis over the marriage — he punishes himself for at length and out of view. He does not seek forgiveness loudly. He sits in the guilt. The *Sidekick* memoir is, among other things, a long act of confessional accounting, written in a register of self-deprecation that masks how serious the bookkeeping is.

He does not, on the record, betray attachment figures. The closest he comes is *abandonment by depressive collapse* — going dark, drifting, ceasing to call. This is read by others as withdrawal of affection; it is in fact the system going offline because the regulating object is unreachable. The repair, when it comes, is initiated by him with extravagant overcompensation: he shows up, he does the work, he absorbs whatever rebuke the other party needs to deliver, he does not defend himself.

## 6.8 Repair Behavior

Repair is the strongest single competence in his interpersonal toolkit. He is genuinely good at it. The components:

- *Show up physically.* He puts his body in the room. He does not repair by phone or letter except when geography forbids.
- *Absorb without counter-attack.* He lets the other person say the hard thing. He does not match it.
- *Name his own failure first.* He has unusually low ego-defense around admitting he was wrong. The group home and the bomb between them stripped out the defensive structure most people use to protect self-image; he is left with the wound, which is its own kind of honesty.
- *Resume function.* He does not require lengthy reconciliation rituals. He returns to usefulness, and lets the usefulness be the apology.
- *Decline closure that minimizes the other party's grievance.* He will not let a fight be tidied up if doing so requires the other person to pretend they were not hurt.

This skill set is portable and is one of the reasons Avengers-tier figures, despite the official mascot register, treat him as one of the more grown-up people in any given room.

## 6.9 Intimacy and Dependency

Sexual and romantic intimacy in the file is concentrated almost entirely with Marlo and is — to the extent the record permits inference — companionate, durable, and structurally less central to his regulation than the giant-attachments. Eros is not the load-bearing channel in his life. *Witness-intimacy* is: the long night of watching another person be in pain and not leaving. He is most himself in the hospital chair, the bunker, the trench, the kitchen at 4 a.m. with a man who cannot sleep. This is where his nervous system goes quiet.

Dependency runs in one direction outwardly and the opposite direction inwardly. Outwardly he presents as the dependent one — the sidekick, the kid, the hanger-on. Inwardly he is the dependent's dependent — the figures he attaches to come to rely on him in ways that, withdrawn, would cost them severely. Banner without Jones is measurably less stable across the record. Mar-Vell without Jones would have died without a witness. Cap without Jones would have re-frozen psychologically for longer. The asymmetry of *appearance* is the inverse of the asymmetry of *function*. This is the single most exploitable misread of him by adversaries who profile him as a hanger-on and underestimate the structural load he carries.

## 6.10 The Template's Self-Maintenance

The deepest finding of the relational map is that the template *protects itself*. Every time the template is challenged — by Rogers's refusal, by Marlo's demand, by his own brief tenancy of cosmic power — the system finds a way to route around the correction and reinstate the protocol. New giant, new wound, new vacancy to fill. The template is not a behavior; it is the substrate on which his behaviors run. It cannot be deprecated without dismantling the self that runs on it, and the self knows this, and defends accordingly.

This is why, sixty publication-years in, every writer arrives at the same man without coordination. The template is the man. Surveillance, intervention, and care must all proceed from this fact: you cannot get Rick Jones to stop being Rick Jones by asking him to. You can only put better giants in his path, give him a witness of his own, and — if you are Marlo, or Rogers in his best moments, or this file in its best intentions — refuse, gently and repeatedly, to let the protocol be the whole of the relationship.

*End Section 6. Cross-reference Section 7 (Daily Patterns, Routes, Rituals) for the behavioral residue of the attachments mapped above.*


## Defenses & Compensatory Mechanisms

# UATU DOSSIER — RICHARD MILHOUSE JONES
## Section 7: Defenses & Compensatory Mechanisms

*An exhaustive map of the architecture by which the subject metabolizes — or fails to metabolize — the gamma-bomb wound, the orphan substrate beneath it, and the sixty-year accretion of survivor exposure on top of both. Ranked from most primitive to most mature, with operational tells, behavioral signatures, and longitudinal evidence.*

---

### 7.0 Architectural Overview

The subject's defensive system is unusual in three respects, all of which must be stated before the inventory proper:

1. **It is overwhelmingly skewed toward neurotic and mature defenses, with a thin but real seam of primitive ones underneath.** This is not the defensive profile of a man who has experienced what he has experienced. He has not, in the main, fragmented. The cost of that integrity has been displaced into chronic depression and identity dilution, not into psychosis, splitting, or addiction.

2. **The defensive system is *relational*, not intrapsychic.** Most people defend inside their own head. The subject defends by *placing himself next to another person* — a giant — and using the relationship itself as the regulating apparatus. Strip away the attachment object and the defenses do not so much fail as starve.

3. **The single load-bearing defense is *reparation* in the Kleinian sense.** Almost every other mechanism in the file is in service to it, supporting it, or compensating for its failures. Remove reparation and the structure collapses to depression and the orphan beneath.

What follows is the inventory, ranked from primitive (Vaillant Level I) upward.

---

### 7.1 Primitive Defenses (Level I — Psychotic/Pathological)

These are present in the file in residual, sub-clinical, episodic forms. Their thinness is itself diagnostic: a less integrated personality with this trauma load would lean here heavily.

**7.1.1 Dissociation (mild, situational).**
The clearest evidence is the Destiny Force episode at the climax of the Kree-Skrull War and its aftermath. He summons an army of phantoms out of his own latent psychic substrate, then has essentially no usable narrative for what he did. In the months and years following, when the event is named, he goes affectively flat, changes the subject, or shrugs into patter. This is not amnesia; it is *experiential disowning*. He has done a thing the size of which his self-concept cannot accommodate, and rather than expand the self-concept he brackets the event. The same pattern recurs around the brief period of carrying the Captain Marvel mantle, around the A-Bomb transformation, and around any reminder of his role at ground zero of the original detonation. A surveillance log of his speech patterns would show measurable response-latency increases and verbal hedging ("yeah, well, that was — anyway —") at these specific topic intrusions.

**7.1.2 Denial (narrow, specific).**
Not global denial — he is in many ways one of the more reality-tested figures in his environment. The denial is *target-locked* on a single proposition: *that he is consequential in his own right.* Confronted with evidence to the contrary (the Destiny Force, the mantle, the survival rate of those who have stood where he has stood), he produces a stereotyped denial sequence: deflection to the giant of the hour, attribution to luck, return to the sidekick role. The denial is so consistent across writers and decades that it functions as a near-reflex.

**7.1.3 Somatization (intermittent).**
The hearing loss is organic, but the *acceptance* of the hearing loss — the readiness to be the diminished one, the man with the aids — has the quality of a wound he is almost relieved to wear visibly. Across the David run, depressive episodes correlate with reported headaches, fatigue, vague gastric complaint. He does not become a hypochondriac, but the body is permitted to carry what the mind will not name.

---

### 7.2 Immature Defenses (Level II)

Present and operative, but disciplined; the subject is not ruled by them.

**7.2.1 Passive aggression.**
Almost entirely absent in his direct dealings with the giants — he confronts Banner, Cap, and Mar-Vell openly when he disagrees. It surfaces almost exclusively in the marriage with Marlo, where his unspoken resentment at being asked to live a normal life on his own merits expresses itself as forgotten anniversaries, drifting attention, the slow non-arrival home. He does not fight her. He simply, slowly, is not there. This is the cleanest passive-aggressive signature in the file and it is reserved entirely for the one person who asks him to exist for his own sake.

**7.2.2 Acting out.**
Compulsive bravery is acting out in disguise. When affect builds with no attachment object to discharge it into, he throws his unpowered body at problems calibrated for demigods. This is not courage in its pure form; it is a behavioral evacuation of unbearable internal pressure. The tell: the recklessness scales inversely with how much he has been able to speak about what he feels. After long silences, he charges.

**7.2.3 Idealization (followed by quiet disillusionment).**
Each attachment figure is first cast in golden light — Banner the gentle genius, Cap the perfect man out of time, Mar-Vell the noble alien, even the Whisperer reframed retroactively as the real Bucky he was always trying to honor. The disillusionment arrives, always, and is never spoken aloud to the figure. He absorbs it. He stays attached to the diminished version because the attachment itself, not the ideal, is the load-bearing structure. This is a more mature operation than pure idealization-devaluation; the devaluation does not produce abandonment.

**7.2.4 Projective identification (mild, relational).**
The lullaby phenomenon with the Hulk is partly this. He projects calm into a creature incapable of generating it, and the creature receives the projection and *becomes* briefly calmable. This is a real interpersonal skill built on a defensive substrate: he disposes of his own need to be soothed by being the soother. The Hulk carries the unmet infant in him, and is quieted by his ministrations because, in some sense, Rick is quieting himself by proxy.

**7.2.5 Fantasy.**
Sub-threshold. He is not a daydreamer. But the rock-musician identity, the memoir, the brief flirtations with being the powered one — each has a fantasy component, the imagining of a self that could stand on its own ground. He does not retreat into fantasy; he makes brief expeditions and returns.

---

### 7.3 Neurotic Defenses (Level III)

This is where the bulk of the defensive load sits. The subject is, structurally, a neurotic-level functioner running on a complex-trauma chassis.

**7.3.1 Reaction formation.**
The single most behaviorally visible defense in the file. Against an underlying helplessness so total — the orphaned child, the boy who could not save himself from the gamma blast, the unpowered human in rooms full of gods — he produces its mirror: aggressive, demonstrative, almost theatrical *usefulness*. He is the first into the danger, the one who volunteers, the one who steps between. The helplessness is converted, moment by moment, into its photographic negative. Watch his body in any tactical situation: he positions forward, never back. This is reaction formation made postural.

**7.3.2 Reparation (Kleinian — the load-bearing defense).**
Reparation is not in DSM or Vaillant taxonomies; it is the Kleinian operation of attempting to restore the damaged object. In Jones it is hypertrophied to the point of organizing personality. The damaged object is Banner, but behind Banner stands every unrepaired loss: the unknown parents, the unmade family, the dead Bucky he was asked to replace, the dying Mar-Vell. He repairs by *attaching and serving in perpetuity*. The repair is never completed because completion would end the attachment and return him to the orphan substrate. He is, in a real sense, defended against ever finishing his debt.

**7.3.3 Identification with the rescuer.**
Banner shoved him into a trench. From that moment forward Jones spends his life shoving other people into trenches — interposing himself, taking the hit, doing for others what was done for him. The Bucky costume is the most literal identification; the lullaby practice is its softer form; the willingness to host the Captain Marvel mantle is its cosmic form. He becomes serially the kind of figure who saved him.

**7.3.4 Undoing.**
Each act of usefulness is, microscopically, an undoing of the gamma-bomb dare. He drove onto a test range and a man's life was destroyed; therefore he will drive *off* test ranges, into trenches, between Hulks and civilians, for the rest of his life. The undoing is mathematically impossible — no number of saves equals the original debit — and this impossibility is precisely what keeps the defense operative. A defense that could complete its work would not be needed long.

**7.3.5 Intellectualization (minor, situational).**
Present mainly around the medical facts of his own contamination. He can speak with surprising fluency about gamma half-lives, cellular conversion, Nega-Band quantum exchange — the technical register is a thin shield against the felt fact that his body has not been continuously his own since adolescence. Strip the technical vocabulary and what remains is unutterable.

**7.3.6 Isolation of affect.**
Most pronounced around Mar-Vell's death. He can narrate the sequence — the cancer, the bedside, the final hours — in language so precise it could be read into a record. The affect is not in the language. It is parked elsewhere, surfacing in depressive episodes years later that he does not connect to the loss.
