The same isolation operates around the deaths of associates and around his own clinical death.

**7.3.7 Displacement.**
The aggression that should be directed at General Ross (who weaponized him as bait more than once), at the institutions that orphaned him, at the giants who absorbed his life into theirs, is displaced laterally — into the cosmic enemy of the week, into his own body via reckless action, occasionally into Marlo via the passive-aggressive channel. He almost never expresses anger upward at the figures who have used him.

**7.3.8 Repression.**
The orphan history. The pre-Banner years. The specific affect of being a child without parents in an institutional setting in mid-century Arizona. He almost never speaks of it. When pressed he produces a few stock phrases. The repression is unusually clean and unusually thorough; it is the foundation on which the rest of the defensive house is built.

**7.3.9 Rationalization.**
"Banner needs me." "Cap needs someone he can trust." "Mar-Vell can't operate here without me." "Marlo understands." Each rationalization is partially true, which is what makes it operative. The lie is in the implied subordinate clause: *and therefore I do not have to ask what I need.*

**7.3.10 Self-deprecation as preemption.**
The wisecracking sidekick patter is a structured neurotic defense, not a personality trait. He performs his own diminishment before anyone in the room can perform it for him. This achieves three things: it forecloses humiliation by metabolizing it in advance; it cues the giants to relax their guard around him; and it secures his role by visibly accepting its limits. Surveillance of his speech across decades shows the patter intensifying in rooms where he feels evaluatively unsafe (early Avengers meetings, encounters with Tony Stark, anything involving a press presence) and relaxing markedly in rooms with Banner alone, Marlo, or other non-powered humans.

---

### 7.4 Mature Defenses (Level IV)

These are real and load-bearing; they are the reason the subject has not decompensated.

**7.4.1 Sublimation.**
The music and the *Sidekick* memoir are the major channels. The guitar predates the gamma bomb and is the one piece of identity that is genuinely his own; he returns to it in every depressive trough and every period of unattachment. The memoir is sublimation of an unusually high order — he converts the unintegrable experience of having stood next to gods into narrative form, makes it legible, sells it, and in the act of authorship recovers a measure of authorship over his own life. That the memoir is also exploited, mocked, and turned against him by enemies does not negate the maturity of the operation.

**7.4.2 Altruism.**
Distinguished from reparation by being genuinely directed at the recipient's good rather than at the discharging of internal debt. The lullaby for the Hulk, on close inspection, is both — but the *care for Marlo during her own illnesses and crises*, the steady decency to civilians at incident scenes, the willingness to talk a panicked bystander through a Hulk-tier event, are altruism proper. He is good to people who cannot pay him back, including himself rarely.

**7.4.3 Humor.**
Distinct from the self-deprecating patter. Real humor — the dry, observational, situationally apt joke — is a mature defense in Vaillant's schema and Jones runs it well. It de-escalates rooms full of demigods. It humanizes encounters that would otherwise tip into the operatic. It is one of the genuine skills he brings to teams that include cosmic-tier intellects, and it is recognized as such by the figures most worth recognizing it (Banner, eventually Cap, eventually even Stark).

**7.4.4 Suppression.**
He has a real capacity to put a thing down and pick it up later. The technical name for this is suppression and it is the most mature of all the defenses. He can table his feelings about the Destiny Force, about Mar-Vell, about his own irradiation, in order to function in a present-tense crisis, and return to them in private later. The "return to them later" sometimes does not happen, which is where suppression slides into repression — but the conscious capacity is there.

**7.4.5 Anticipation.**
Years of proximity to Banner have produced a finely calibrated capacity to anticipate the transformation, the threat, the social fallout. He scans rooms for exits, for civilians, for the heart-rate change in his attachment figure. This is mature defense converted into operational tradecraft.

---

### 7.5 Positive Compensatory Structures (What He Built To Live)

Distinct from defenses; these are the *constructed* features of the personality that compensate for the deficits and have become real strengths in their own right.

- **The lullaby skill.** A genuine, learned, transferable capacity to lower the arousal of a dysregulated other. Not a gimmick; not magic. Built by thousands of repetitions with the most difficult subject imaginable. He could do the same work in a trauma ward or a hostage scene.
- **Moral steadiness under cosmic pressure.** Has not bent on essentials when figures of vastly greater power have. The Kree-Skrull War climax is the dramatic instance; the quieter instances — refusing to lie for Ross, refusing to abandon Banner when it would have been wise to, refusing to take the easy mantle when offered — are the structural ones.
- **Tactical literacy.** Sixty years of after-action data has produced a real operator. Reads rooms, reads battlefields, reads the precursor signs of Hulk-out and of Mar-Vell-class energy events. Underrated by himself and by everyone around him.
- **De-escalation as a craft.** The verbal and postural skills are real. He can talk to a Hulk. He has talked to worse.
- **Loyalty as a load-bearing virtue.** Not a defense; a chosen value, sustained against incentive, across decades. Few in his world can match it.
- **Witness function.** He is one of the few people who has been present at the actual events and can narrate them truthfully. The *Sidekick* memoir, whatever its commercial fate, is a real act of historical preservation.

---

### 7.6 Negative Compensatory Structures (What He Built That Costs Him)

- **The sidekick identity as career.** Functional, but self-foreclosing. Every year he occupies the role is a year he does not build the independent life Marlo asks of him.
- **Serial attachment to giants.** Solves the affect-regulation problem; creates the identity-diffusion problem.
- **Indispensability seeking.** He arranges his presence to be necessary. When it is necessary he is stable; when it is not he disintegrates. The arrangement guarantees future destabilizations.
- **Compulsive bravery.** Has kept him useful; has nearly killed him repeatedly; has caused the cumulative orthopedic and neurological toll a polytrauma survivor carries.
- **Self-deprecation as habit.** Started as defense; has become reflex; now operates even in rooms where it costs him standing he could use.
- **Refusal of his own power.** The Destiny Force, the mantle, the A-Bomb form — each was an opportunity to integrate a larger self-concept. Each was, in effect, declined. The declination is itself a compensation: it preserves the sidekick identity at the cost of the larger life.
- **Marriage as a site of failure.** Marlo is the relationship that asks him to use the mature defenses without the giant-attachment scaffolding, and the mature defenses, real as they are, are not yet load-bearing enough alone. The marriage is therefore the consistent site of his collapses.

---

### 7.7 The Defensive System Under Specific Stressors

- **Acute crisis with attachment figure present.** Full integration. Mature defenses lead; humor, anticipation, altruism, suppression all online. He is at his best.
- **Acute crisis without attachment figure.** Reaction formation and acting out lead; reckless interposition. He survives by luck more than design.
- **Chronic unattachment.** Defenses starve. Suppression slides to repression; sublimation (music, writing) partially compensates; depressive collapse follows. The David-era dysthymic stretches are the textbook picture.
- **Being named as significant in his own right.** Dissociation, denial, isolation of affect, deflection to patter. The full primitive seam comes online briefly. He cannot metabolize his own size.
- **Being weaponized via the original debt ("Banner because of you").** Defenses *do not engage* — the proposition is already endorsed by the ego. This is the file's central vulnerability and any hostile actor with the dossier would know to use it.
- **Being asked to refuse the real Bucky anything.** Defenses do not engage. The substitution wound is open tissue; the identification with the rescuer collapses into compliance.
- **Being loved for himself.** Defenses engage *against* the love. Passive aggression, drift, depressive withdrawal. The most pathogenic stressor in the file is the offer of a life of his own.

---

### 7.8 Summary Architecture

A neurotic-level defensive profile, structurally sound, with a thin primitive seam, an unusually heavy reliance on *reparation* and *identification with the rescuer*, a robust mature top-layer (humor, sublimation, altruism, suppression, anticipation), and a relational rather than intrapsychic operating principle. The whole system runs on the presence of an attachment object large enough to absorb the debt by needing him. With one present, he is one of the more functional figures in his cohort. Without one, he degrades along a slow depressive vector that the mature defenses can slow but not reverse.

The defensive system has kept him alive and largely intact through a trauma load that would have produced psychosis, addiction, or sociopathy in a less integrated personality. The cost has been the foreclosure of the life that would have been his own.

*End Section 7. Section 8 (Habits, Rituals, Routes, Tells) follows.*


## Longitudinal Psychological Profile

# UATU DOSSIER — SECTION 7
## Longitudinal Psychological Profile: Richard Milhouse Jones
### Decade-by-Decade Clinical Picture (Affect Regulation, Cognitive Style, Self-Concept, and Their Evolution)

*Frameworks employed: attachment theory (Bowlby/Ainsworth/Main), object relations (Klein, Winnicott, Fairbairn), self psychology (Kohut), trauma response models (van der Kolk, Herman C-PTSD), Linehan biosocial model for affect regulation, Eriksonian life-stage staging, Loevinger ego development, McAdams narrative identity. All inferences sourced to behavior in the published canon.*

---

## 7.0 ORIENTING NOTES

A longitudinal read of the Subject's life is unusually clean because the index trauma is so precisely datable (the gamma detonation, age ~16) and the attachment substitutions so cleanly serialized (Banner → Captain America → Mar-Vell → Rom → Banner again → Marlo → A-Bomb-self → Whisperer/Barnes). What follows treats each developmental decade as a clinical chart-period: presenting affect, dominant defenses, cognitive register, organizing self-state, and the shift that closes the period and seeds the next.

Two structural facts must be held in mind throughout. First, **the Subject's developmental clock is non-standard**: the gamma event functioned as a foreclosure of late adolescence, collapsing identity-formation (Erikson Stage 5) into a single, externally-imposed answer — "I am the one who owes Banner" — before any normal exploration could occur. Every subsequent stage is therefore worked *through* a foreclosed identity rather than out of an integrated one. Second, **his affect-regulation system is exogenous from the start**: he was never given the internalized soothing object that allows for autonomous regulation, and he found a substitute (the attachment-figure-as-mission) before he could discover the lack. The whole life is a series of attempts to keep that substitute online.

---

## 7.1 ADOLESCENCE (ages ~14–17): Pre-Trauma Baseline and Index Event

### Presenting picture

Institutional orphan, group-home raised, Scarsdale Arizona; no recorded primary caregiver, no siblings; identifies via hot-rods, guitar, peer-group bravado. The brief pre-bomb glimpse establishes a *counterphobic adolescent* — the dare to drive onto a live test range is not curiosity, it is the standard adaptation of a parentless boy who manages a chronic sense of expendability by repeatedly proving he is not afraid of his own death. This is significant: the Subject's *baseline*, before any cosmic event, was already a fragile, externalizing, risk-courting boy with no continuous attachment object.

### Affect regulation

Wholly external and behavioral: speed, music, group dares. No internal capacity to sit with affect; no model for having done so. Affect is *discharged* (through engine noise, guitar, performance) rather than processed.

### Cognitive style

Concrete-operational, present-oriented, morally clear in a folk-American register. No evidence of reflective function in the Fonagy sense — he does not yet conceive of his own mind as an object of inquiry.

### Self-concept

Diffuse, peer-mirrored, with an undercurrent of expendability ("nobody would miss me"). The dare onto the test range is, read clinically, a near-suicidal gesture in counterphobic dress.

### Closing event

The gamma bomb. Banner's body interposed between his body and annihilation. This single act installs the organizing schema of the entire remaining life — *another man's existence was destroyed in exchange for mine* — and the foreclosure of identity development around it.

---

## 7.2 LATE ADOLESCENCE / EARLY 20s: The Reparative Phase

### Presenting picture

The Subject attaches to Banner with the intensity of a child who has just discovered his mother is alive after being told she was dead. He hides Banner, manages the Hulk, lies to Ross, sings the creature to sleep. The behavior is around-the-clock; there is no other life.

### Affect regulation — Phase I externalization

For the first time, the Subject has a *regulator outside himself who needs regulating*. This is the discovery that organizes everything that follows: he stabilizes his own affect by stabilizing another's. The Hulk-lullaby is the prototype — a literal externalization of the Winnicottian holding function, with the roles inverted (the child holds the giant). This is **caretaking inversion** as a primary affect-regulation strategy, and from this point forward it is the Subject's only reliable one.

### Cognitive style

Sharpens noticeably. Pattern-recognition for Banner's prodromal cues (gait, breath, pupil, jaw) becomes acute. He develops what is, in effect, a clinician's eye for a single patient — micro-attunement to one person's autonomic shifts, with no generalization to other domains. This is the cognitive signature he will retain for life: *exquisite specific attunement, poor system-level abstraction*.

### Defenses (in Klein/Vaillant terms)

- **Reparation** (primary, mature): undoing the harm of the index event by indefinite installments.
- **Identification with the rescuer**: he becomes Banner's protector as Banner was his.
- **Reaction formation against helplessness**: charges into Hulk-adjacent danger.
- **Humor (immature-to-neurotic register)**: the wisecracking sidekick patter begins here as preemptive self-diminishment.

### Self-concept

A new, stable, but *borrowed* identity: "Banner's keeper." This is functional pseudo-coherence — Loevinger's *Conformist* stage hardened by trauma into a single role. The role works because it is doing genuine moral work; the danger is that the Subject cannot distinguish the role from the self.

### Shift

Cap defrosts. Banner becomes intermittently unavailable. The Subject discovers that the regulation strategy is *transferable*.

---

## 7.3 EARLY-TO-MID 20s: Serial Attachment and the Bucky Wound

### Presenting picture

Attaches to Captain America in the Bucky-substitution role, explicitly dons the costume, is gently but firmly told by Cap that the substitution is unhealthy and refused the mantle. Recoils, attaches to Mar-Vell, ends up Nega-Band-fused — a literal bodily merger that constitutes the most extreme expression of the caretaking-inversion strategy possible: *not having a separate body from the attachment figure*.

### Affect regulation — Phase II symbiotic

With Mar-Vell, the external-regulator strategy is taken to its logical and somatic limit. There is no longer a boundary between regulator and regulated; they alternate corporeality. This should be understood as **regulation by fusion** — the dissolution of self-other boundary in order to guarantee that the attachment object cannot be lost. It is, in object-relations terms, a re-entry into the symbiotic phase (Mahler) that the Subject never properly resolved because there was no caregiver with whom to resolve it the first time.

The clinical consequence is severe and largely unmetabolized: for years of his early adulthood, the Subject *did not have a continuous body*. The standard developmental task of young adulthood — consolidating an embodied self capable of intimacy (Erikson Stage 6) — was performed in conditions that made embodied continuity impossible. He emerges from this period with a permanent uncertainty about whether his body is his.

### Cognitive style

Bifurcates. The Mar-Vell fusion exposes him to cosmic-scale information he is not equipped to process, and he develops a defensive *concreteness* — refusing the abstraction, gripping the human-scale frame ("I'm just a kid from Arizona"). This anti-intellectual self-presentation is established here as a stable defense against the vertigo of the cosmic.

### The Bucky wound

Cap's gentle refusal of the substitution is, paradoxically, more wounding than acceptance would have been. It tells the Subject that he is not even adequate as a replacement for a dead boy. This wound is **silently archived** and reactivates with full force decades later when Bucky returns as the Whisperer; the Subject's documented incapacity to refuse the real Bucky anything is the unresolved residue from this period.

### Self-concept

Fragmented and outsourced. He is alternately "Cap's not-Bucky," "Mar-Vell's other half," and, in the gaps, no one. Identity is now distributed across attachment objects rather than carried internally.

### Shift — the Destiny Force episode

The Kree-Skrull War climax, *Avengers* #97: the Subject mentally summons the Golden Age heroes from limbo, demonstrating latent psychic capacity of historic magnitude. He collapses. The episode is then largely ignored by his own self-narrative — **he cannot metabolize his own significance**. This is the first clear evidence of what becomes a lifelong dissociative response to evidence of his own power.

---

## 7.4 LATE 20s — THE DEATH OF MAR-VELL: The First Decompensation

### Presenting picture

Mar-Vell dies of cancer. The Subject witnesses this at intimate proximity, having been bodily fused with him for years. The loss is unlike any normal bereavement because the lost object was, for a long period, *part of his own corporeality*. The bereavement is therefore a partial somatic amputation as well as a relational catastrophe.

### Affect regulation — collapse

The external regulator is gone, and no replacement is immediately available. The Subject's regulation system fails. Behaviorally: aimless drift, low-level alcohol use (the only period in the record where substance use is implied), depressive flattening, return to music as discharge activity (a regression to the pre-trauma adolescent strategy). This is a **first major depressive episode**, prolonged, with prominent features of complicated grief and survivor guilt redoubled: *another, better man died; I lived again.*

### Cognitive style

Slowed, ruminative, present-focused but in a depressive rather than vital register. Reflective function begins to emerge here, painfully — for the first time he is forced to examine his own pattern because the pattern has just killed someone he loved.

### Self-concept

Bottoms out. The borrowed identities are revealed as borrowed. Without an attachment object, the Subject discovers he does not know who he is. This is the first genuine **identity crisis** in the Eriksonian sense, occurring roughly a decade late, and it is what makes the subsequent David-era work possible.

### Shift

Slowly, partially, returns to Banner's orbit. But something has changed: he no longer believes the attachment will permanently solve him.

---

## 7.5 30s — THE PETER DAVID YEARS: Partial Maturation

This is the decisive clinical decade. The Subject does more genuine psychological work here than in any other period.

### Presenting picture

Ages visibly. Marries Marlo Chandler — the first relationship structured around equality rather than service to a giant. Briefly carries the Captain Marvel mantle himself. Writes *Sidekick*, a tell-all memoir. Cycles in and out of Banner's orbit. Experiences marital strain, separation, reconciliation. Cycles through depressive episodes between missions.

### Affect regulation — Phase III, attempted internalization

For the first time, the Subject *tries* to develop endogenous regulation. The memoir-writing is the central activity here, and it should be read clinically as **narrative-identity construction in the McAdams sense** — the attempt to author a coherent life-story that integrates the trauma rather than re-enacting it. He does not fully succeed. The memoir is partly defensive (it is also a way to monetize and externalize the wound), and the marriage is partly used as a new regulator. But he is, for the first time, *aware* of the pattern, and the awareness itself is new.

The cycle is now visible to him: attached → stable → un-attached → depressive collapse → re-attach. He names it, fights it, fails to break it, but no longer denies it. This is movement from Loevinger's *Conformist* through *Self-Aware* toward (but not into) *Conscientious*.

### Cognitive style

Sharpens and matures. Reflective function comes online in earnest. He develops the capacity to hold his own mental states as objects of inquiry — visible in the *Sidekick* project, in his arguments with Banner, in his negotiations with Marlo. The anti-intellectual self-presentation persists as defense, but the internal cognition has matured beneath it. He becomes capable of irony about himself in a non-defensive register, which is a developmental marker.

### Self-concept

Bifurcates more visibly than before. Surface: husband, memoirist, ex-sidekick trying to be a man. Latent: still the boy who owes Banner, still the cosmic-adjacent figure who summoned the Golden Age. The two selves now coexist in conscious awareness without integrating. This is **the central unresolved structural problem of the Subject's psychology** and it does not resolve in this decade or any subsequent one.

### The Marlo problem

The marriage is the test case. Marlo asks him to exist for his own sake, which is precisely the task he has organized his entire adult life around avoiding. He fails her repeatedly — not by infidelity or cruelty, but by **chronic absence into mission-attachment**, which is the only way he knows to feel real. The pattern is consistent with the parentified-child's adult marriage: he can love her but cannot center her, because centering anyone for their own sake (rather than as a recipient of his reparative debt) requires a self he has never built.

### Defenses

Mature defenses (humor in a non-self-attacking register, sublimation through writing, anticipation) come online for the first time, layered over the persisting reparation/identification core. The defensive structure becomes more textured and less rigid.

### Shift

Closes with the gamma transfusion arc and a deepening sense that his body is no longer his — preparing the ground for the next decade's somatic catastrophe.

---

## 7.6 40s — THE A-BOMB PERIOD: Wish-Fulfillment and Its Cost

### Presenting picture

Gamma-converted into a powerful blue Hulk-form. For the first time in his life, the Subject *is* the giant rather than the keeper of one. The arc is so transparent it is itself diagnostic.

### Affect regulation — Phase IV, attempted role-reversal

The Subject tries to solve the lifelong problem by becoming the attachment object himself — to be the one others need to regulate. This is the **manic defense** in Klein's sense: the omnipotent reversal of helplessness. It does not work. The behavioral signature is wrong: he is uncomfortable with the power, deflects credit, returns compulsively to the human-scale role even while in monster-form. The arc demonstrates ego-syntonic refusal of grandiosity — he has the wound for narcissism but not the structure, and given the power he discovers he does not want it.

This is the most important *negative finding* of the entire profile: confronted with the literal solution to his original problem (now I am the giant, now the debt is paid), the Subject finds that the problem was never really about power. It was about being needed. And being the giant does not make him needed in the way being the keeper did.

### Cognitive style

Largely unchanged by transformation, which is itself diagnostic — the cognitive habits are deeply consolidated and survive even a total somatic shift. He continues to think like the human in the room, even when he is the monster.

### Self-concept

The bifurcation persists and acquires a new layer. Now there are three: the boy who owes Banner, the cosmic figure who summoned the Golden Age, and the gamma-mutate who could have been a giant. None integrate. The Subject's identity is now a stratigraphy of unintegrated selves, each from a different decade.

### Hearing loss

Acquired in this period (and earlier Hulk-proximate combat). Becomes canonically depicted. Functionally and symbolically appropriate: the man whose entire skill is *listening to giants* loses some of his hearing. He does not visibly catastrophize this, which is consistent with his lifelong somatic stoicism — the body has not been fully his since adolescence; another loss to it is absorbed rather than mourned.

### Shift

Killed by the Intelligencia. Resurrected. The experience of clinical death is not, in canon, given the psychological weight it would warrant; the Subject absorbs it into the ongoing pattern.

---

## 7.7 50s+ — THE WHISPERER ERA AND LATE-LIFE PATTERN

### Presenting picture

Reverts. Abducted by Bucky Barnes / the Whisperer and employed as intelligence asset. Continues as the figure adjacent to the story.

### Affect regulation — return to baseline strategy

The maturational gains of the David years are not lost, but they are not sufficient to resist a sufficiently powerful pull from the most over-determined attachment object available — *the real Bucky*. The Subject is operationalized by Barnes because Barnes is uniquely incapable of being refused: he is simultaneously the dead boy the Subject tried to replace for Cap, the rescuer-archetype, and a wounded giant who needs a keeper. Every vector of the Subject's attachment system points the same direction. His agency in this arrangement is, clinically, severely compromised — not in a way that excuses him, but in a way that explains him.

### Cognitive style

Tactically seasoned, unflappable, morally steady. Sixty years of proximity to cosmic events have produced a genuine operator's mind, which the Subject continues to discount in his self-presentation. The gap between his demonstrated competence and his self-attributed competence is now enormous and is the most reliable marker of the unresolved core wound.

### Self-concept

Stable in its instability. The bifurcation/trifurcation persists. The Subject has, in effect, made peace with not being one person, but he has not integrated. He has reached a kind of *resigned coherence* — a late-life adaptation in which the multiplicity is no longer fought but is also no longer worked on. This is sub-optimal but functional.

### Depressive baseline

Persistent dysthymia continues, punctuated by episodes around major losses and separations. He has never, in the published record, received treatment. The cultural milieu (super-adjacent, military-coded, masculine-stoic) makes treatment-seeking nearly impossible for him; he self-medicates through mission-attachment and, in fallow periods, through music and writing.

### Mortality posture

Has died and returned. Has been irradiated, fused, transformed, reverted. The Subject's relationship to his own mortality is unusual: he does not fear death (the counterphobic adolescent never fully left), but he fears *outliving usefulness*. The terror is not of ceasing to exist but of existing without an attachment object to discharge the debt into. This is the late-life form of the original survivor-guilt schema and it will, in all likelihood, organize his death whenever it comes.

---

## 7.8 CROSS-DECADE SYNTHESES

### Affect regulation, longitudinal arc

1. **Adolescent**: external/behavioral discharge (speed, music, dares).
2. **Reparative phase**: caretaking-inversion (regulate self by regulating attachment object).
3. **Symbiotic phase**: regulation by fusion (Nega-Bands).
4. **Post-Mar-Vell collapse**: failure of external regulation, first depressive decompensation.
5. **David years**: attempted internalization via narrative (memoir), partial success.
6. **A-Bomb period**: attempted role-reversal / manic defense, ego-dystonic, abandoned.
7. **Late life**: return to caretaking-inversion as default, now consciously known, no longer denied, not transcended.

The trajectory shows *partial* maturation. The Subject moved from purely external regulation to a hybrid system in which narrative self-reflection plays a real but secondary role, with attachment-based regulation remaining primary. He is more mature at 50+ than at 20, but the core strategy has not changed; it has only acquired self-awareness.

### Cognitive style, longitudinal arc

Concrete and present-focused throughout, with progressive accumulation of *domain-specific* sophistication: clinician-grade attunement to single persons (especially Banner), tactical fluency at Avengers-level operations, narrative self-understanding from the memoir work, and a stable anti-intellectual self-presentation that defends an actually-adequate intellect. He never becomes a systems thinker; he becomes an extraordinarily seasoned *particular-person* thinker.

### Self-concept, longitudinal arc

From diffuse peer-mirrored adolescent → foreclosed Banner-keeper → distributed-across-attachments → collapsed → narratively-reconstructed but bifurcated → stratified across unintegrated selves → resignedly coherent. The integration that would have closed the Eriksonian identity stage never occurs. He lives, instead, as a stable plurality.

### What changed and what did not

**Changed**: reflective function (came online in the 30s and persists), capacity for irony without self-attack, awareness of the pattern, ability to name it, tactical seasoning, accumulated moral weight.

**Did not change**: the core survivor-guilt schema, the caretaking-inversion strategy, the inability to metabolize his own significance, the dissociative response to evidence of his own power, the incapacity to center a non-giant for their own sake, the somatic uncertainty about whether his body is his, the silent Bucky wound.

### Clinical prognosis (life-course)

The Subject is functional, morally intact, and unlikely to deteriorate. He is also unlikely to substantially heal the core wound without a therapeutic relationship he will not seek. The most likely late-life trajectory is continued service-attachment, periodic depressive episodes between deployments, deepening of the resigned coherence, and — if Marlo or an equivalent peer-figure can hold him through a sustained un-attached period — possibly a final, late integration in which the cosmic and the human selves are at last permitted to belong to the same man. The Subject has done enough internal work that this is possible. He has not done enough that it is likely.

*End Section 7. Section 8 (Relational Map) proceeds from here.*


## Psychiatric Assessment & Differential

# PSYCHIATRIC ASSESSMENT & DIFFERENTIAL

## Subject: Jones, Richard Milhouse

*Longitudinal psychiatric formulation derived from sixty years of observed behavior, hospital-equivalent encounters, witnessed affective episodes, marital-record collateral (M. Chandler-Jones), and the subject's own published self-account (the* Sidekick *memoir, treated here as autobiographical document of variable reliability — confessional in tone, defensively comedic in register).*

---

## I. FRAMING NOTES BEFORE DIAGNOSIS

Three constraints must precede any nosological claim about this subject.

**First**, the subject has never, to the file's knowledge, completed a course of formal psychotherapy or been the patient of a treating psychiatrist of record. He has been examined medically more times than can be counted — radiation oncology, neurology, post-cardiac-arrest workups, gamma-cellular pathology — but his psychiatric history is uncharted clinical territory inferred from behavior. He is, in effect, a sixty-year unmedicated naturalistic case.

**Second**, ordinary diagnostic categories were built for ordinary lives. The subject's life is not ordinary. A diagnosis of, say, PTSD presupposes a baseline of safety relative to which intrusive re-experiencing is pathological; the subject's *baseline* has been proximity to gamma detonations, cosmic-scale combat, and the dying of a fused partner. Symptoms that would be florid in a civilian are, in this subject, calibrated coping. The file therefore distinguishes throughout between **clinical-threshold pathology** (impairing function relative to his peculiar environment) and **adaptive trauma physiology** (the same symptomatology functioning correctly given that environment).

**Third**, the subject's defensive style is to *narrate himself comedically*. He pre-empts assessment. Any direct clinical interview would be met with the wisecrack register — the same register he uses to soothe the Hulk and to deflect Captain America. Self-report will be unreliable by default; behavior, somatics, and collateral (Chandler-Jones, Banner, Barnes) are the more diagnostic data.

---

## II. PRIMARY DIAGNOSIS

### Complex Post-Traumatic Stress Disorder (ICD-11 6B41)

The cleanest single label for the totality. DSM-5-TR PTSD (309.81) captures parts of the picture but understates the developmental layering; ICD-11's C-PTSD construct — PTSD plus persistent disturbances in self-organization (DSO: affect dysregulation, negative self-concept, interpersonal disturbance) — is a precise fit.

**Etiology, layered chronologically:**

1. *Type II developmental trauma (childhood).* Institutional rearing in the Scarsdale group-home environment; loss or absence of primary caregivers prior to encoding; absence of a continuous attachment template. This is the *substrate*. No single incident, but a sustained deficit of mirroring, contingent response, and the experience of being uniquely valued. The subject enters adolescence with attachment circuitry primed for any available figure and a self-concept already organized around "I must earn my place."

2. *Index Criterion A event (adolescence, the test-range incident).* The proximate detonation, near-death by gamma radiation, and the immediate cognitive imprint that another person — specifically the rescuer — has been catastrophically harmed in his stead. This is a textbook PTSD-A1 exposure compounded by survivor-perpetrator role confusion: the subject is simultaneously victim (would have died), bystander, and proximate cause. The role confusion is essential. A simple survivor would carry guilt; this subject carries debt.

3. *Chronic recurrent Criterion A exposure (adulthood).* Decades of life-threatening combat, witnessed deaths, clinical death of his own person, the slow dying-by-cancer of M. Mar-Vell at intimate proximity (the dying happened *in* him, given the Nega-Band fusion, which is a category of trauma the literature has no name for). The cumulative exposure dosage is extraordinary.

4. *Embodiment trauma (sustained, non-Criterion-A).* Years of discontinuous corporeal existence under Nega-Band fusion. The phenomenology — being not-present in your own body, alternating realities, somatic occupancy by another consciousness — is closer to chronic dissociative experience than to any acute trauma, and it occurred during the window when normal young-adult bodily-self consolidation should have been completing. This produced a permanent low-grade depersonalization baseline that the subject has carried since.

**Symptom presentation, mapped to behavior:**

- *Intrusion (PTSD-B).* Pattern-evidence in the subject's compulsive return to the gamma-bomb scene as the explanatory event for everything; in his startle profile around any gamma signature (Banner's transformations produce a specific somatic response — shoulders forward, breath held, weight shifted onto the balls of the feet, hands open and slightly raised; this is not heroic readiness, it is freeze-with-orientation). The *Sidekick* memoir's structure — circling repeatedly back to the test range — is intrusive re-experiencing converted into prose.

- *Avoidance (PTSD-C).* Less prominent than expected, but present in specific topical avoidances: he does not, in private, discuss the period of acute gamma sickness; he does not discuss the Mar-Vell dying in any depth; he does not visit certain locations (the Arizona desert) without observable distress. The avoidance is *narrow and specific*, which is itself a marker of organized trauma rather than diffuse anxiety.

- *Negative alterations in cognition and mood (PTSD-D).* The persistent self-concept ("I'm just the kid," "I'm the hanger-on") is the single most stable feature of the subject across sixty years. This is the C-PTSD *negative self-concept* criterion in undiluted form. Foreshortened sense of future during depressive intervals; flat affect between attachment objects; persistent inability to claim his own consequential acts (the Destiny Force episode is the test case — he was canonically the most important human in the room and cannot integrate it).

- *Arousal and reactivity (PTSD-E).* Hypervigilance for the welfare of attachment figures, not for self. Sleep disturbance reported by Chandler-Jones collateral during high-stakes intervals. Notably *low* irritability/aggression — he routes activation into protective behavior rather than into anger, which is unusual and points back to the parentified-caretaker substrate.

- *DSO-1: Affect dysregulation.* Externalized, not internalized. He stabilizes via proximity, destabilizes via separation. The dysregulation is not the lability of borderline pathology — it is a *contingent* dysregulation, modulated by attachment availability, which is the signature pattern of disorganized-developmental trauma.

- *DSO-2: Negative self-concept.* As above. Core, pervasive, treatment-resistant by his own design (he disconfirms positive feedback as flattery and confirms negative as accurate).

- *DSO-3: Interpersonal disturbance.* Capacity for closeness is *intact and over-functioning* — the disturbance is in calibration. He attaches asymmetrically, gives more than he asks, withholds his own needs to the point of resentment or depressive collapse. The marriage to Chandler-Jones is the case study: a relationship that asks him to be an equal and is therefore the relationship he most consistently fails to fully inhabit.

**Course.** Chronic, lifelong, with episodic exacerbations rather than progressive deterioration. Improvements during stable attachment intervals (long Mar-Vell fusion period, periods of Banner-proximity, stable Chandler-Jones marriage stretches). Marked decompensations following Mar-Vell's death, following Destiny Force collapse, during separations from Chandler-Jones, and during the immediate post-A-Bomb reversion. The Whisperer-abduction asset-period likely represents an exacerbation invisible to outside observers because the subject was actively *grooming-compliant* with a figure (Barnes) onto whom decades of Bucky-substitution material was projected — i.e., the trauma was being re-enacted as cooperation.

**Prognosis.** Without treatment: stable chronicity, with risk concentrated at attachment-loss inflection points. With treatment: genuinely good, because the subject has the prerequisites — capacity for relationship, moral coherence, intact reality testing, intelligence, no characterological obstruction. He has simply never been offered the room to be the patient instead of the helper.

---

## III. COMORBID DIAGNOSES

### Persistent Depressive Disorder (DSM-5-TR 300.4), with intermittent Major Depressive Episodes

The chronic low mood between missions is not "downtime"; it is dysthymic baseline. Symptoms: anhedonia in non-mission registers (cannot enjoy ordinary leisure for sustained periods), low energy without organic cause, low self-worth (overdetermined with the C-PTSD picture), mild concentration disturbance during prolonged unattached intervals, sleep irregularity. Duration criterion (>2 years) abundantly met; in fact the dysthymic baseline appears to be the subject's *modal* state when not in active partnership.

**Superimposed MDEs** identifiable around: (a) the death of M. Mar-Vell, with severe melancholic features lasting an extended period, ego-syntonic survivor guilt prominent, weight change, anhedonia, hopelessness, possible passive ideation; (b) the post–Destiny Force collapse, with admixed dissociative/somatic features and a longer fatigue tail than the medical workup justified; (c) marital separation intervals with Chandler-Jones, presenting more typically as agitated depression with rumination; (d) the period immediately post-A-Bomb reversion, when the brief experience of power was lost and the return to "ordinary" carried a humiliation component the subject did not metabolize.

The *Sidekick* memoir is itself a depressive product — the late-life-review project, executed too early in the lifespan, characteristic of subjects who feel they have already lived past their relevance.

### Prolonged Grief Disorder (DSM-5-TR 309.89; ICD-11 6B42)

Specific to the Mar-Vell loss. Unlike ordinary bereavement, the subject lost a person with whom he had been *literally somatically continuous*. The grief response therefore had no precedent in the human bereavement literature. Persistent yearning, identity disturbance ("a part of me died"), avoidance of reminders, emotional numbness, sense that life is meaningless without the deceased — present beyond the twelve-month threshold and arguably never fully resolved; periodically reactivated by Captain-Marvel-mantle proximity (his own brief assumption of the role functioned as both reparation and re-traumatization).

### Persistent Depersonalization-Derealization (DSM-5-TR 300.6), residual

Subclinical most of the time, but present as a baseline trait. The years of Nega-Band discontinuous embodiment installed a permanent low-amplitude sense of *not quite occupying oneself*. Manifests as: the subject's tendency to narrate himself in the third person (visible in the memoir voice); a slight observable lag between affect and expression in low-stakes moments (absent under crisis, where he integrates instantly); occasional reports of "watching myself do this" during high-meaning events. Does not meet full disorder threshold most years; flared to threshold during the A-Bomb period, when bodily identity was again destabilized.

### Survivor Guilt Syndrome (non-DSM, clinically robust construct)

Carried as a permanent feature, not an episodic symptom. Drives more of the behavior than any categorical diagnosis. Specifically of the *role-confused* variant — the subject was both survivor and proximate agent of the harm — which is the variant most resistant to ordinary cognitive reframing because the guilt has a factual basis the therapist cannot dispute away.

---

## IV. SUBTHRESHOLD / TRAIT-LEVEL FEATURES

### Dependent traits, sub-threshold for Dependent Personality Disorder (301.6)

Visible: preference for being in others' orbit, difficulty initiating projects on his own behalf (versus on a partner's behalf), discomfort being alone, tendency to subordinate his preferences. Absent: he retains independent judgment, will disagree with his attachment figures vigorously (the record contains him telling Banner, Captain America, and Mar-Vell each that they are wrong, repeatedly), can function alone — badly, depressively, but functionally. The dependency is *trauma-derived attachment strategy*, not characterological dependency. Important distinction for any treatment plan.

### Mild dissociative tendency under specific cues

Not DID, not DDNOS. A circumscribed tendency to "go away" briefly when confronted with his own significance — the deflection response when called a hero in his own right. Phenomenologically: brief unfocusing, change of subject, retreat to the sidekick patter register. This is a *defensive dissociation*, narrow and predictable, not a dissociative disorder.

---

## V. RIGOROUS DIFFERENTIAL — WHAT THE SUBJECT IS *NOT*

Diagnostic discipline requires explicit exclusion. The following have been considered and rejected, with reasoning.

### Not Narcissistic Personality Disorder (301.81)

The grandiose data points exist — the Destiny Force episode, the Captain Marvel mantle assumption, the A-Bomb period — and a careless reader might pattern-match. But the grandiose moments are **ego-dystonic**: he is visibly uncomfortable with the power, deflects credit, surrenders the mantle, and the A-Bomb arc reads on close inspection as a wish-fulfillment the subject himself finds embarrassing once the wish is granted. He does not require admiration, lacks fantasies of unlimited success (his fantasies are of *adequacy*, not of triumph), shows abundant empathy of the affective and cognitive kinds, and exploits no one. The diagnostic structure simply is not there. What is there is a *narcissistic wound* — the injury — without a *narcissistic defense* — the compensation. He bears the hole without the architecture built around it. This is rarer than NPD itself and more painful, because the subject has none of the protections.

### Not Borderline Personality Disorder (301.83)

Surface resemblances: identity disturbance, attachment intensity, affective episodes, history of self-endangering behavior. Disconfirming evidence is overwhelming. (a) Attachments are *stable across decades* — sixty years of Banner, fifty-plus of Captain America/Avengers loyalty, decades-stable marriage to Chandler-Jones with normal-range conflict. BPD attachments do not look like this. (b) No idealization-devaluation cycling — idealization is stable; the disillusionment, when it arrives, is *muted and grieved*, not flipped into rage. (c) No frantic efforts to avoid abandonment — when abandoned (Cap's rejection of the Bucky substitution, separations from Chandler-Jones) he responds with depressive withdrawal, not pursuit. (d) No identity-disturbance of the BPD type — his self-concept is in fact *too stable*, fixed in a single self-deprecating valence. (e) No characteristic impulsivity in the BPD domains (spending, sex, substance use, binge eating). (f) No characteristic suicidality or self-harm. The identity diffusion he does carry is *trauma-derived* and *organized around* its diffusion, not characterologically chaotic.

### Not Antisocial Personality Disorder (301.7)

Inverted on every axis. Hypermoralized rather than under-moralized. Empathic. Loyal. Guilt-prone to a fault. Excluded categorically.

### Not Histrionic Personality Disorder (301.50)

The sidekick patter, the wisecracks, the performative register, the visible presence in dramatic events — superficially histrionic. But the function is wrong: histrionic performance seeks attention as supply, while the subject's performance seeks to *deflect* attention, pre-empt rejection, and minimize his own presence. When offered the spotlight he repeatedly declines it. The affect is comedy-as-armor, not theater-as-fuel.

### Not Schizoid or Avoidant PD

His relational orientation is the opposite of schizoid — toward, not away from. Not avoidant either: he is socially fluent, takes interpersonal risk constantly, and does not fear evaluation in the avoidant sense. He fears *being important*, which is a different fear with different etiology.

### Not Substance Use Disorder, any class

Despite a trauma load that would predict it. The light alcohol use in the rock-musician period and during depressive intervals never escalated, never produced functional impairment, never produced withdrawal, never produced tolerance escalation. This is *diagnostically significant absence*. The expected self-medication pathway has been displaced into the attachment pathway — compulsive proximity to attachment objects is itself the regulator, and it works well enough that chemical regulators have not been recruited. (A clinical risk note: should attachment availability be permanently removed, the substance risk would likely emerge late in life. He has not yet been tested by that scenario.)

### Not Adjustment Disorder (any code)

The presentation is far past adjustment-disorder duration and severity, and the stressor is not bounded.

### Not Bipolar Spectrum

No hypomanic or manic episodes on the record. The brief elevations during A-Bomb and Captain-Marvel-mantle periods were *situationally appropriate* and did not show the cognitive, energetic, sleep, or judgment features of mania. They were power-states, not mood-states.

### Not Schizophrenia-Spectrum

No psychotic features. The Destiny-Force psychic projection was a real exogenous event, not an experience of reference or grandiose delusion. Reality testing intact under conditions that would have shattered most subjects'.

### Not Autism Spectrum

Strong social-pragmatic intuition, normal-range affect reading, no restricted interests of the ASD type, no sensory-processing pattern, no early developmental markers. Excluded.

### Not ADHD

The impulsive-charge-in-where-he-can't-help behavior is sometimes mistaken for impulsivity. It is not. It is *compulsive bravery as reaction formation against helplessness* — a trauma-driven behavior with a stable, predictable trigger profile. Attention, executive function, and task persistence are unimpaired.

### Not "arrested adolescent hero-worshipper"

This is the lazy clinical read and must be explicitly refused. The pattern is not adolescent fixation on glamorous figures; the pattern is *reparative attachment to powerful figures whose neediness can absorb his debt*. He attaches not to the cool ones but to the wounded ones — Banner (the unwilling monster), Mar-Vell (the exiled soldier dying of cancer), Cap (the displaced veteran), Rom (the surgically dehumanized knight), Barnes (the brainwashed survivor). Every one of these figures is a *fellow trauma case who needs handling*. Adolescent hero-worship picks winners; the subject picks wounded sovereigns. The distinction is diagnostic.

---

## VI. COMORBIDITY MAP AND COURSE OVER TIME

The diagnoses interact. A schematic of the longitudinal interplay:

- **Adolescence through young adulthood:** C-PTSD substrate plus acute PTSD from index event; survivor guilt syndrome consolidating; dependent attachment strategy crystallizing through the early Banner-handler period.
- **Nega-Band years:** Embodiment disturbance laid down; dysthymic baseline begins; C-PTSD features partially *masked* by the constant proximity-regulation of the fusion arrangement (he was, in effect, on a continuous attachment infusion).
- **Mar-Vell terminal illness and death:** Acute MDE with melancholic features; prolonged grief disorder onset; depersonalization residual flares; C-PTSD DSO features dramatically worsen with the sudden loss of the continuous regulator.
- **Avengers-honorary/wandering middle period:** Chronic dysthymia, intermittent MDEs, stable C-PTSD; attempts at autonomy (the music, eventually the memoir) that are themselves depressive products masquerading as projects.
- **Marriage to Chandler-Jones:** Genuine therapeutic effect — a non-trauma-bonded relationship for the first time. Also exposes the dependency-without-DPD pattern: he cannot fully inhabit a relationship that does not need him as *handler*. Episodic crises around this incompatibility.
- **Acute gamma sickness, near-death, clinical death-and-resurrection events:** Each adds a layer to the trauma load. Notably, the subject does not develop new diagnoses from these — the existing structure absorbs them. This is itself a sign of how completely the trauma identity has consolidated; new traumas are filed under the same heading.
- **A-Bomb period:** Brief partial remission of the negative self-concept via finally *being* a giant; rapid recurrence on reversion; identity disturbance and depersonalization flare; possible humiliation-laden depressive interval not fully visible in the public record.
- **Whisperer asset period:** Re-enactment compliance with the literal returned Bucky. The subject was, in clinical terms, *exploitable* during this interval because the substitution wound made refusal psychologically impossible. This is a vulnerability of diagnostic interest: under sufficiently precise attachment-keyed pressure, the subject's moral judgment can be circumvented by his attachment judgment. He does not know this about himself.
- **Current era:** Stable chronicity, ongoing C-PTSD, manageable dysthymia, intact marriage with periodic strain, late-life-review tendency, increasing hearing loss adding a somatic isolation factor that bears watching as a depressogenic risk.

---

## VII. RISK ASSESSMENT

- **Suicide risk:** Low to moderate, chronic. No history of attempts on record. Passive ideation likely during MDEs. Risk factors: chronic depression, identity instability, foreshortened sense of future during depressive intervals, hearing loss / aging isolation. Protective factors: the marriage, the moral framework against self-removal, the persistent low-grade belief that he is still *needed* by someone, the absence of substance use.
- **Other-directed risk:** Negligible. The trauma routes outward as protection, not aggression.
- **Exploitation risk:** Elevated and specific. He is vulnerable to figures who can credibly occupy his attachment-debt template — particularly anyone connectable to the Bucky substitution. Counterintelligence consideration, not strictly psychiatric, but it lives at the seam.
- **Decompensation triggers to monitor:** Permanent loss of Banner (final, irreversible); permanent loss of Chandler-Jones; any event that returns him to the original gamma-bomb scene cognitively (anniversaries, geographic returns, narratives told back to him); any further somatic destabilization (re-irradiation, new fusion arrangements).

---

## VIII. FORMULATION IN ONE PARAGRAPH

The subject is a sixty-year survivor of layered trauma — developmental depr


## Behavioral Atlas

# BEHAVIORAL ATLAS: RICHARD M. JONES

*Sub-file 5 of the longitudinal dossier. Catalog of observable tells, micro-behaviors, decision habits, and somatic patterns across all known affective states. Compiled from sixty publication-years of cross-writer corroboration. Granularity prioritized; redundancy retained where the redundancy is itself the datum.*

---

## I. BASELINE / CALM STATE

The calm baseline is rare and almost never sustained for more than seventy-two hours at a stretch. When observed, it has a recognizable signature.

**Posture and carriage.** Habitually leans - against doorframes, kitchen counters, hospital bed railings, the side of a Quinjet, Banner's lab benches. Rarely occupies the center of a room; orients to walls, corners, and exits. When seated at a table with peers, takes the chair nearest the door or nearest the most powerful person present, never the head. Slouches forward with forearms on thighs when listening; this is the *sidekick posture* and it is involuntary - he assumes it in front of waitresses and senators alike.

**Hands.** Always doing something. In calm, the hands gravitate to: a guitar pick rolled between thumb and index, a coffee cup rotated a quarter-turn at a time, a pen tapped against the underside of a tabletop where the sound is muffled, the inside of his left wrist (the Nega-Band site - more on this below). When nothing is available he cracks the knuckles of his right hand against his left palm, one knuckle at a time, in order, beginning with the index.

**Eyes.** Scanning. Even in calm he tracks the room: doors, the position of the strongest person, the position of the most vulnerable. He does not make sustained eye contact in casual conversation - he looks at mouths, at hands, at the middle distance - but locks on hard when an attachment figure speaks to him directly. Pupils dilate visibly when Banner enters a room; this is documented across decades and is not under conscious control.

**Speech.** Loose, slangy, anachronistic - he carries vocabulary from every decade he has lived through and never updates cleanly. Uses *daddy-o* and *cool beans* and *legit* in the same sentence without irony. Pitch is mid-tenor, slightly nasal, with a residual Arizona vowel on words like *can't* and *bag*. Cadence accelerates when nervous, slows almost to a drawl when grounded. Sentence-final laughter - a short exhaled *heh* - punctuates roughly one in three utterances and is a defense, not amusement.

**Daily rituals (calm period, married, off-mission).**
- Wakes early, usually before Marlo; makes coffee for two before she is awake. The making of coffee for someone else is a recurring tell across the entire record - it is his most consistent gesture of care.
- Plays guitar for thirty to ninety minutes most mornings, unamplified, sitting on the edge of the bed or on a fire escape. Repertoire skews to early Dylan, Buddy Holly, and a small private rotation of songs he wrote in the 1960s and has never finished.
- Reads the newspaper - physical, not digital, this is generational and stubborn - back to front, sports and obits first, world news last.
- Checks in by phone or text with at least one of: Banner, Betty, Marlo's brother Keith (when alive), Jen Walters. The check-in is brief and ostensibly casual; he is taking attendance on the people he is responsible for.

## II. UNDER STRESS - LOW-GRADE, CHRONIC

This is his most-observed state. Stress here means: an attachment figure is unwell, a mission is pending, an anniversary of a death is approaching, or he has been alone too long.

**Sleep.** Erodes first. Drops to four to five hours, fragmented. Wakes at 3:00-3:40 AM regularly; this is the gamma-bomb hour by his internal clock (the test was pre-dawn). Goes to the kitchen, drinks water standing at the sink, does not turn on the overhead light.

**Eating.** Skips meals without noticing. Will then over-eat junk food - diner food specifically, eggs and hashbrowns and bacon, the meal of a teenage hot-rodder - in a single sitting at odd hours. Coffee intake doubles.

**Hands (escalation).** The wrist-rubbing intensifies. Left wrist specifically, where the Nega-Band sat for years. He is unaware he is doing it. When the rubbing produces a visible red band on the skin, he is in deeper trouble than he will admit.

**Music.** Plays louder, longer, and starts working on the unfinished songs. Never finishes them. The act of *almost* finishing is the regulation; completion is not the goal.

**Phone behavior.** Calls Banner more. The calls are pretextual - a question about a news item, a joke, a question Banner answered last week. He is checking the line is live. If Banner doesn't pick up within two attempts he begins driving toward Banner's last known location.

**Speech (stress register).** Wisecracks per minute increase by a factor of three. Old slang resurfaces. He performs *the kid* harder - this is observable in real time and is involuntary regression to the persona that has historically secured care.

## III. UNDER ACUTE THREAT / COMBAT-ADJACENT

The trained register. Sixty years of standing next to gamma detonations, alien invasions, and Avengers-level engagements have produced something close to professional composure under fire. Civilians and rookies routinely misread him here as braver than he is; he is not braver, he is *practiced*.

**Voice.** Drops half an octave. Loses the *heh*. Loses the slang. Sentences shorten to two and three words. Uses names hard - *Bruce. Listen. Bruce, eyes on me.* The lullaby cadence to the Hulk is the same neural circuit running at lower volume.

**Body.** Stops leaning. Squares to the threat. Distributes weight evenly across both feet. The slouch disappears entirely; he stands at his actual height, which is taller than people remember.

**Decision habits in combat.**
- Default first move: position himself between the threat and the most vulnerable non-combatant in the room. Will do this for civilians he has never met.
- Default second move: locate his attachment figure and assess their state (transforming, injured, cornered, escalating).
- Default third move: talk. He will talk to anything. He has talked down the Hulk, Mar-Vell in rage states, Rom in despair states, Genis-Vell mid-psychosis, and at least one Skrull infiltrator who shot him for the trouble.
- Will charge a being who outclasses him by ten orders of magnitude without hesitation if an attachment figure is at risk. This is not bravery in his own self-concept; it is the only behavior available to him. He has been observed to apologize, mid-charge, to the cosmic entity he is charging.

**Tells of fear (which he denies feeling).** A specific muscular freeze at the base of the jaw, visible as a tightening below the ear. A swallow before speaking. The left hand goes to the right wrist briefly - the *opposite* of the calm wrist-rub, and a separate gesture entirely; this one is a self-pat, a *you're still here* check.

**What he will not do under threat.** Will not run from a friend in danger. Will not use a firearm except as last resort (history with Banner has trained him out of guns). Will not lie to the threat - he negotiates but does not bluff; this is a documented limitation and has nearly killed him on multiple occasions.

## IV. INTIMACY - ROMANTIC, MARITAL, DOMESTIC

Intimacy is the state in which he is *least* fluent. With Marlo, observed patterns:

**Approach.** Touches her hand or the small of her back when passing in a hallway - many small contacts rather than few large ones. Sits on the floor by her chair rather than across from her. Brings her coffee, water, food, without being asked; will forget to feed himself in the same hour.

**Verbal intimacy.** Uses humor to open and close emotional conversations; the middle of the conversation, where the actual content lives, he handles haltingly and often with the lights off or while driving (sideways intimacy - looking forward, not at her). Tells her he loves her easily and often; tells her he is *afraid* almost never, and only in the dark.

**Sexual.** Tender, attentive, somewhat anxious - performance of adequacy is part of the dynamic, which Marlo has called out and which he has only partly metabolized.

**Withdrawal.** When stressed by external events he withdraws not by leaving but by being physically present and affectively absent - sitting on the same couch, watching the same television, looking at the screen and not seeing it. Marlo has learned to read this and to ask one question: *Where are you?* He will sometimes answer truthfully.

**Argument behavior.** Does not raise his voice with her. Goes quiet. Leaves the room briefly - to the porch, the fire escape, the garage - and returns within ten to twenty minutes. Will not let an argument go overnight if he can help it; the abandonment fear is too loud. Apologizes first, even when not at fault. This is not weakness; it is triage.

**With Banner (a different kind of intimacy).** Sits close. Reads him constantly - skin tone, pulse at the temple, jaw set, pupil size, breathing rate. Speaks softly. Hand on Banner's shoulder is one of his most-photographed gestures across decades. With Banner he allows silence; with Marlo he fills it.

## V. GRIEF

He has buried more people than most soldiers. The grief signature is consistent and specific.

**Acute phase (first 48-72 hours).** Hyper-functional. Makes the arrangements, calls the people, brings the coffee, stands at the back of the room. Does not cry in public, with two recorded exceptions (Mar-Vell's death; one of Marlo's medical scares). Eats almost nothing. Drinks coffee continuously. Speech compresses to logistics.

**Sub-acute (days 4-30).** Plays the guitar more, talks less. Disappears for hours at a time - drives. The driving is a regulation strategy that goes back to adolescence: a car, alone, fast roads, no destination. He returns smelling of gas station coffee and looking calmer.

**Anniversary behavior.** Knows the dates without consulting a calendar. On Mar-Vell's death anniversary he is observably elsewhere - quieter, slower, prone to long silences. Does not announce it. Marlo has learned the date and lets him be. He visits no graves; the grief is not located in places, it is located in his body.

**Survivor-guilt spike with each death.** Each loss reactivates the prime scene. After every major death in his orbit, he engages in a brief, semi-conscious behavioral compensation: takes on a new dependent (a stray, a rookie hero, a neighbor), increases his check-ins on the surviving attachment figures, sometimes drinks slightly more for a finite period and then stops. The drinking is symptomatic, not addictive - it tracks the grief curve and disappears with it.

**What he never does in grief.** Does not blame the killer with sustained intensity. Does not seek revenge. Does not romanticize the dead in speech - the dead are dead, and sentimentality offends his sense of accuracy about them. He will tell true stories about them, including unflattering ones, and laugh.

## VI. VICTORY

The most diagnostically revealing state because it is the one he handles worst.

**Immediate post-victory.** Deflects credit instantly and reflexively - *I just stood there, it was Bruce, it was Cap, it was the big guy.* This is not modesty performance; it is genuine inability to incorporate the win into his self-concept. If credited publicly he will look at the floor, rub the back of his neck, and change the subject within two sentences.

**The dissociative slip.** After a clear personal victory - the Destiny Force summoning, the Captain Marvel period, the A-Bomb arc - he exhibits a recognizable destabilization: sleep degrades, wisecracks intensify, he picks fights with people he loves over trivia. The pattern is consistent enough across decades to be predictive. *Significance is a stressor for him.* Defeat he can metabolize; victory he cannot.

**Celebration behavior.** Buys drinks for the team; drinks one himself, slowly. Tells stories that center other people. Will sometimes play guitar at the end of the night if asked, never if not asked.

**Private post-victory.** Goes home and is quiet for two or three days. Marlo has identified this and named it the *good-news flu*. He recovers when the next problem arrives.

## VII. DEFEAT / FAILURE

Paradoxically more comfortable.

**Immediate.** Absorbs blame faster than it can be assigned. Will claim responsibility for outcomes he had no causal role in. This is the survivor-guilt schema offered the food it craves.

**Operational recovery.** Fast. He is in the next room, on the next mission, on the next call, within hours. The motion is the medicine.

**Affective recovery.** Slow and incomplete. Each failure is filed in the same drawer as the original gamma bomb; the drawer has no bottom.

**Tells of internalized failure.** The wrist-rub returns. The unfinished songs come out. He calls Banner at odd hours and pretends it is about something else. He gets a haircut - genuinely, this is a documented behavior: after major failures, within two weeks, he gets his hair cut shorter. Read this as a small somatic *start over*.

## VIII. AROUND COSMIC / GODLIKE FIGURES

A distinct interpersonal mode. With beings of cosmic scale (Mar-Vell, Genis, the Watcher when present, Thanos at proximity, the Destiny Force itself), he displays:

- **Inappropriate familiarity.** Treats them as people. Uses first names, nicknames, jokes. This is not bravado; it is the only register he has and he refuses to upgrade it. The effect on cosmic beings is often disarming and occasionally life-saving.
- **No awe display.** Will not perform smallness for power, even when he feels it. This is a hard ethical line for him and one of the few places he is rigid.
- **Vigilance for the moment power slips its leash.** Watches for the eyes, the breath, the language drift that precedes an episode. He has more reps at this than any non-powered human alive.

## IX. AROUND OTHER NON-POWERED PEERS

Less anchored, more performative, more uncertain. With ordinary humans:

- Over-explains his life, then under-explains it, then deflects.
- Drinks slightly more.
- Asks more questions than he answers - genuine curiosity but also defense.
- Locates the most powerless person in the room and orients to them. Will end the evening talking to the bartender or the bouncer rather than the celebrity.

## X. SOMATIC AND MICRO-TELLS - CONSOLIDATED INDEX

For ease of field reference.

- **Left wrist rub** - chronic low-grade stress, unconscious, Nega-Band site.
- **Right-hand knuckle crack, index outward** - calm-state self-soothing.
- **Right-wrist self-pat** - acute fear check, distinct from the calm rub.
- **Jaw freeze below the ear** - suppressed fear, combat-adjacent.
- **Sentence-final *heh*** - defensive humor, baseline.
- **Pupil dilation on Banner's entry** - involuntary, decades-stable.
- **Slouch dissolution** - threat detected, body squaring.
- **Slang regression** - stress-induced persona retreat.
- **Sideways intimacy (driving, dark rooms)** - permitted vulnerability conditions.
- **3:00-3:40 AM wakeups** - gamma-hour somatic memory.
- **Coffee for two** - care expression, dating to adolescence.
- **Post-failure haircut** - somatic reset, within two weeks.
- **Guitar volume** - direct index of internal pressure.
- **Phone check-ins to Banner** - line-live verification, escalates linearly with stress.
- **Driving without destination** - regulation strategy, lifelong.

## XI. DECISION HABITS - GENERAL

- **Defaults to loyalty over law, every time.** Has lied to military authorities, federal authorities, Avengers leadership, and S.H.I.E.L.D. for the sake of attachment figures. Does not regret these decisions in the moment; sometimes regrets them years later, never enough to change the policy.
- **Cannot refuse a direct request from a recognized attachment figure.** This is the single largest exploitable vulnerability in his profile and has been weaponized against him repeatedly. The Whisperer/Bucky relationship is the most acute example: the cost to him of saying no is greater than the cost of any plausible mission.
- **Will refuse a request from an institution.** Reflexively suspicious of organizations, even ones he serves. Does not trust S.H.I.E.L.D., did not trust the Initiative, will not trust whatever comes next.
- **Tells the truth as a baseline.** Lies only under combat necessity and only to protect a person. Cannot sustain a long-form deception; will break under social pressure within hours.
- **Volunteers for the worst job in the room.** This is so reliable it functions as a tell - if no one has volunteered to do the hard, dirty, dangerous, unrewarding thing within thirty seconds of it being identified, he will. Predictable enough to be planned around by allies and exploited by adversaries.
- **Will not abandon a position once committed.** The flip side of the volunteer reflex. Once he says yes, he stays. This is the single most reliable thing about him and the basis of every long attachment in his life.

*End Behavioral Atlas. Cross-reference Sub-file 6 (Routes, Routines, Geography) and Sub-file 9 (Exploitable Vulnerabilities - Restricted) for operational continuation.*


## Daily Life, Routines & Rituals

# UATU DOSSIER — SECTION 7
## Daily Life, Routines & Rituals
*Subject: Jones, Richard Milhouse ("Rick")*
*Surveillance basis: longitudinal behavioral inference, cross-era. A composite "median week" is reconstructed from observed patterns; deviations by life-phase are flagged.*

---

### 7.1 The Architecture of a Day

Subject does not keep a schedule in the civilian sense. He keeps a **standby pattern** — the cadence of a man who has, since age sixteen, lived on call to a being or a mission larger than himself. The day is organized not around tasks but around **the phone, the door, and the news.** Remove those three vectors and Subject's day collapses into low-grade aimlessness within seventy-two hours; this is documented across at least four extended "civilian" interludes in the record, most clearly during the David-era Reno period and the post-Marlo separation months.

**Wake time** is irregular and trends late: typical first movement between 0930 and 1115, later in depressive phases (1300+), abruptly normal (0530–0630) when attached to an active operation or proximate to Banner. He does not use an alarm by preference; he wakes to **ambient cue** — light, traffic, a phone, the specific creak of whatever apartment he is currently occupying. The exception is operational tempo, in which case he is up before the alarm and has been awake, lightly, for an hour.

**First fifteen minutes after waking** are diagnostic and constant across decades:
1. Lies still, eyes open, ninety seconds to two minutes. Listening. (Inferred origin: years of waking next to a man who might already be green.)
2. Checks his hands. A specific tic — turns them palm-up, palm-down, flexes the fingers. Pure somatic verification, traceable to the Nega-Band years when waking might mean discovering one was in the Negative Zone. He still does it. He does not know he does it.
3. Reaches for the bedside surface — phone now, transistor radio in earlier eras, comm-bracelet during the Mar-Vell fusion — and checks for messages before standing.
4. Stands, cracks his neck left then right, walks to a window, looks out for a count of roughly ten seconds. Threat-scan disguised as a stretch.
5. *Then* coffee.

### 7.2 The Coffee, the Kitchen, the Radio

Coffee is **the only ritual Subject performs with reverence.** Drip, never instant, never espresso — he is suspicious of espresso the way a man raised in 1950s Arizona group-home institutional food remains suspicious of anything that announces itself. Black, two cups before he speaks to anyone he is not sleeping with. The pot is started before the bathroom. In Marlo-cohabitation periods, whoever is up first starts it; she has commented on the fact that he measures grounds with a tablespoon by feel and is always within a quarter-spoon of correct.

Breakfast: minimal, and **always the same three or four items in rotation** — toast with butter; eggs over easy with toast; cereal (sweetened, a tell — the orphanage child never lost the taste); occasionally, when nostalgic or hungover or grieving, a diner run. He eats standing or at a counter; sitting down to a plated breakfast in his own home reads to him as an event and makes him self-conscious.

The radio or its equivalent is **on by 0945** and stays on most of the day. Music in the morning (rock-era station, classic-rock by the David run, eclectic by present day — he genuinely likes the music, this is not just background); news in the afternoon. He prefers AM talk and local news to national broadcasts. **He does not watch much television by choice**, though he will leave it on for company. The screen makes him passive; the radio lets him pace.

### 7.3 Movement Through the Apartment

Subject **paces.** This is the single most observable somatic-behavioral fact about him. Surveillance footage of any extended indoor period will show a worn track in carpet or floor finish: kitchen-to-window, kitchen-to-door, occasionally a longer loop through the living room. He paces while on the phone (always), while thinking (always), while listening to music (often), and while drinking his second coffee. He does not sit for extended periods. When he does sit, it is on the **arm** of a couch or the edge of a chair — a posture of provisionality, ready to stand. Sustained relaxed sitting (deep in a chair, legs extended) is reserved for two contexts: watching a ball game alone, or sitting with Banner in a safe room, where he deliberately performs ease as a regulatory cue for the other man.

He keeps **doors slightly ajar** — bathroom, bedroom, closet. A man who has been trapped in too many small spaces (trench, Negative Zone, holding cells, the inside of his own gamma-mutated body) and who unconsciously refuses to be sealed in again. Marlo has reportedly closed them behind him and he has reportedly reopened them without comment.

### 7.4 The Guitar

The guitar is the **second-most-reliable daily ritual** and the most psychologically loaded one. Subject plays nearly every day, in short sessions — fifteen to forty minutes — almost never longer. He plays:
- *In the morning,* warming up his hands while the coffee brews. Scales, a few bars of something familiar, no song completed.
- *In the late afternoon,* when the day's purposelessness is at its peak. This session is the longest and the most likely to produce actual songs, fragments, or recorded voice-memo ideas. It functions as **affect regulation** — the equivalent of another man's run or another man's drink.
- *Before bed,* occasionally. Slow, quiet, fingerpicked. The Hulk-lullaby register. He does this most reliably on nights when he has been in proximity to Banner or to violence.

He owns more guitars than he needs and tunes them obsessively. He restrings by feel, no tuner for the final pass. Notebooks of half-written lyrics accumulate; he loses them and does not look for them. The *Sidekick* memoir is the prose analog of this — episodic life-review, written in bursts, abandoned and resumed.

### 7.5 The Phone

The phone is **the central object of Subject's life** and has been since rotary days. He keeps it close, charges it religiously, answers on the second ring (never the first — a tell; he wants a half-second to compose his voice), and **never lets it go to voicemail if he recognizes the number** of an attachment figure. If the number is unknown he lets it ring out and then immediately calls back from a different posture (standing, pacing). His call-back latency is under five minutes for anyone in his Tier-1 attachment circle; under an hour for Tier-2; he forgets Tier-3 entirely for days.

Tells on calls:
- **With Banner:** voice drops half an octave, slower cadence, more silence. He paces *less* during these calls — they ground him. Often he is sitting on the floor against a wall by the end.
- **With Marlo:** faster, brighter, performatively casual. Wisecracks per minute spike. He paces more. He ends these calls with "yeah" three or four times before hanging up.
- **With Cap:** stands up straighter even though no one is watching. Speech becomes mildly more formal. Will not interrupt.
- **With any cosmic/Avengers-tier operational contact:** completely flat, professional, efficient. The sidekick patter vanishes entirely. This is the operator voice almost no one in his civilian life ever hears.

### 7.6 The Walk
