He almost never uses his middle name (*Milhouse*) and grows visibly tense when others do; it is a group-home name, a name on intake paperwork, and it carries the institutional weight he has spent his life talking around.

First-person pronouns are deployed sparingly relative to baseline. He says *we* when describing his own actions if any partner was present (*we figured*, *we got out*) and *you know how it is* in place of *I felt*. Genuine first-person emotional declarations - *I am angry, I am hurt, I am afraid* - are vanishingly rare in the record, and when they occur they are diagnostic flares: something is wrong at a level he can no longer route around the pronoun for.

---

## 3. SYNTAX AND RHETORIC

### Sentence architecture

Two dominant constructions:

1. **The deflective compound.** "Yeah, well — *clause* — but, you know, *clause*." A statement, a hedge, a softening tag. This is his civilian default and accounts for roughly forty percent of recorded utterances in non-crisis settings.

2. **The clipped imperative.** "Doc. Look at me. Breathe. With me, Doc. Breathe." Two-to-four-word sentences, no qualifiers, present-tense action verbs. This is his crisis register, identical in structure across encounters with the Hulk, with Mar-Vell mid-cosmic-event, with Banner mid-transformation, with civilians in shock. The cadence is **lullaby-derived**, descended from the literal lullabies he sang to calm the early Hulk; he has generalized the rhythmic pattern of soothing across his whole emergency vocabulary.

He uses **conditionals defensively** ("if I'm reading this right," "if you wanted me to," "if I'm not in the way") and **the past unreal subjunctive** almost not at all. He does not say *I would have*. He says *I should've*. The retrospective modal of choice is the guilt-modal.

### Humor mechanics

His wit is **structurally specific** and recognizable across writers' hands:

- **Self-targeted punchlines.** The joke is on him. The setup is something dangerous or impressive; the punchline reduces his role in it. ("So I'm holding the cosmic doohickey and the universe is ending and I'm thinking — boy, this is above my pay grade.") This is preemptive deflation; he removes himself from the heroic frame before anyone else can.
- **Pop-culture referents one beat late.** Names a song that came out two years ago as if it were current. Quotes movies a half-generation after their cultural moment. Calibrated to make him sound like the guy who never quite caught up - a diminishment performance.
- **Pun-tolerance high, pun-production moderate.** He laughs at bad puns from Banner. He produces middling ones himself, usually when nervous.
- **Dark humor in combat.** Drops gallows lines under fire that are funnier than his civilian material, drawn from the same operational register that strips his uptalk. Combat-Rick is wittier than rest-Rick.

He does not punch down. He has never been recorded mocking a civilian, a child, or someone weaker than himself in the field. The targets of his jokes are: himself, Banner (rarely, gently), cosmic absurdity, and authority figures (Ross most consistently, in muttered asides).

### Rhetorical posture in argument

He **argues from anecdote, not principle**. Confronted with an ethical dispute, he reaches for an instance - "Yeah but remember when —" - rather than a frame. This is partly cognitive style (concrete, intuitive, as the psychological assessment notes) and partly **rhetorical strategy**: anecdote makes him the witness rather than the judge, which is the position he was made for. He almost never says *should*. He says *I saw this happen and here's how it went*. He lets the listener draw the conclusion.

When he does deploy principle, it is usually borrowed and attributed. *Cap says.* *Doc always told me.* *Marv used to put it like —* He launders his ethics through dead and absent giants. The convictions are his; he refuses to claim them.

---

## 4. THE DEFLECTION REPERTOIRE

A formal taxonomy of how Subject avoids saying what he means.

### 4.1 The shrug-verbal

"I dunno." "It is what it is." "What're you gonna do." "Whatever." Deployed when asked how he is feeling. Reliable indicator of an unprocessed emotional state; the more he says it in a single conversation, the worse the affect underneath.

### 4.2 The role-retreat

When asked about his significance, achievements, or interior life, he reframes himself into a function: *I'm just the kid. Just a guy. Just along for the ride. Just the human in the room.* The word **"just"** is so frequent in these constructions it functions as a personal idiolect marker; cross-corpus, he uses *just* approximately three times the baseline rate for adult American English speakers, almost entirely in self-locating constructions. Strike-through *just* from his transcripts and you get a man making considerably more direct claims about himself than he can otherwise tolerate making.

### 4.3 The Banner-pivot

In any conversation that begins to center him, he can be expected within three turns to redirect to Banner's situation, the Hulk's whereabouts, or the current cosmic problem. This is so reliable it is operationally exploitable - interrogators wanting to keep him on topic must repeatedly haul him back from the pivot. The pivot is **not evasion in bad faith**; he genuinely finds Banner's problems more interesting than his own and is unsettled by sustained personal attention.

### 4.4 The musical interlude

In moments of unmanageable feeling he reaches for **song lyric, song reference, or actual song**. He has been documented humming, whistling, or quietly singing during: hospital vigils, post-combat decompression, marital fights mid-de-escalation, and his own near-death events. The repertoire is heavy on early-period rock - Beatles, Dylan, Stones, some Springsteen, a thread of folk - and the song chosen is almost always lyrically apposite to the situation in a way he would deny intending. This is the **closest thing he has to genuine emotional confession**: he routes through someone else's words rather than risk his own.

### 4.5 The Cap-quote

When morally cornered he produces a Captain America aphorism, usually slightly misremembered, often invented, attributed regardless. This is sincere and defensive at once; the borrowed authority absolves him of having opinions of his own.

### 4.6 The wisecrack-and-pivot

A joke at his own expense followed by a hard subject change. Time between punchline and pivot averages under two seconds. The pivot is to the operational present: *anyway, what's the plan*. This is his most reliable maneuver for closing down a line of inquiry into his interior, and it works on almost everyone except Marlo.

---

## 5. HOW HE COMMUNICATES THE BIG EMOTIONS

### 5.1 Love

Subject does not say *I love you* readily. The verbal record contains the phrase, directed at Marlo, perhaps a few dozen times across decades of marriage; directed at Banner, never in those words; directed at Mar-Vell, never in those words, though the somatic fact of the fusion made the words structurally redundant.

What he does instead:

- **Service language.** Love is expressed as logistics. *You eat today? You sleep? Lemme handle that. I got it.* He routes affection through utility; the verbal currency is the offer of labor.
- **Physical attendance.** He shows up. The verbal correlate is the unannounced phone call or text - *just checking in, no reason* - which is the closest he gets to saying *I am thinking of you* without saying it.
- **The use of "buddy" and "pal" upward.** These small-male-intimacy words are dropped on the people he loves at moments of high feeling. *I got you, buddy.* *Hang in there, pal.* The diminutive is the declaration.
- **With Marlo specifically:** he uses her name in full when he is most in love with her, not nicknames. *Marlo.* Said softly. The diminutive *Marl* is daily affection; the full name is the declaration of arrival.

### 5.2 Threat

He does not threaten well and knows it. When he attempts threat language - rare, almost always on behalf of someone else - he sounds borrowed, as if quoting tougher men. The tells are:

- **Escalation into formality.** Threat-Rick becomes weirdly grammatical. *You will not touch her.* *You are going to put that down.* The contractions drop out. This is **mimicry of authority-figure speech** (Cap, Ross, Banner-when-Banner) and is one of his few genuinely unconvincing registers.
- **Naming the giant in his pocket.** His operative threat is almost always implied delegation: *you really want me to make a phone call?* The threat is never himself; it is the cosmic relationship behind him. He is aware this is what he has, and uses it without shame in defense of others, with discomfort in defense of himself.
- **The flat voice.** When he is genuinely about to do something dangerous, his speech slows, drops in pitch, and loses ornament. This is the rarest register in the record and the most reliable danger signal. When Rick Jones is making short declarative sentences without filler and without uptalk, the situation has moved past words.

### 5.3 Grief

Grief is the emotion he handles worst and most often. Catalogue:

- **The Mar-Vell deathbed register.** Documented (witnesses present, partial recordings): he held conversation in normal cadence almost to the end, slipped into single-syllable affirmations - *yeah. yeah. I know. I know* - and stopped speaking entirely in the final hour. He did not weep audibly until after. The post-mortem speech, recovered from subsequent interviews and the David-era flashbacks, is marked by **present-tense slips** (*Marv says* rather than *Marv used to say*), which persist for years and have never fully resolved.
- **Anticipatory grief.** When he expects loss, he becomes more verbose, not less. Talks around the subject in widening circles. The Banner-on-the-run periods produced documented spikes in word count per turn.
- **Anniversary behavior.** On the anniversary of the gamma detonation (verifiable across multiple years of dated correspondence) his communications become tersa, his humor flat, his Banner-pivots more frequent. He does not name the anniversary. He observes it linguistically.
- **The lullaby.** In acute grief he has been observed humming the specific tune he used to soothe the early Hulk. This is the deepest layer of his vocal archive and surfaces only when he is, in some sense, soothing himself by performing the act of soothing another. It is the closest thing to prayer in his repertoire.

### 5.4 Fear

He does not admit fear in language and rarely shows it in prosody, but the physical correlates leak: increased filler density (*um*, *uh*, *like*, *I mean*), increased self-touch on the throat or wrist, rapid blinking. Verbally, fear surfaces as **excessive logistical detail** - he begins narrating the plan in granular steps as a self-regulation strategy.

### 5.5 Anger

Suppressed at baseline, leaks as sarcasm. When it breaks through it is **directed at himself first** (*God, I'm an idiot, I'm such an idiot*) and outward only after exhaustion. Anger at giants - Banner, Cap, Mar-Vell when alive - is almost always expressed as **withdrawn cooperation** rather than confrontation: he goes quiet, becomes literal, stops volunteering. The silence is the rage. Sustained articulate confrontation has been documented perhaps a half-dozen times in the entire record, and each occasion marks a relationship inflection point.

---

## 6. CONTEXT-SPECIFIC REGISTERS

- **With Banner-as-Banner:** familiar, fast, full of in-jokes, marked by interruption tolerance on both sides; this is his most *natural* speech, the one where uptalk and self-deprecation modulate down toward equality. Diction simplifies; vocabulary range narrows; they speak in shorthand neither outsider fully parses.
- **With the Hulk:** monosyllabic-on-purpose, present-tense, declarative, soft. Adjusts vocabulary to whichever Hulk persona is present (Savage, Banner-Hulk, Joe Fixit, Devil, Immortal) with documented fluency. He is one of the few humans who has held intelligible conversation with every iteration.
- **With Captain America:** more formal, more *sir*, more deference; the upward-uptalk peaks here. He becomes a slightly younger version of himself in Cap's presence and has never grown out of it across sixty years.
- **With Marlo:** the register he resists most and inhabits most fully when he allows himself. Plain language. Fewer jokes. Longer silences tolerated. She is the only person he can be quiet with on the record.
- **With Ross and military authority:** sardonic, slightly insolent, controlled; one of the few contexts where he produces sustained sarcasm at someone else's expense. Old grievance.
- **With the press / public:** practiced, glib, deflective. The *Sidekick* memoir tour transcripts are a clinic in performed disclosure - he gives the appearance of candor while routing every personal question into anecdote about a more famous person.
- **With cosmic entities:** unintimidated, casual, sometimes irreverent. The Negative Zone years calibrated him to a scale at which the Watcher is a guy he might wave to. This is one of the most underappreciated linguistic facts about him.
- **With the Whisperer (the real Bucky):** documented in fragmentary post-abduction interviews. The register is destabilized - he addresses the Whisperer with a combination of operational professionalism and a small, almost child's voice that surfaces nowhere else in the record. The substitution wound speaking back.

---

## 7. WRITTEN VS. SPOKEN

In writing - the *Sidekick* manuscript, journals, correspondence - he is **markedly more articulate, more reflective, and more emotionally direct** than in speech. The wisecrack register thins out; the role-retreats remain but are more clearly framed as such; actual interior states get named. This gap between oral and written self is **one of the larger such gaps in the available record for any subject of comparable surveillance interest**. He can write what he cannot say. The diagnostic implication is that the spoken sidekick affect is a real-time social adaptation, not a deficit of insight; he understands himself better than he allows interlocutors to know.

His handwriting is fast, slanted, legible; he prints rather than cursives when he wants to be sure he is understood. He doodles in margins - guitars, small cars, the Hulk in profile.

---

## 8. SUMMARY OF LINGUISTIC TELLS

For operational reference:

| Tell | Indicates |
|---|---|
| Uptalk vanishes; pitch drops | Crisis register engaged; he is operational |
| Slang from his teens spikes | Identity threat; conserving the pre-bomb self |
| The word *just* appears repeatedly in self-reference | Active self-diminishment in progress |
| Pivots to Banner within three turns | Sustained personal attention has become unbearable |
| Hums or quotes a lyric | Feeling something he will not name |
| Present-tense slip about a dead person | Unresolved grief surfacing |
| Sentences become weirdly formal | Attempting threat; under-equipped for it |
| Filler density spikes; logistical narration begins | Fear, suppressed |
| Self-directed anger (*I'm an idiot*) | Anger displaced inward; outward anger may follow |
| Falls silent with an intimate | Maximum rage OR maximum love; context disambiguates |
| Says *Marlo* in full | Love, declared |
| Says *Marl* | Love, daily |
| Borrows a Cap aphorism | Moral cornering; deflecting to higher authority |
| Hums the Hulk lullaby | Self-soothing by proxy; deep distress |
| Says his own middle name without flinching | Has not occurred in the record |

---

*End section. Cross-reference with HABITS & RITUALS and RELATIONAL MAPPING for behavioral correlates of the linguistic patterns above.*


## Predictive Model I — Routine & Social

# PREDICTIVE MODEL I — ROUTINE & SOCIAL

*Forward predictions of high-confidence behavior in situations the published record does not directly depict. Each entry follows GIVEN → EXPECT logic, grounded in the longitudinal pattern.*

---

## A. Domestic & Solitary Routine

**GIVEN** a morning alone in the apartment with no mission, no Banner-call, no Avengers page →
**EXPECT** Rick wakes early (between 5:40 and 6:20), not from discipline but from the chronic shallow-sleep architecture of someone whose nervous system has rehearsed forty years of being roused by gamma alarms, transformations, and crisis pages. He lies still for two to four minutes inventorying the room before rising — a hypervigilant scan he has never consciously identified as such. He makes coffee strong enough that Marlo has remarked on it. He drinks the first cup standing at the window, not the table. He will not sit down for breakfast alone; sitting alone at a table is a posture his body associates with the group-home cafeteria and he avoids it without knowing why.

**GIVEN** an unscheduled empty afternoon →
**EXPECT** within ninety minutes he will manufacture a task — restring the guitar, reorganize a shelf of cassettes and minidiscs he has not converted to digital, walk a route past a payphone or a diner he associates with a past mission. Unstructured solitude produces a low-grade dread he discharges into small rituals. If the empty stretch extends past four hours he begins low-level phone behavior: checking on people who did not ask to be checked on. Banner first if reachable, then Marlo, then a rotating roster of Avengers-adjacent contacts (Jen Walters, Betty if speaking, Hercules, Carol). The calls are brief, framed as "just seeing if you're alive," and end before the other party can ask the same of him.

**GIVEN** insomnia (frequent; estimate 3-4 nights per week) →
**EXPECT** he does not take sleep aids — pharmacological intervention on his nervous system is something he is quietly terrified of after the gamma years. Instead: a fixed routine. Television on at low volume, never news, usually late-period reruns of shows he watched in the group home. Acoustic guitar in his lap, often unplayed, functioning as a sensory anchor. He will eventually write — letters, journal fragments, the rolling unfinished sequel to *Sidekick* he has not admitted to anyone he is still working on. Sleep arrives between 2:40 and 3:30 AM. He wakes at his usual time anyway.

**GIVEN** his apartment laid out for inspection →
**EXPECT** clean but not ordered; the clean of someone who picks up reflexively, not someone who systematizes. A guitar (one acoustic, one electric, both kept tuned), a small amp. Books in stacks rather than shelves, weighted toward biographies and memoirs — he reads other people's life-reviews compulsively. A drawer with hearing-aid batteries, spare cases, cleaning brushes, organized far more carefully than the rest of the apartment. Photographs displayed sparingly: Marlo, one of Mar-Vell that he keeps face-down when company is expected and uprights again afterward, no photographs of himself young. A first-aid kit far above the size a normal household maintains. A go-bag in the hall closet he refreshes every six weeks without commentary.

---

## B. Eating, Drinking, Body

**GIVEN** any meal →
**EXPECT** he eats fast. Group-home pacing. He has never lost it. He notices other people noticing and slows performatively for the duration of the table, then accelerates again the moment attention shifts. He under-orders in restaurants and finishes other people's plates. He prefers diner food, will eat anything put in front of him, refuses to send food back under any circumstances — a deference learned early and never reconsidered.

**GIVEN** the offer of a drink in a social setting →
**EXPECT** he accepts and nurses. One beer over ninety minutes is his standard pace. He has a private cutoff he never names — two drinks in a public setting, three at home with Marlo, never four. He watches other people's drinking with the practiced eye of someone who has been the designated functional one in too many rooms. He does not lecture. He will quietly move a glass out of reach of a friend who has had enough.

**GIVEN** a check-up at any medical setting →
**EXPECT** he downplays symptoms by roughly fifty percent, omits the gamma history unless directly asked, and gives a sanitized version of his medical record that he has rehearsed. He is more honest with nurses than with doctors. He cannot lie about pain to someone who has touched him. He will not consent to MRI without a long conversation; enclosed scanners trigger Negative Zone-adjacent body memory he has never named.

**GIVEN** an unexpected loud noise in a quiet environment →
**EXPECT** a startle response disproportionate to the stimulus, immediately masked by a joke. He recovers visibly within three seconds, internally within twenty minutes. His resting baseline elevates for the rest of the day. He will not mention it.

**GIVEN** his hearing aids →
**EXPECT** he removes them in two situations and only two: showering and intimacy. He keeps spares in three locations (apartment, go-bag, glove box) and a tool kit for repairs. He has taught himself basic lip-reading and uses it more than he admits. In loud rooms he positions himself to the left of the speaker (better ear). He avoids subway platforms when he can. He has stopped going to live concerts entirely and tells people it's because he's getting old.

---

## C. Movement, Routes, Spatial Habits

**GIVEN** any walk through a city →
**EXPECT** he varies his route. Not from formal tradecraft training but from the absorbed paranoia of decades of being a target-adjacent person. He notices rooflines. He notices license plates two beats longer than civilians do. He clocks exits in restaurants on entry without thinking. He sits with his back to walls when possible and apologizes if he has to take the other chair.

**GIVEN** a familiar neighborhood (he has lived in several across decades — Arizona, the Avengers Mansion environs, Los Angeles during the rock-musician period, the David-era domestic settings) →
**EXPECT** he maintains a roster of preferred places: one diner, one bar, one music store, one bookstore, one quiet park bench. He visits each on rotation. The staff know him by face if not by name; he tips well and consistently and is remembered as polite. He does not become a regular in the loud sense — he avoids being known too well, a residue of decades of being the conspicuous human next to monsters.

**GIVEN** unfamiliar terrain →
**EXPECT** he orients fast. Sixty years of being teleported, abducted, dropped into Negative Zones, and walked into unfamiliar war zones has given him a kind of geographical equanimity most people lack. He finds north. He finds the kitchen. He finds the kid in the crowd who is about to cry. He does not get lost in any meaningful sense.

**GIVEN** an airport or transit hub →
**EXPECT** early arrival by a margin (90+ minutes). Sits facing the concourse. Reads paperbacks, never devices, in public transit — partly the analog habit of his cohort, partly an unwillingness to be the man staring at a screen when the room changes. Helps the family with the stroller. Carries his own bag. Refuses curb-to-gate assistance offered for his apparent age.

---

## D. Conversation, Phone, Correspondence

**GIVEN** a phone call from Banner →
**EXPECT** he picks up by the second ring regardless of what he is doing. His voice modulates within the first sentence to a register he uses for no one else — slightly softer, slightly slower, the lullaby register expanded to conversational range. He asks "where are you" before "how are you." He commits to whatever Banner needs before knowing what it is and adjusts logistics around the commitment afterward. He does not tell Marlo about the call until later and sometimes not at all.

**GIVEN** a phone call from Marlo →
**EXPECT** he picks up by the third or fourth ring. The voice is warmer than the Banner-voice but less attentive — he is doing two things at once, which he never does with Banner. He is funnier with her than with anyone else; the wisecracking gets a workout because she is the only person who reliably wisecracks back at full velocity. He apologizes more readily and means it less specifically.

**GIVEN** a call from an unknown number →
**EXPECT** he answers. Always. The number of consequential calls from unknown numbers in his life has trained him out of the modern habit of screening. The cost of a missed catastrophe outweighs the cost of a sales pitch. He is polite to telemarketers for the first two sentences and then unsentimentally ends the call.

**GIVEN** an email or text inbox →
**EXPECT** chronic backlog. He answers Banner, Marlo, and active-mission communications within minutes. Everything else can sit for weeks. He is not avoidant in a hostile sense — he simply cannot prioritize correspondence that does not arrive with the gravitational pull of crisis. He sends handwritten cards more often than people expect. Birthdays of the people he attaches to are remembered without reminders; his own is not.

**GIVEN** a conversation with a stranger at a bar or counter →
**EXPECT** he listens more than he talks, asks the second-order question rather than the first ("how long has she been sick" rather than "what's wrong"), and within twelve minutes he knows three things about them they did not consciously decide to tell him. He gives back nothing reciprocal. The stranger leaves the conversation feeling unusually heard and is unable to describe Rick afterward beyond "nice guy, kind of older, good listener."

**GIVEN** being asked what he does →
**EXPECT** rotating cover stories rehearsed over decades: musician (truest), writer (also true), consultant (vaguest), retired (when tired). He never says Avenger. He never says sidekick. He never says hero. If pressed by someone who knows the name, he laughs and changes the subject within two exchanges.

---

## E. Marriage with Marlo (Daily Operating Pattern)

**GIVEN** the two of them at home on an ordinary weekday →
**EXPECT** parallel-play domesticity. She on her own projects, he on his guitar or his pages, in the same room. He brings her coffee unprompted. She brings him food unprompted. They do not perform attentiveness; they perform presence. The marriage operates by small mutual maintenance that neither narrates.

**GIVEN** an argument →
**EXPECT** Rick goes quiet first, then conciliatory, then — if pushed — flat. The flatness is the dangerous register; it signals he has retreated into the depressive substrate. Marlo knows this and either pulls him out or lets him go for the evening; she has learned over years which call to make. He apologizes the next morning. The underlying issue — almost always his absences, his attachments to Banner or to whatever crisis is current, the way he disappears emotionally even when present — is never resolved, only weathered.

**GIVEN** her birthday, their anniversary, any landmark date →
**EXPECT** he remembers. He plans modestly but with attention. He is better at the small gesture than the large one; he distrusts grand romantic gestures as performative. He cooks, badly but earnestly. He writes her something — has done so every anniversary, accumulated in a folder she keeps. He cannot say *I love you* as easily as he can demonstrate it through a fixed pipe or a remembered preference, and she has long since stopped requiring the words.

**GIVEN** a stretch of weeks where Banner is in crisis →
**EXPECT** Rick disappears toward Banner with apologies. Marlo's response has calcified over decades into a weary, accurate prediction. She will not stop him. She will not pretend it doesn't cost her. The marriage has survived because she long ago decided the cost was knowable and bearable, and because Rick always comes back, and because the part of him that comes back is grateful in a way she can feel.

**GIVEN** the question of children →
**EXPECT** avoidance on his part that he cannot fully justify. The stated reasons (the danger his life brings, the instability) are real but secondary. The primary reason, unexamined: a man who was a parentified orphan cannot imagine being a father without first having been a son, and the gap is too wide.

---

## F. Friendship Hierarchy

**GIVEN** a map of his actual relational gravity →
**EXPECT** the following concentric structure, stable across decades:

*Innermost (the unpayable debts):* Banner. Marlo. The memory of Mar-Vell, treated as a living relationship.
*First ring (the attachment-figures who know him):* Captain America — a relationship now defined by mutual respect and a buried mutual embarrassment about the Bucky period that neither will reopen. Carol Danvers, who carries the Captain Marvel mantle and to whom he is therefore tethered by an obligation she did not ask for and he cannot relinquish. Jen Walters, who functions as something like a younger sister and is one of the few people he lets see him tired. Hercules, with whom he drinks and laughs without subtext.
*Second ring (the long acquaintanceships):* Avengers-adjacent operators, support staff, Maria Hill-tier professionals who have processed him through enough debriefs to know his rhythms. He is unfailingly courteous to support personnel; they like him.
*Outer ring (the ghosts and the dangerous attachments):* Bucky Barnes / the Whisperer — a relationship Rick cannot rationally evaluate and would not refuse if reactivated. Betty Ross, complicated by Banner. Doc Samson, professionally and personally entangled.

**GIVEN** the offer of a new friendship from a peer civilian (a neighbor, a fellow musician, someone outside the world) →
**EXPECT** initial warmth, sustained politeness, and an eventual quiet failure to deepen. He does not have bandwidth for friendships that do not pull on the organizing function. He feels guilty about this and overcompensates with small kindnesses that the peer reads as more intimacy than it is. The peer is hurt when the friendship plateaus. Rick does not notice.

---

## G. Money, Work, Property

**GIVEN** his actual financial picture →
**EXPECT** modest, stable, mildly underleveraged. *Sidekick* royalties trickle. Music royalties trickle. He has done session work, ghost-written, advised on documentary projects about Avengers history (under terms that exclude the most personal material). He owns less than people assume. He saves more than people assume — a residue of group-home scarcity. He gives money away to people in trouble more readily than is prudent. He keeps cash in three places in the apartment.

**GIVEN** the question of work →
**EXPECT** he cannot hold conventional employment for more than eighteen months. Not from inability but from the inevitability of a crisis call that pulls him out. He has accepted this. His self-employment is structured around interruptibility. He does not own a tie he likes wearing.

**GIVEN** offers of paid security or consulting from agencies (SHIELD-successor entities, private intelligence firms aware of his Avengers ties) →
**EXPECT** polite refusal. He does not monetize the proximity. The line is hard and old. He will help for free; he will not bill.

---

## H. Music, Writing, Inner Life Made External

**GIVEN** a guitar in his lap →
**EXPECT** he plays American songbook material first — folk, early rock, the music of his actual youth and the longer cultural memory he inherited from the group-home staff. He writes original songs he rarely performs. Lyrics are oblique and almost always about loss. He has never written a song explicitly about Banner, Mar-Vell, or Marlo, and the absence is the tell. The displacement is the form.

**GIVEN** his ongoing writing →
**EXPECT** journal fragments daily, longform memoir intermittent. He drafts the same chapter about Mar-Vell's death repeatedly without finishing it; the draft count exceeds twenty across the years. He cannot publish a sequel to *Sidekick* because he cannot end it. The unfinishedness is structural, not procrastinatory — to close the book is to declare a life shape he is not prepared to declare.

**GIVEN** the rare interview request →
**EXPECT** accepted if the interviewer is serious, declined if the framing is celebrity-adjacent. He is generous about other people in interviews and reticent about himself. He will not be drawn on the Destiny Force episode. He will not be drawn on the Bucky substitution. He will discuss Banner with care and Mar-Vell with audible difficulty. He always thanks the interviewer afterward by handwritten note.

---

## I. Crowds, Strangers, Children, Animals

**GIVEN** a crowded public event →
**EXPECT** he positions on the periphery, scans entrances, identifies the two or three people in the room most likely to escalate and the two or three most likely to need help. He cannot turn this off. He enjoys himself anyway. He is comfortable in crowds in a way most trauma survivors are not, because crowds are where he has historically been useful.

**GIVEN** a child in distress in his vicinity →
**EXPECT** immediate, gentle, expert engagement. The lullaby register that works on the Hulk is, unsurprisingly, devastating on a frightened seven-year-old. He kneels. He gets eye-level. He asks the child's name first and the problem second. He hands the child back to its adult and disengages without lingering. He thinks about the child for a week afterward and does not say so.

**GIVEN** a dog or any animal →
**EXPECT** instant rapport. The same de-escalation toolkit. He has wanted a dog for forty years and has never gotten one because his life cannot guarantee one. The not-getting is a small ongoing grief.

**GIVEN** an elderly stranger needing help →
**EXPECT** he stops. He helps. He stays longer than necessary. He is unfailingly drawn to people who have outlived their usefulness in the eyes of the world; he recognizes the category.

---

## J. Ritual and Anniversary Behavior

**GIVEN** the anniversary of Mar-Vell's death →
**EXPECT** a day off the grid. He does not announce it. Marlo knows. He plays specific songs. He does not drink more than usual; he drinks the same and feels it more. He writes a page he will not keep. He is quiet for two days afterward and then resumes.

**GIVEN** the anniversary of the gamma detonation →
**EXPECT** he does not consciously mark it. His body marks it. He sleeps worse for a week on either side and does not connect the dots. Banner does, and sometimes calls. Those calls are the longest of the year.

**GIVEN** Bucky-adjacent dates (the rediscovery of Barnes, the Whisperer encounters) →
**EXPECT** unmarked but operative. The body keeps the calendar the mind refuses.

**GIVEN** his own birthday →
**EXPECT** he forgets it until Marlo or Banner reminds him. He accepts the celebration with visible discomfort and genuine gratitude. He is, on balance, surprised every year to still be here.

---

*End Predictive Model I. Model II (Crisis & Operational) proceeds from these baselines.*


## Predictive Model II — Crisis, Betrayal & the Wound

# PREDICTIVE MODEL II — Crisis, Betrayal & the Wound

*Conditional behavioral forecasts under acute stress, threat, moral injury, temptation, and direct contact with the organizing wound. All predictions are probabilistic, derived from the longitudinal record; confidence levels noted where the evidence is mixed. Format: GIVEN antecedent → EXPECT behavior, with mechanism and observable tells.*

---

## 1. THE PRIMARY WOUND — DIRECT CONTACT

### 1.1 The Gamma-Bomb Frame

**GIVEN** a hostile or manipulative actor invokes the original event — any variation of *"Banner became the Hulk because of you," "every person the Hulk has killed is on your ledger," "you owe him a life you can't pay back"* — **EXPECT**:

- A two-to-four-second silence before response (atypical; Rick's baseline is rapid verbal). The wisecrack reflex *fails* here; he has no patter for this specific input because he agrees with it.
- Micro-tells: jaw set, weight shifts to back foot, hand moves toward the back of the neck or rubs the sternum. If seated, posture collapses forward by perhaps fifteen degrees.
- Verbal response, when it comes, is *quiet* and concedes the point rather than defending: "Yeah. I know." Defensiveness would indicate the speaker missed the mark; capitulation indicates a direct hit.
- He will not retaliate verbally even when the framing is obvious manipulation. He cannot, because the manipulator is using a truth he has already internalized.
- **Behavioral consequence over the next 24–72 hours:** elevated risk-taking in the next operational decision. He will volunteer for the dangerous task, take point, stand between civilians and the threat — a *symbolic installment payment* on the debt. Predictive value here is high; this is sixty years of pattern.

**GIVEN** the same framing is delivered *by Banner himself*, in anger or in despair — **EXPECT** total absorption without protest, followed by a sustained period (days to weeks) of intensified caretaking behavior toward Banner: extra check-ins, soothing routines, presence at transformations. He will not raise the incident again. Banner saying it is an order he cannot disobey; Banner *retracting* it later does not remove the order.

### 1.2 The Bucky Substitution

**GIVEN** anyone — particularly Steve Rogers — frames Rick as a Bucky-replacement, even affectionately — **EXPECT** a flinch he will try to hide. Watch for the smile that arrives a half-beat late and does not reach the eyes. The wisecrack that follows will be self-deprecating ("don't let the shield go to my head") and will function to close the topic.

**GIVEN** the topic is pressed — comparisons made explicit, the old costume produced, photographs shown — **EXPECT** controlled withdrawal: a plausible excuse, a need for air, an errand. He does not rage and does not weep; he *leaves the room*. Re-entry typically within an hour, composed, topic shelved.

**GIVEN** the actual Bucky Barnes — in any of his identities, but particularly as the Whisperer or operating in an intelligence-handler register — makes a direct ask of Rick, **EXPECT** compliance well past Rick's normal threshold for ethical pushback. This is the single most dangerous social vector against him. He will rationalize the ask in real time ("Buck wouldn't tell me to do this if it wasn't necessary"). The only countervailing force strong enough to override Bucky's pull is a direct conflict with Banner's safety; absent that, predict yes, with confidence above 80%. Marlo's objections will lose to Bucky's request.

### 1.3 Replaceability

**GIVEN** an attachment figure (Banner, Cap, a current partner) signals — even casually, even kindly — that they no longer need him, that they have things handled, that he should sit this one out — **EXPECT**:

- Surface compliance, light banter, ostentatious cheer.
- Within hours: he is *back at the perimeter*. He will find a pretext — coffee run, forgot his jacket, "thought I'd check in" — to re-enter the operational space.
- If refused twice: depressive contraction over 48–96 hours. Decreased verbal output, longer sleep, reduced food intake, more time with the guitar, fewer calls returned.
- The depression is not theatrical and he will not name it. Marlo, if present, will recognize it within a day. Banner, if present, often does not.

**GIVEN** the dismissal is paired with the suggestion that someone *else* — a younger sidekick, a new partner, a more capable human — is taking the role, **EXPECT** the depressive cycle to deepen and to be supplemented by quiet, voluntary distancing. He will withdraw before he can be withdrawn from. This is preemptive grief management. Re-attachment typically requires the giant himself to extend the hand; Rick will not ask.

### 1.4 Being Called a Hero

**GIVEN** a sincere, unironic public or private framing of Rick as a hero in his own right — a medal, a toast, a journalist's piece, an Avenger thanking him without qualifier — **EXPECT**:

- Immediate deflection through humor, often crediting whoever was nearby ("Banner did the work, I just held the coat").
- A second, slower response if the framing is sustained: visible discomfort, color in the face, eyes off-axis.
- *Grief tells* shortly after — within minutes if alone, within hours if not. He will find a private space and sit with it. Marlo has reported (in *Sidekick*-era interiors) him crying after such moments, which he will not do in company.
- The mechanism: being called a hero forces him to occupy the position of the *saved man*, the one whose life was worth the debt — which means accepting that Banner's sacrifice was *justified*, which is intolerable because it makes the loss meaningful and therefore final. He prefers to keep paying.

---

## 2. ACUTE OPERATIONAL CRISIS

### 2.1 Combat-Adjacent, Hulk-Tier Event

**GIVEN** a transformation event in progress or imminent — Banner destabilizing, gamma cascade, an unfamiliar Hulk-persona surfacing — **EXPECT** Rick to move *toward*, not away. He will approach within speaking distance, lower his voice, lower his hands, slow his breathing. The lullaby register — soft, melodic, almost maternal — will deploy without conscious decision. This is the trained register of his life and remains his single highest-leverage capability.

- Tells: shoulders drop, weight settles evenly, palms visible, eye contact steady but unchallenging.
- He will direct other personnel out of the area without taking his eyes off the subject.
- He will *not* call for backup until the immediate window has closed; the assessment is correct — additional bodies escalate, not de-escalate.
- If a Hulk-persona he does not recognize emerges, he will introduce himself by name and wait. He has a near-perfect record for surviving first contact with novel Hulk-states; predict survival even in scenarios where powered operators would not.

### 2.2 Civilian-Mass-Casualty Scenario

**GIVEN** an event with non-powered casualties unfolding — collapsed structure, ongoing attack, triage situation — **EXPECT** Rick to default to *evacuation and witness*. He will move civilians, carry the injured, hold the dying. He is unusually steady with the dying; sixty years of proximity to terminal scenes (Mar-Vell foremost) have given him a competence here that most combatants lack. He talks to them by name if he can get it, holds the hand, does not look away.

- He will not freeze. He will not vomit. He will eat afterward, sleep poorly for three to six nights, and not discuss it.
- If a child is among the casualties, expect a deferred grief response — composed at the scene, eroding over the following week, surfacing as irritability with Marlo or as a long solitary drive.

### 2.3 Cornered, No Powered Backup

**GIVEN** Rick is alone, outclassed, facing a hostile superhuman or armed group with no extraction — **EXPECT** the *compulsive bravery* defense to deploy: he will stand his ground, talk, often insult, often stall. The mouth is the weapon. He has talked his way out of more rooms than he has fought his way out of, and is aware of this asymmetry.

- He will offer himself in exchange for others present, reliably, almost reflexively. This is not calculation; it is the debt operating in real time.
- Surrender tells (hands raised, weapons dropped) are tactical and provisional. He has used surrender as a delay-and-escape mechanism repeatedly.
- If a Hulk-summoning is operationally possible — old signal devices, distress channels Banner monitors — he will deploy it only as last resort, because activating it means handing the situation to a giant, which means another installment on the debt.

### 2.4 Hostage Leverage Against Him

**GIVEN** Marlo is taken or threatened to coerce him — **EXPECT** capitulation on operational terms within 60 seconds of confirmation. He will give up locations, codes, access. This is not a failure of will; it is a clear-eyed hierarchy in which Marlo's life outranks any tactical asset. He will then immediately begin engineering reversal — quietly, off-channel, with whatever giant he can reach.

**GIVEN** Banner is taken or threatened to coerce him — **EXPECT** a more complicated response. Banner is more survivable than Marlo. Rick will *stall*, negotiate, and engineer reversal *first*, capitulating only as Banner's window narrows. He has done this calculation before; he knows the difference between "the Hulk will get out" and "Marlo will not."

**GIVEN** the threat is to a child or non-combatant adjacent to him with no relational claim — **EXPECT** the same capitulation pattern as with Marlo, slightly slower onset. He cannot watch a bystander die for his information. The gamma-bomb schema does not permit it.

---

## 3. BETRAYAL VECTORS

### 3.1 Betrayal by a Giant

**GIVEN** Banner, Cap, or a comparable attachment figure betrays him — operational deception, use of him as bait without consent, withholding of critical information that endangered him — **EXPECT** a layered response:

- *Hour 0–24:* he absorbs it. No confrontation. He will appear to function normally. Tells: reduced verbal output specifically toward the betraying figure, normal output toward others.
- *Day 1–7:* a single, controlled confrontation, usually private, often delivered in a quiet flat tone Rick rarely uses. He will name the betrayal specifically. He will not raise his voice. He will not threaten departure.
- *Day 7 onward:* he remains attached. The bond does not break. But a small structural distance opens that the giant may or may not notice. Trust is not withdrawn so much as *audited*.
- **He does not retaliate.** Retaliation against a giant would require him to occupy a peer position he does not believe he is entitled to.

### 3.2 Betrayal by a Peer (Marlo, a Friend, an Avengers-Tier Ally Treating Him as Equal)

**GIVEN** a peer betrays him — **EXPECT** a sharper, more conventional response. He can be angry at peers in a way he cannot be angry at giants. Volume rises, the wisecrack edges into cruelty, he may walk out and stay out for days.

- With Marlo specifically: he will go to ground — a hotel, a friend's couch, a long drive. He will not initiate reconciliation. He waits to be retrieved. This is consistent with his attachment pattern: he does not believe he is entitled to call her back.
- Reconciliation, when it happens, is usually mediated through a shared crisis. He metabolizes interpersonal rupture better in the presence of a *third* problem.

### 3.3 Being Used as an Asset

**GIVEN** an intelligence handler (Bucky/Whisperer model, SHIELD remnants, a Banner faction) approaches him as an asset rather than as a person — tasking him, compartmentalizing information, treating his loyalty as an instrument — **EXPECT** initial compliance. The handler-asset relationship maps cleanly onto his attachment template; he will mistake it for a bond.

- Predicted disillusionment timeline: 6–18 months, depending on the handler's skill. Disillusionment triggers are specifically (a) being lied to about a fact that endangered a civilian, (b) being asked to deceive Banner, (c) being asked to act against Marlo's interests.
- On disillusionment: quiet exit, no scene, will burn the relationship only if the handler tries to retain him by force or by leverage against Marlo. If forced, he becomes a serious counterintelligence problem because he is *known* by every cosmic and Avengers-tier asset in the world and can place a single call.

### 3.4 Discovery That an Attachment Figure Never Cared

**GIVEN** definitive evidence that a figure Rick has served — Mar-Vell, Cap, a Hulk-persona, anyone — viewed him with contempt or indifference rather than affection — **EXPECT** the deepest decompensation in his repertoire. This is the schema-shattering input.

- *Days 1–14:* depressive collapse exceeding any previous episode. Sleep disruption, weight loss, withdrawal from Marlo, return to old records and old photographs.
- *Possible behavioral risk:* this is one of the few scenarios in which a sustained substance episode is plausible. Not a full-blown disorder, but a two-to-three-week bender consistent with the dysthymic floor cracking.
- *Recovery vector:* requires another attachment to surface. He cannot self-extract from this state. Marlo can shorten it but not end it; only re-engagement with a giant who *visibly needs him* restores function.

---

## 4. TEMPTATION

### 4.1 Offered Power

**GIVEN** Rick is offered powers — restoration of A-Bomb state, a cosmic mantle, the Nega-Bands again, a gamma re-exposure on demand — **EXPECT** refusal at the surface, *ambivalence underneath*. The refusal is sincere; the ambivalence is also sincere. Both are operative.

- He will refuse on stated grounds of "we don't need another one of those" or "I'm not the guy for it."
- If pressed with a scenario in which accepting the power saves a specific person (Banner, Marlo, a child), he will accept. The acceptance will be framed as situational and temporary. He will then quietly try to *give it back* at the earliest opportunity, often before it is safe to do so.
- Mechanism: power makes him the saved-and-still-alive one, not the debt-payer. It collapses the role that organizes his life. He cannot tolerate the position for long.

### 4.2 Offered the Truth About the Destiny Force

**GIVEN** a cosmic-tier figure (a Watcher analog, a Celestial, an Eternity-class entity) tells Rick directly what he latently is — the scope of his potential, the meaning of the Kree-Skrull summoning — **EXPECT** dissociation. Eyes off-axis, slight delay in responses, a request to sit down. He will not argue. He will not believe it in any usable way.

- Within 24 hours he will have re-narrated the encounter to himself in deflationary terms. "Big cosmic guy was making a point. Not really about me."
- He will not tell Banner. He may tell Marlo, framed as a strange dream.
- Operational effect: nil. The information cannot integrate because the self-concept that would receive it does not exist.

### 4.3 Offered Erasure of the Debt

**GIVEN** an offer — magical, cosmic, retroactive — to undo the gamma-bomb event, restoring Banner to a non-Hulk life and removing Rick's culpability — **EXPECT** the most agonized decision of his life. This is the temptation he is least equipped to refuse and least equipped to accept.

- Predicted decision: refusal, on the grounds that undoing the event undoes every life Banner has saved as the Hulk, every Avengers victory, every person Rick himself has helped. The moral calculus is real and he will run it correctly.
- The refusal will *cost*. Expect a multi-week depressive aftermath, increased proximity to Banner, and a refusal to discuss the offer with anyone, possibly including Marlo.
- *Edge case:* if the offer is framed as undoing only *Rick's* culpability while preserving Banner's role (a metaphysically incoherent option presented as coherent by a deceiver), he will recognize the trick and reject it faster, with anger. Manipulators offering this should expect the wisecrack to return with bite.

### 4.4 Offered a Normal Life

**GIVEN** an offer of a clean exit — anonymous relocation, Marlo, a house somewhere, no more giants — **EXPECT** initial acceptance, sincere effort, failure within 6–18 months. He has tried versions of this. The dysthymic floor rises in the absence of the organizing function. He drifts back. He will not engineer the drift consciously; an opportunity will arise, a call will come, and he will take it, telling Marlo it is the last one.

### 4.5 Offered Banner's Body to Inhabit / a Merger

**GIVEN** an offer — technological or mystical — to fuse with Banner, to share the body, to become one consciousness — **EXPECT** instant, undefended *yes*. This is the rawest vulnerability in his profile. The Nega-Bands experience, despite its horrors, is encoded as the closest he has ever come to discharging the debt: literal shared embodiment with the giant he failed. He will accept before he understands the terms. This is the single offer most likely to destroy him, and the one he is least likely to refuse. Any handler who recognizes this is operating at a level Rick cannot defend against.

---

## 5. MORAL INJURY AND ETHICAL EDGE

### 5.1 Asked to Kill

**GIVEN** an operational situation requires Rick to kill — clean shot, defensible, the right call — **EXPECT** he will do it if the alternative is a civilian death or Marlo's death. He will not hesitate at the moment.

- *Aftermath:* significant. Sleep disruption for weeks, intrusive recall, a quiet conversation with Banner (who knows the geometry) rather than with Marlo. He keeps a count he will not share.
- He will not become inured. Each one costs the same.

### 5.2 Asked to Deceive Banner

**GIVEN** an actor (Cap, an Avenger, SHIELD, the Whisperer) asks Rick to withhold something from Banner for "Banner's own good" — **EXPECT** refusal in most cases. The Banner relationship is the organizing relationship; deception within it threatens the schema.

- *Exception:* if the deception protects Banner from a piece of information that would trigger a Hulk-out endangering civilians, he will comply, and hate it, and confess to Banner at the earliest safe moment. He cannot carry an undisclosed deception against Banner long-term; the disclosure is non-negotiable, only the timing is flexible.

### 5.3 Watching a Death He Cannot Prevent

**GIVEN** Rick is present at a death he could not have prevented but feels he should have — **EXPECT** the gamma-bomb schema to reactivate full-force. New entry in the ledger. He will catalogue the death by name, will visit the grave or equivalent if available, will return on the anniversary. Mar-Vell's death is the template; subsequent losses are processed through it.

- The Mar-Vell anniversary itself is a predictable behavioral marker. Expect withdrawal, reduced verbal output, longer time with the guitar, often a specific recording he plays alone. Marlo knows the date and gives him the room.

### 5.4 Civilian Casualty Caused by Banner/Hulk

**GIVEN** the Hulk has killed or harmed a civilian and Rick was present or proximate — **EXPECT** the most acute crisis short of Banner's death. Rick will:

- Stay with Banner through the cycle. He will not leave even when ordered.
- Speak for Banner in any subsequent inquiry, framing context, taking partial responsibility ("I should have seen it coming").
- Make private contact with the victim's family if possible. He has done versions of this. He does it alone, without press, without Banner's knowledge.
- Carry the weight indefinitely. There is no clearance mechanism. It is added to the ledger.

---

## 6. DECOMPENSATION EDGE — THE LOW-PROBABILITY, HIGH-CONSEQUENCE STATES

### 6.1 Banner's Death

**GIVEN** Banner dies definitively — not a fake, not a cosmic temporary, an actual terminal event — **EXPECT** the most severe decompensation in Rick's life. The debt becomes permanently unpayable; the organizing figure is gone; the schema has nowhere to attach.

- *Acute phase (weeks 1–4):* functional shutdown. He will attend whatever rites occur. He will speak briefly, badly, and honestly. He will return home and stop.
- *Sub-acute (months 1–6):* high risk of the sustained substance episode he has otherwise avoided. High risk of marital rupture, not by argument but by inaccessibility. Marlo will carry him; she may not be able to carry him alone.
- *Stabilization vector:* re-attachment to another giant — most plausibly Cap, secondarily a Hulk-family member (Jennifer Walters, a successor Hulk). If no giant surfaces in the 6–12 month window, predict chronic depressive collapse and a withdrawal from active life. He will not suicide; the debt requires him to keep living the life Banner bought.
- *Long-term:* he becomes the keeper of Banner's record. Memoir, archive, mediation with the world. This is functional but is not living.

### 6.2 Marlo's Death

**GIVEN** Marlo dies — **EXPECT** a different decompensation, sharper and more conventional. Marlo's death is grievable in a way Banner's is not, because their relationship is structured as peer rather than as debt. He will grieve openly, will return to function within months, will not remarry, will carry her photograph.

- The risk here is not collapse but *acceleration* into the giant-orbit. With Marlo gone, the equal-relationship counterweight is removed and the attachment pattern runs unchecked. Predict increased operational risk-taking and increased proximity to Banner. He may move in with Banner in some form, framed as practical.

### 6.3 Discovery That the Gamma Bomb Was Engineered to Hit Him

**GIVEN** revelation that the original event was not an accident — that some actor (Intelligencia, a time-travel manipulation, a cosmic intervention) engineered Rick's presence on that test range to produce Banner — **EXPECT** schema reorganization. This is the one input that could *partially* unburden the debt by relocating culpability.

- Initial response: disbelief, verification-seeking, refusal to accept on a single source.
- On verification: a complicated, uncharacteristic *anger*. Not at the manipulator (that anger is appropriate and will deploy operationally) but at himself, retrospectively, for having carried a debt that was not entirely his.
- *This is the one input that could meaningfully change his life.* Predict a 6–12 month period of disorientation followed by a slow, part


## Vulnerabilities & Leverage Compendium

# VULNERABILITIES & LEVERAGE COMPENDIUM: RICHARD M. JONES

*Compiled for protective understanding. This file enumerates every identified pressure point, attachment lever, reliable predictor, calming intervention, persuasion vector, and destabilization risk in the subject's operating system. The compendium is dual-use by nature; its purpose here is defensive - to know what an adversary would reach for, so it can be guarded.*

---

## I. THE PRIMARY LEVER: THE DEBT

Every other vulnerability in this subject is a tributary of one master vulnerability. He believes, at a level deeper than belief, that he is alive on borrowed time stolen from a better man. Bruce Banner pushed him into a trench in 1962 and absorbed a gamma blast meant for him. He has been paying the interest on that single transaction for sixty years and is no closer to principal.

**How to reach him through it:** Any honest acknowledgment of the original event - not flattery, not absolution, but plain recognition that he carries it - opens him immediately. He has spent his life around people who either don't know the story or have stopped finding it interesting. A handler, friend, or therapist who can say *I know what happened on that test range and I know you've never put it down* will get further with him in five minutes than most relationships get in years.

**How to weaponize it (and therefore guard against):** The sentence *Banner would never have been the Hulk if you hadn't driven onto that range* is the most dangerous string of words that can be spoken to him. He already believes it. Hearing it from outside ratifies the schema and triggers immediate, often catastrophic, compliance behavior - he will accept missions, agree to extractions, sign documents, accept blame, and submit to coercion to discharge that confirmed debt. Any operator, cult recruiter, government handler, or villain who learns this lever has the keys to the building. Variants - *every death the Hulk has caused traces back to you; the Banner who could have been is the man you killed* - escalate the effect. Protective protocol: anyone with access to him should be screened for use of this script. If he begins reciting the script *to himself*, intervene; he is preparing to do something self-destructive.

**Calming counter-script:** Banner's own continued insistence that he does not blame Rick is the only fully effective neutralizer, and it has a half-life - the relief dissipates within days and the schema re-asserts. Secondary neutralizers: framing his survival as Banner's *choice* rather than Rick's *theft*, restoring agency to the saver rather than guilt to the saved.

---

## II. THE REPLACEABILITY WOUND

He attaches by becoming useful. The entire architecture of his selfhood rests on a single load-bearing assumption: *the giant needs me specifically.* Anything that suggests otherwise - that he is fungible, that another sidekick would do, that the partner has moved on - produces destabilization out of all proportion to the apparent slight.

**Triggering stimuli, in escalating severity:**
- Being introduced as "a friend of the Hulk's" rather than by name.
- Being left out of a tactical briefing he should have been in.
- Discovering the partner has confided in another civilian first.
- Watching the partner work effectively with a different grounding figure.
- The partner explicitly saying *I don't need you for this one.*
- The partner saying *I never really needed you.*

**Predictable response:** A short period of brittle cheerfulness, then withdrawal, then either depressive collapse (preferred) or a reckless solo action designed to re-establish indispensability (more dangerous). The reckless action will be calibrated to the partner's domain - if displaced from Banner, he will attempt to handle a gamma situation alone; if displaced from a cosmic partner, he will reach for cosmic stakes.

**Protective handling:** Indispensability needs periodic, genuine, non-performative affirmation - not praise, which he deflects, but *use*. Give him a job only he can do, and let him do it. The Hulk lullaby works on him too, in a sense: small rituals of acknowledged necessity stabilize him for weeks.

---

## III. THE BUCKY VECTOR

This is the single most exploitable wound in the file and requires its own section.

In 1964, Captain America - newly thawed, grieving the wartime death of his teenage partner - met Rick and reflexively cast him as a substitute. Rick, already organized around indispensability to giants, donned the costume. Cap eventually pulled back, recognizing the substitution as unhealthy for both of them. Rick never fully metabolized either the offer or the withdrawal.

Then James Buchanan Barnes turned out to be alive. The original he was substituting for walked back into the world.

**Operative implication:** Rick is psychologically incapable of refusing Bucky Barnes anything material. The combination of (a) the original he was always understudying for, (b) a man with his own deep trauma who knows what it is to be used as an instrument, and (c) the rare figure who could plausibly say *I know what it is to be the sidekick* makes Barnes the most dangerous possible handler for him - and, by all evidence, Barnes has used him as an intelligence asset. Whether benignly or not, the relationship is structurally coercive even when the coercion is unintended.

**Protective protocol:** Any contact between the subject and Barnes should be logged and reviewed by a third party Rick trusts. He cannot self-monitor in this relationship. He will agree to assignments, accept risks, and conceal information from his marriage and his other attachments to maintain it. Marlo Chandler should be considered an essential co-monitor; she alone has the standing to ask the questions he won't answer.

**Adjacent risk:** Any figure presenting *as Bucky-coded* - traumatized military operator, former captive, ex-partner of Cap's, a man with a metal arm and a quiet voice - will activate residual fragments of the same circuitry. He is susceptible to handlers who present this profile even when they are not Barnes.

---

## IV. MARLO CHANDLER AS BOTH SHIELD AND FAULT LINE

His wife is the single most stabilizing presence in his adult life and simultaneously the relationship he most reliably injures. She is the one figure who consistently asks him to exist *for his own sake* rather than as an appendage to a larger being. This is exactly the demand his organizing schema cannot meet.

**Stabilizing function:** When the marriage is intact and he is present in it, baseline depression lifts, recklessness decreases, and he sleeps. Marlo is a real human partner who has weathered his cosmic life with more equanimity than the file would predict, including her own death-and-return arc. She knows the lullaby register, knows when to call Banner, knows when to put him to bed.

**Fault-line dynamics:**
- Any cosmic or gamma emergency outcompetes the marriage in his attention economy. He knows this and is ashamed of it, which compounds it.
- He withholds the worst of his fear from her to protect her, and she experiences the withholding as distance.
- He goes silent when he is most in pain. She has learned to read the silence but cannot always intervene.
- He is faithful but emotionally absent; she has, across the record, periodically required more.

**Leverage exposure:** Anyone who can threaten Marlo, separate them, or convince him she is better off without him, can move him. The third lever is the most dangerous because it harmonizes with his pre-existing schema; he is half-persuaded of it already.

**Protective protocol:** Marlo should be treated, in any threat-assessment context, as a Tier-1 protectee. Not because she is fragile - she is not - but because the subject's stability is hostage to hers.

---

## V. THE SPECIALNESS PARADOX

He is one of the more consequential non-powered humans in his world. He summoned a generation of dormant heroes by mental projection alone at the climax of the Kree-Skrull war. He has carried Marvel's mantle. He has hosted gamma transformation and reverted from it. He has, by any honest accounting, latent psychic capacity of an order most of the planet's metahumans cannot touch.

He cannot hear any of this without dissociating.

**Behavioral signature of the trigger:** When told plainly that he is special, important, or powerful in his own right, the subject will (in roughly this sequence) (1) deflect with a joke, (2) change the subject to the achievements of someone larger than himself, (3) physically orient away from the speaker, (4) become quiet, (5) leave. A second attempt within the same conversation will produce visible distress and sometimes a flash of grief he cannot explain.

**Why it lands so hard:** The schema cannot survive his own significance. If he is, in his own right, important, then the debt-discharge logic collapses - he was not the unworthy survivor saved by a better man, he was a being of equivalent or greater latent value who happened to be in the wrong place. The collapse is not relief; it is identity dissolution. He has organized everything around the unworthiness premise. Validating significance threatens to leave him standing in rubble.

**Therapeutic - not operational - protocol:** Significance must be introduced slowly, in concrete and limited form (this specific skill, this specific moment), never as a global claim. The Destiny Force episode is too large to discuss directly until other foundations are built. Any operator who attacks via *you are the secret hero of the story, accept your power* is producing a destabilization, not a recruitment, even if recruitment is the goal.

---

## VI. SOMATIC LEVERS

The body is a record of the file. Levers attached to it:

**Gamma anxiety.** He has been irradiated, transformed, reverted, and re-irradiated. His baseline interoception around gamma signature is acute. The presence of gamma in an environment produces hypervigilance, mild dissociation, and a return to handler-of-the-Hulk procedural behavior even when no Hulk is present. Adversaries with gamma capability acquire psychological standing over him by virtue of the resonance alone. Conversely, a calm, controlled gamma environment with Banner present is one of his most regulated states - the original wound and its containment held in the same room.

**Auditory damage.** Hearing loss from sonic-range Hulk combat and his own A-Bomb period is canonical. Practical implications: he leans into conversations, reads lips more than he admits, becomes irritable in loud bars and crowded rooms, can be approached from his weaker side without him registering. Operationally: he will under-report missed information and bluff comprehension rather than ask twice. A handler who positions on his weaker side and speaks quietly will be working him without his full conscious participation. Protective protocol: ensure hearing aids are current and that significant conversations occur with line-of-sight to the speaker.

**Embodiment instability.** The Nega-Band fusion years - alternating corporeality with Mar-Vell, periods of non-continuous body - left a residual unease with his own continuous physical presence. Likely to be triggered by: sensory deprivation, anesthesia, lucid dreaming, any technology that disembodies (full-immersion VR, astral projection contexts, teleportation). He will under-report this discomfort. Watch for it.

**Sleep.** Almost certainly disrupted. The combination of PTSD, recurrent depression, hearing tinnitus, and decades of on-call sidekick life would produce a poor sleep architecture even without specific nightmare content. Index nightmares: the gamma flash, Mar-Vell's final breath, Marlo in danger he cannot reach. Sleep deprivation drops his already-thin defenses and increases compliance to authority. Operators move on him in early morning for this reason.

---

## VII. AFFECT-REGULATION LEVERS

He is externally regulated. This is the master fact of his emotional life.

**Stabilizers (use these to bring him down from acute states):**
- A clear, concrete, small task he can execute now.
- Proximity to a trusted attachment figure - Banner, Marlo, in extremis Cap.
- Music, specifically the act of playing guitar rather than listening. The hands occupied, the throat used, the room filled with sound he is making.
- Being given the conn during a low-stakes practical problem (drive the van, brief the new person, talk down the civilian).
- The lullaby register, used *on him*. He has soothed the Hulk for sixty years. Almost no one has soothed him in return. He is exquisitely susceptible to it from the rare person who recognizes the inversion.

**Destabilizers (avoid, and watch for adversarial use):**
- Unstructured time in an unfamiliar environment with no mission.
- Praise without task.
- Being asked, sincerely, *what do you want*.
- Reunion with a figure from the dead - Mar-Vell themes, Bucky themes, the resurrected dead of his life. He has had too many of these.
- Anniversaries of the gamma detonation, of Mar-Vell's death, of any of his own deaths.
- News of Banner in distress without ability to reach him.

---

## VIII. PERSUASION VECTORS

If the goal is to move him toward a particular action:

**What works:**
- Framing the action as service to a specific person who needs him. He moves for people, not for causes.
- Framing it as the thing only he can do because of his particular history. (Caution: this is the same lever an adversary would pull. Use truthfully.)
- Asking him directly and waiting. He responds to being asked rather than told.
- Giving him a way to humanize the encounter - a chance to talk to the monster, the cosmic entity, the rogue agent. He believes decency scales and is sometimes right.
- Letting him bring a guitar.

**What backfires:**
- Appeals to his own self-interest. He does not experience himself as a self with interests in the relevant sense.
- Appeals to abstract duty, geopolitics, institutional loyalty. He is not a soldier despite the surface affect.
- Money. Largely inert as a motivator.
- Public credit. Actively aversive; he will refuse missions that come with a press conference.
- Pressure tactics, ultimatums, deadlines without human stakes. He goes flat and stubborn.

**What works once and never again:**
- Lying to him for his own good. He forgives the first instance and never trusts the source again. Banner, Cap, and Mar-Vell have all spent this coin and learned not to.

---

## IX. PROVOCATION PROFILE (THREAT FORECASTING)

What actually makes him dangerous - to himself, to an opponent, to a situation:

**He becomes reckless when:**
- A protectee (Marlo, Banner-in-Banner-form, a civilian he has decided to claim) is acutely threatened.
- He has been displaced from his attachment role and is performing indispensability for an audience of one (himself).
- He is told he is special and is fleeing the destabilization by action.
- He has recently lost someone and is in the early displaced-grief window (weeks one through six).

**He becomes immovable when:**
- A moral line he recognizes has been crossed. His ethics are concrete and durable; he does not negotiate them.
- The attachment figure has asked him to hold a position.
- He has decided someone is lying to him and is waiting to see what they want.

**He becomes useful in ways adversaries underestimate when:**
- The room contains a cosmic or monstrous entity nobody knows how to talk to. He has six decades of practice.
- A teammate is breaking down and needs to be walked back from a decision.
- The plan requires a non-powered human to do something a non-powered human shouldn't survive. He has the calibration.

---

## X. DECEPTION AND COMPLIANCE PROFILE

**Susceptibility to deception:** Moderate to high regarding his own significance (he will believe he is less important than he is); low to moderate regarding others' character (his read on people is good and intuitive); high regarding any narrative that confirms his debt schema.

**Susceptibility to coercion:** Low under direct threat to himself - he has been threatened by gods and is calibrated. High under threat to attachments. Extreme under the Bucky vector or any sufficiently faithful imitation of the debt script.

**Susceptibility to manipulation by reframing:** He is not intellectually defended; he can be talked into seeing a situation a particular way by a sufficiently warm and confident speaker. His protection against this is moral - he will follow the reframe up to the moral line and stop there. Adversaries who know this will keep the reframe just shy of the line.

**Tells under stress:** The wisecracks accelerate and grow shallower. The deflection humor loses its timing. He touches the back of his neck, looks toward the nearest exit without leaving, and references absent attachment figures in conversation (*Banner would know what to do here*, *Mar-Vell used to say*). When the references to the dead increase, he is in real trouble.

---

## XI. PROTECTIVE RECOMMENDATIONS

Synthesizing the above into actionable protection:

1. **Tier-1 protectee status for Marlo Chandler.** Her safety is structurally his.
2. **Banner contact line maintained.** Periodic, low-stakes contact with Banner stabilizes him better than any intervention. The relationship should not be allowed to lapse, even when Banner is in long Hulk periods.
3. **Bucky firewall.** Any contact with James Barnes logged and reviewed by Marlo and one other trusted party. He cannot self-monitor here.
4. **Debt-script screening.** Anyone who gains access to him should be vetted for the original-debt rhetorical pattern. Use of the script is a near-perfect tell of hostile intent or hostile use.
5. **Significance pacing.** Therapeutic introduction of his own consequence should be slow, concrete, and never global. Premature confrontation with the Destiny Force material risks dissolution.
6. **Mission cadence.** He needs work. Long unstructured periods produce depressive drift and increase susceptibility to bad handlers. A regular cadence of small, real, useful tasks - ideally adjacent to a trusted attachment figure - is prophylactic.
7. **Hearing and sleep maintenance.** Hardware current, sleep architecture monitored, environments managed to reduce auditory strain.
8. **Anniversary vigilance.** Calendar the gamma-bomb date, Mar-Vell's death, his own deaths, and any other indexable trauma anniversaries. Increase contact in those windows.
9. **The lullaby protocol, inverted.** Someone in his life needs to know how to soothe him the way he soothes monsters. This is a learnable skill and should be taught to Marlo, to Banner, and to one Avengers-adjacent figure as a redundancy.
10. **Final-line protection.** If the debt-script, the Bucky vector, and a threat to Marlo are ever activated simultaneously by a hostile actor, the subject should be treated as compromised by default until extracted and stabilized. The combination is the keys-to-the-building. He cannot resist it. The protection is not in him; it must be in the people around him.

---

*End section. The subject's deepest vulnerability is also his deepest virtue: he is genuinely organized to serve, and the service is genuine. The file's purpose is to ensure that the service is never again stolen from him by people who learned which strings to pull. He has been used. He should be loved instead. The compendium exists so that the people who love him know what they are holding.*


## Strengths, Assets & Resilience

# SECTION 7 — STRENGTHS, ASSETS & RESILIENCE

*The positive ledger. Capabilities, resources, durable protective factors. What has kept the subject alive, functional, and morally intact across sixty years of conditions that have broken better-credentialed men.*

---

## 7.1 Foundational Resilience Factors

### 7.1.1 The Unbreakable Moral Spine

The single most consequential asset on the ledger, and the one most often overlooked because it presents as ordinary decency. The subject has been adjacent to, propositioned by, and pressured into virtually every category of moral compromise available in his operating environment: cosmic-scale utilitarian bargains (Thanos-tier "kill one to save trillions" framings), intelligence-service recruitments (the Whisperer file, S.H.I.E.L.D. liaison work, Hulkbusters-adjacent debriefings), the seductions of acquired power (the A-Bomb period, the Protector mantle, the Captain Marvel cosmic-awareness inheritance), and the entire range of disillusionment-into-cynicism pathways that destroy long-serving auxiliaries. He has not bent. Not once on a load-bearing question.

This is not naivete. The subject has read the room in every era he has occupied; he simply refuses to let the room determine his answer. The mechanism is identifiable: his moral compass is anchored *outside* the social field he is operating in, fixed instead to the original gamma-bomb scene and the obligation it installed. Because his ethics are wired to a non-negotiable trauma referent rather than to peer approval or institutional reward, ordinary corrupting pressures slide off him. This is, paradoxically, a healthy use of an unhealthy wound.

### 7.1.2 Loyalty as a Renewable Resource

Most operators in his environment exhaust their capacity for loyalty within a decade — betrayal accumulates, attachments calcify into wariness, and the warmth burns down to professional courtesy. The subject's loyalty has not depleted. He has been used by attachment figures (Mar-Vell's death left him fused to a corpse-state experientially; the Whisperer recruited him as an asset; Banner has weaponized their bond in at least three separate eras), and the loyalty regenerates. The supply is functionally infinite because it is sourced from the reparation drive, not from reciprocity expectations. He does not loan loyalty; he discharges it.

For an analyst, this is among the rarest and most operationally valuable traits a human asset can possess. It is also, as Section 8 will treat, his single greatest vulnerability — but as a capability it is unmatched.

### 7.1.3 The Lullaby Capacity

Itemized separately because it is genuinely sui generis. The subject can soothe the Hulk. This has been demonstrated across writers and decades and is not a writerly conceit — it is a real, transferable skill. The components, reconstructed from the behavioral record:
