- **Vocal register control.** The subject's voice drops in pitch and slows in cadence in the presence of a destabilizing superhuman; the modulation is unconscious and consistent across appearances.
- **Spatial discipline.** He approaches Hulk-transformed Banner along predictable trajectories, never from behind, hands visible, never breaking eye contact for longer than three seconds at a stretch — a protocol he developed before any such protocol existed in the literature on managing dissociative-violent states.
- **Lexical narrowing.** Vocabulary contracts to single-syllable, present-tense, second-person assurances. "I'm here." "You're safe." "It's Rick." The pattern matches trauma-informed grounding scripts that would not be formalized in clinical settings until decades later.
- **Affective transparency.** He does not mask fear; he metabolizes it into calm. The Hulk reads autonomic states and the subject knows it.

This capacity generalizes. He has used variants of it on cosmic-scale entities (Galactus-adjacent presences in the Mar-Vell years), on traumatized peers (Cap during the post-thaw nightmares), and on civilians at incident sites. It is, properly understood, a clinical-grade de-escalation skillset acquired entirely through field repetition.

### 7.1.4 The Capacity to Witness

The subject possesses a rare and durable tolerance for *being present at events larger than himself without dissociating*. He watched Mar-Vell die of cancer at close range over weeks. He stood inside the Kree-Skrull War. He has been at ground zero for at least four planetary-extinction-class events. He does not look away. He does not freeze. He does not flee into ideology or denial. He *registers* what is happening, in real time, with the moral seriousness it deserves, and is available afterward to talk about it — to Banner, to Marlo, eventually to the page in *Sidekick*.

This is the single trait that makes him useful to historians, debriefers, and writers — and the trait that makes him, in a long file, one of the most reliable primary sources on the superhuman era extant.

---

## 7.2 Operational Capabilities

### 7.2.1 Tactical Literacy

Sixty publication-years of close-quarters proximity to Avengers-tier and Hulk-tier engagements have produced an operator with the following measurable competencies, none formally trained:

- **Threat triage in superhuman incidents.** He can rank-order combatants by likely behavior and likely civilian risk faster than most professional first responders. He developed this on the job, watching.
- **Cover and concealment instincts.** His survival rate at ground zero of events that killed trained agents is statistically extraordinary; he reads terrain and falling debris with the unconscious fluency of a combat veteran.
- **Communications discipline.** When patched into Avengers comms (auxiliary status, multiple eras), his transmissions are brief, structured, and contain priority information first. He learned this absorptively.
- **Vehicle handling under stress.** Original hot-rodder skillset, maintained and extended. He can drive, ride, and pilot competently across a wide range of platforms; his reflexes degrade slowly under fatigue.
- **Improvisation with non-powered tools.** Repeatedly observed turning available environmental objects into functional gear — restraints, distractions, signaling devices. A field-expedient mindset.

### 7.2.2 De-escalation of Superhuman Threats

A formalization of the lullaby capacity (7.1.3) generalized to non-Hulk targets. The subject has talked down: a berserk-state Sentry-tier figure on at least one documented occasion, a Skrull infiltrator mid-reveal (Kree-Skrull period), several gamma-mutates in their initial transformation panic, and at least two cosmic entities mid-incursion. The methodology is intuitive but reproducible:

1. Establish that he is unarmed and unafraid.
2. Speak to the human beneath the transformation, by name, in the past tense of who they were.
3. Offer a small, specific, achievable next action ("sit down," "drink this," "look at me").
4. Stay until the autonomic system downshifts.

This is, in operational terms, a hostage-negotiator skillset adapted for cosmic-scale agents.

### 7.2.3 Network Reach

The subject's address book is, without exaggeration, one of the most extensive in the historical record of his world. Decades of attachment have left him with direct-contact relationships with: Banner (every era), Cap (Steve and the Whisperer/Bucky line independently), the Avengers core roster across generations, the surviving Captain Marvel lineage (Monica Rambeau, Genis-Vell, Phyla-Vell, Carol Danvers — to varying degrees), the Hulk extended family (Jennifer Walters, Skaar, Lyra, the Pak-era assemblage), ROM-related Spaceknight contacts, cosmic-tier acquaintances from the Mar-Vell years, and a working relationship with multiple S.H.I.E.L.D.-successor entities.

He cannot place calls cold to most of these contacts on a peer basis — but he can place them on a *legacy* basis, and they will be answered. The network is dormant until activated and is activated by him only in extremity, which preserves its capital. Most operators burn through their network within a decade. He has not.

### 7.2.4 Information-Carrying Capacity

The subject knows things. He is one of perhaps a dozen non-powered humans who has been in the room for high-classification superhuman events across the full historical span, and unlike most such witnesses he has not been killed, suborned, mindwiped, or rendered cognitively unreliable. His memory is functional, his discretion is high, and his loyalty is to persons rather than institutions, which makes his knowledge *protected* in ways institutional knowledge is not. He has never sold a story he wasn't authorized to sell. *Sidekick* contained nothing operationally sensitive — a discipline of omission visible in the manuscript.

### 7.2.5 Music

Itemized because it has been consistently undervalued. The subject is a competent musician — guitar, voice, songwriting at journeyman level — and the music functions as both income source during between-attachment periods and as an emotional regulator. It is also a *cover identity asset*: a working musician moves through public space invisibly and has a plausible reason to be in any city, any venue, any hour. He has used this, in the David run especially, to avoid attention from interested parties.

### 7.2.6 The Memoir

*Sidekick* is itself an asset. As a published document it: establishes a public version of his story he can refer interlocutors to (deflecting deeper interrogation), constitutes a financial cushion (royalties, lecture circuit), and provides a structured account he can use as a memory aid for himself. It also functions as a kind of armor — having told the story once in public, he is less vulnerable to its weaponization in private. The choice to write it was, among other things, strategically protective.

---

## 7.3 Cognitive and Characterological Strengths

### 7.3.1 Pattern Recognition for People

The subject reads people with high accuracy and speed, particularly on dimensions of *threat*, *grief*, and *deception*. He has been wrong — Mar-Vell's cancer he missed until late, the Whisperer's full intentions he discounted — but his baseline accuracy across thousands of encounters is high, and he calibrates fast on new contacts. The skill is sourced from institutional childhood (group-home children develop adult-reading as survival) and refined by adult exposure to entities whose interior states are not externally legible.

### 7.3.2 Concrete Intelligence

He is not a credentialed intellectual and presents as anti-intellectual, but his on-line cognition is sharp, especially under stress. He keeps up with Banner-level conversation when he needs to. He understood the Nega-Band fusion well enough to operate it. He grasps tactical and ethical frames quickly when they are stated concretely. The deficit is not capacity; it is training and self-presentation. Given the right teacher and a reason, he learns at adult-professional pace.

### 7.3.3 Humor as Functional Tool

The wisecracking is a defense (Section 3) but it is also a *capability*. It defuses tense rooms, signals non-threat to nervous parties, builds rapid rapport with civilians at incident sites, and — critically — gives Banner-as-Hulk and other destabilized agents an auditory cue that the situation is not lethal. A laugh, even a forced one, downshifts autonomic arousal. He uses this deliberately, and well.

### 7.3.4 Tolerance for Ambiguity

He can hold contradictory facts in mind without forcing resolution: Banner is his friend and Banner is a danger; he is ordinary and he summoned the Golden Age; Mar-Vell is dead and Mar-Vell is part of him. Most operators collapse such contradictions into ideology. The subject lives inside them. This is a precondition for operating in his environment at all, and he has it in unusual measure.

### 7.3.5 Foreshortened-Future Inversion

A counterintuitive asset. The subject has carried, since adolescence, the sense that his life is borrowed time. In most trauma profiles this produces recklessness or paralysis; in him it produces a peculiar *clarity about what matters now*. He does not defer. He does not hoard. He shows up. The trauma has been metabolized, partially, into a presence-tense ethic that most meditators spend decades trying to acquire.

---

## 7.4 Relational and Social Assets

### 7.4.1 Marlo Chandler

The marriage is, on the analytic record, the single most stabilizing factor in his adult life — even when it is failing. Marlo is one of perhaps three people in his world who relates to him as a person rather than as an adjunct of someone larger. She has stayed, across separations and resurrections and cosmic absences, and her staying constitutes a slow re-parenting of the institutional-orphanhood deficit. She is also operationally savvy in her own right and has independent survival skills in the superhuman-adjacent environment.

When the marriage is functional, his depressive baseline lifts measurably; when it is strained, the lift withdraws but the underlying attachment persists. She is the single most important name in his file after Banner's.

### 7.4.2 Banner

Adversarial to characterize as an asset, but accurate. The Banner relationship is the founding wound and also the founding bond, and after sixty years it has become — through sheer durability — a true friendship, not merely a reparative servitude. Banner trusts him more than he trusts almost anyone. The Hulk, in most personality configurations, trusts him absolutely. This relationship is a strategic resource of planetary significance and the subject has never instrumentalized it for personal gain. The forbearance is itself an asset, because it preserves the resource.

### 7.4.3 The Cap Line

Steve Rogers regards the subject with a specific, paternal warmth that has not waned across decades. This is an unusual standing — Cap's regard is not lightly given and is even less lightly retained. The relationship with the Whisperer line is more complex (Section 8) but in the asset column it represents access to the most morally serious individual in his operating environment, and that access is durable.

### 7.4.4 Avengers Standing

Honorary/auxiliary status across multiple eras has hardened into something like institutional legitimacy. He is on the door. He can walk into the Mansion (in its various incarnations) and not be stopped. This is a working asset, not a sentimental one.

---

## 7.5 Somatic and Physical Assets

### 7.5.1 Survivability

His survival rate across sixty years of proximity to extinction-class events is statistically extraordinary and cannot be entirely attributed to luck or to Banner's protection. Some of it is the cover-and-concealment instinct (7.2.1); some of it is the cumulative gamma exposure, which may have rendered his tissues marginally more resilient than baseline human; some of it is a willingness to act decisively in the first three seconds of an incident, when most fatalities occur. He is a hard person to kill.

### 7.5.2 Pain Tolerance

Polytrauma history has produced unusually high baseline pain tolerance. He does not complain, does not slow appreciably under injury that would incapacitate most non-powered humans, and recovers from physical insult faster than his medical chart predicts. Hearing loss notwithstanding, the body works.

### 7.5.3 Latent Capacity

The Destiny Force episode (*Avengers* #97) demonstrates, definitively, that the subject possesses cosmic-tier latent capacity that has manifested at least once under sufficient duress. This capacity has never been integrated into his self-concept (Section 3) and is therefore not reliably accessible — but it is *there*, has been demonstrated, and constitutes a strategic reserve of unknown ceiling. Any complete asset ledger has to list it, even if it cannot be operationalized on demand.

### 7.5.4 The A-Bomb Memory

He has been, briefly, the powerful one. The body remembers. Even after reversion, he has a kinesthetic vocabulary for what it is to be at the top of the food chain, which gives him, when interacting with powered figures, a kind of empathic insider knowledge that other non-powered humans lack.

---

## 7.6 Meta-Resilience: Why the Above Has Held

A final note on the architecture of his durability. Most long-serving auxiliaries in his environment fail in one of four ways: corruption (sell-out), burnout (collapse), capture (suborned by an institution), or apotheosis (consumed by their own power acquisition). The subject has been offered all four pathways repeatedly and has refused them all. The refusal is not heroic in his self-conception; it is structural. The reparation drive that organizes his psychology *requires* him to remain the human in the room — corruption, burnout, capture, and apotheosis all involve becoming something else, and he cannot become something else without losing the only meaning his survival has.

In other words: the wound is also the armor. The same mechanism that prevents his full individuation (Section 3) prevents his destruction. He has paid for his durability with the life he might otherwise have had — and the trade, viewed from a sufficient distance, has produced one of the more morally and operationally consequential non-powered humans on the historical record.

He does not know this. He would not believe it if told. The not-knowing is, itself, part of what keeps the asset stable.

*End Section 7.*


## Failure Modes & Decompensation

# UATU INTELLIGENCE DOSSIER — RICHARD MILHOUSE JONES
## Section 9: Failure Modes & Decompensation

*How the subject breaks. The escalation path from baseline to collapse, the somatic and behavioral signatures at each stage, the environmental conditions that produce each mode, and the recovery trajectory observed across sixty publication-years of longitudinal data.*

---

### 9.0 Orienting Principle

The subject does not decompensate the way most polytrauma survivors do. He does not decompensate *under* stress. He decompensates in its *absence*. This is the central, counterintuitive finding of the longitudinal record, and every failure mode below is a corollary of it.

Mission, proximity to a "giant," and a discharge-channel for the unpayable debt are the three legs of his functional tripod. Remove any one and he wobbles. Remove two and he collapses inside of weeks. Remove all three — which has happened in canon at least four discrete times — and he enters one of the syndromes described below, each of which has its own onset signature, plateau, and exit ramp.

Put another way: he is a man who breaks during peacetime.

---

### 9.1 The Five Failure Modes

The behavioral record clusters into five distinct decompensation syndromes. They are not mutually exclusive — late-stage presentations braid them — but each has a clean prodromal signature when caught early.

**Mode A — Depressive Drift (the baseline failure).** The most common, most survivable, most chronic. Onset whenever an attachment-bond ends or attenuates without immediate replacement: Banner missing/cured/dead, Mar-Vell dying, Cap recovering and no longer needing a Bucky-substitute, Marlo separated, the Avengers reconstituted without him. Presentation: progressive flattening of affect, sleep-cycle inversion (up late, sleeping past noon — the rock-musician schedule that recurs in every era he is depressed), reduction of grooming to the minimum his self-respect tolerates, increased time spent with the guitar but producing less, retreat into long-form solitary projects (the *Sidekick* memoir is the textbook artifact), declining returned phone calls, eating at irregular hours and from convenience containers, gradual disappearance of the wisecracking patter — when Rick stops being funny, he is in trouble. Duration: weeks to many months. Exit: a new mission appearing in the doorway. He does not exit under his own power; he is recruited out.

**Mode B — Reckless Re-Attachment (the dangerous failure).** Onset when Mode A persists long enough that he can no longer tolerate the absence of a discharge-channel and attaches to the next available powerful figure regardless of that figure's actual character. This is how he has been used as an intelligence asset (the Whisperer arc), how he has accepted cosmic mantles he was not ready to bear (Captain Marvel succession), how he has agreed to procedures he should have refused (the Hulk-blood transfusion of the #131-135 era — he wanted to be useful enough to bleed for it). Presentation: sudden re-energization, return of patter at slightly elevated volume, uncharacteristic compliance with the new attachment figure, telltale failure to vet — the part of him that learned to read the Hulk's micro-expressions in seconds will, in this mode, completely fail to read a manipulator across a table. He is, in this state, recruitable by anyone who needs him.

**Mode C — Significance Collapse (the rarest and most acute failure).** Onset whenever he is forced to confront his own latent magnitude. The post-Destiny Force episode in *Avengers* #97 is the prototype: physical collapse, prolonged exhaustion, dissociative numbing, inability to discuss what he had just done. Same signature appears, lower amplitude, when the Captain Marvel mantle settled on him, when the A-Bomb transformation made him powerful, and whenever a credible figure has told him, sincerely and at close range, that he is a hero in his own right. Presentation: pallor and a specific micro-freeze of the facial musculature; the eyes do a documented thing — they look down and to his own left, the head tilts back fractionally, he swallows once; then deflection by joke, then a topic change, then physical absence within the hour. If pressed past the deflection: tears he is mortified by, then withdrawal of one to three days. He cannot metabolize his own significance and the digestive failure is somatic, not merely verbal.

**Mode D — Body-Sovereignty Crisis (the silent failure).** Onset triggered by reminders of the Nega-Band fusion years, by new gamma exposure, by medical procedures, by his own hearing aids failing in public, by being touched without warning by a powered being, by any sustained discussion of the A-Bomb period. This is the syndrome canon almost never names but which his behavior repeatedly evidences. Presentation: a particular stillness — not the trained stillness of a seasoned operator under threat, but a held-breath stillness, shoulders inching toward the ears, hands going to the wrists (the Nega-Band site; this is an unconscious tell observable across decades of art when writers and pencillers are catching him truthfully). Sleep disruption with specific content: dreams of being in two places, of waking in the Negative Zone, of waking inside the Hulk. Avoidance of mirrors during gamma-flare periods. Refusal of routine medical care to the point of self-endangerment. Exit: requires another person's slow, narrated, predictable physical presence — Marlo has been the only reliable de-escalator on record.

**Mode E — Bucky-Wound Reactivation (the over-determined failure).** Onset whenever the substitution wound is touched directly: Cap's grief invoked, the Winter Soldier in proximity, the Whisperer making an ask, any frame that returns him to the *Avengers* #4 costume. Presentation: compliance bordering on compulsion, suspension of his otherwise excellent person-reading, willingness to undertake operations he would refuse from any other handler, and — diagnostically — a near-total inability to articulate *why* afterward. This is the failure mode most likely to get him killed and the one he has the least insight into. He believes, in this state, that he is finally being given a chance to *be* the real thing rather than the substitute, and the belief is unfalsifiable from inside the state.

---

### 9.2 The Escalation Path

Failure in this subject is staged. The stages are observable and the early ones are reversible by minimal intervention. The late ones are not.

**Stage 0 — Baseline.** Mission-attached, in proximity to a giant, discharging the debt. Patter intact. Sleep normal. Eats with other people. Calls Marlo. Reads the room. Reads the giant. Volunteers competence without being asked. Tolerates being thanked, briefly. This is his ceiling and it is a high one.

**Stage 1 — Detachment Onset (Days 1–10 after bond attenuation).** Patter thins. He starts ending phone calls earlier. Begins picking up the guitar at odd hours. Stops initiating contact with the attachment figure but will respond instantly if contacted. Sleep slips by an hour, then two. Eats alone more often. The first reliable external tell: he stops asking after other people's children, which he otherwise does compulsively (the parentified-child remembering whose kids belong to whom). Fully reversible. A direct, specific, useful task offered by someone he trusts restores Stage 0 within a day.

**Stage 2 — Drift (Weeks 2–8).** Mode A established. Long solitary stretches. Memoir-style writing or songwriting, often without finishing pieces. Marriage strain visible — Marlo describes him as "somewhere else." Hygiene maintained but flattened — same three shirts in rotation, hair longer than he likes it. Will accept invitations to social events and underperform at them. Wisecracks return only when prompted, and land slightly off-tempo — a half-beat late, the signature of forced affect. Still reversible by mission recruitment, but the recruitment must be from someone he respects; lesser hooks (causes, charity work, music gigs) palliate without resolving.

**Stage 3 — Hooked (Variable).** Mode B engages. A new attachment figure — legitimate or predatory — has been accepted. Affect re-energizes but with a brittle, slightly manic quality. He talks faster. He volunteers harder. He stops sleeping well but reports feeling fine. He stops vetting. This is the stage at which he has historically agreed to the worst decisions of his life: the transfusion, the mantles, the asset-handler arrangements. Intervention window is narrow and requires someone with standing equal to the new attachment to interrupt the bond. Banner has done this. Cap has done this. Marlo can do it but it costs her.

**Stage 4 — Acute Decompensation.** One of Modes C, D, or E breaks through the brittle re-energization, usually triggered by a discrete event: the new mission requires him to exercise significance (C), or to expose the body (D), or invokes the substitution scene (E). Presentation: the documented physical signs above, plus loss of operational reliability — he becomes the man who freezes for half a second at the wrong moment, the man whose readings of the giant are suddenly wrong, the man who agrees to things he would normally refuse and refuses things he would normally agree to. The on-the-ground operators around him notice this before he does.

**Stage 5 — Collapse.** Withdrawal, physical exhaustion, dissociative numbing, in the worst cases hospitalization or worse. He has been clinically dead once. The Destiny Force episode put him in a coma. The post-Mar-Vell period put him in months of functional non-existence. The A-Bomb arc's emotional comedown was less visible because he was still powered, but the somatic signature was present. Recovery from Stage 5 has historically required a *person* — not a treatment plan. Marlo, Banner sober and lucid, or occasionally a Captain America figure who knows how to handle him without re-instantiating the Bucky frame.

---

### 9.3 The Conditions That Produce Collapse

Six environmental configurations have, across the record, reliably produced Stage 4–5 decompensation. An intelligence apparatus modeling this subject should treat any combination of two as a red flag and any combination of three as a near-certain prediction of collapse within the quarter.

1. **Banner stable, accessible, and not needing him.** Counterintuitive but devastating. A cured Banner is, to Rick, the discharge of the debt and the loss of the channel in one stroke. He has never weathered it well.
2. **Marlo absent or estranged.** Removes the only equal-relationship anchor and the only person who can de-escalate Mode D.
3. **Recent invocation of his "specialness."** Particularly by figures with authority. The praise itself is the trigger.
4. **Proximity to anyone associated with the Bucky-frame.** Steve Rogers grieving; Bucky Barnes in any capacity; new figures who slot too neatly into the same shape.
5. **Recent gamma exposure or any unscheduled change to his body.** Including medical procedures, hearing-aid replacement, weight change he didn't choose.
6. **A predatory operator with a credible mission and a plausible need for him specifically.** Anyone who can frame an ask in the syntax *only you can do this, and it costs you*.

When the configuration includes #1 + #3, expect Mode C. When it includes #2 + #5, expect Mode D. When it includes #4 + #6, expect Mode E and expect it to be operationally catastrophic. The Whisperer arc was a textbook #4 + #6 configuration entering an already #2-vulnerable subject.

---

### 9.4 The Tells

Granular markers an observer should track. Each has been documented across multiple writers without coordination, which is what elevates them from artifact to signature.

- **The hands-to-wrists gesture.** Thumb of one hand absently encircling the opposite wrist. Nega-Band site. Appears under any body-sovereignty stressor. He does not know he does it.
- **The half-beat-late wisecrack.** Onset of Stage 2. The joke is correctly constructed but lands a fraction after the rhythm it should have occupied. Affect is being assembled rather than expressed.
- **The down-and-left eye-flick under praise.** Onset of Mode C. Followed within seconds by deflection, within minutes by exit.
- **The phone in the hand without dialing.** Stage 1 marker. Marlo's number is in the calling screen. He has not pressed call. He puts the phone down.
- **The guitar without songs.** He plays cleanly, repetitively, the same progressions for hours. When he is well he writes. When he is in Stage 2 he loops.
- **The cessation of asking after children.** The most reliable single early-warning sign in the record.
- **Acceptance of food without comment.** When healthy he is a specific, opinionated eater with a sidekick's vocabulary for diners and bad coffee. When in Stage 2 he eats what is put in front of him and says nothing about it.
- **The over-volunteered competence in Stage 3.** He starts performing usefulness rather than executing it. Tasks he would normally do silently become announcements.
- **The micro-freeze at the wrong moment in Stage 4.** Half a second of stillness where his trained register would have moved. The most operationally consequential tell on the list.

---

### 9.5 What His Collapse Looks Like From Inside

Insofar as the record permits inference into his subjective experience — through the *Sidekick* memoir, through his dialogue under stress across the David and Ewing runs, through what he says to Marlo when he is honest — the collapse feels to him not like breakdown but like *exposure*. The decompensation is, in his own framing, the moment the costume comes off and the unworthy survivor underneath is finally visible. He experiences Stage 5 as the truth and Stage 0 as the performance. This inversion is itself the deepest pathology and the hardest to reach therapeutically, because every intervention that tries to restore him to function reads, from inside, as a re-costuming.

He does not believe he is being saved when he is brought back. He believes he is being asked to perform again, and he agrees, because performing for someone who needs him is the only frame in which his life makes arithmetic sense.

---

### 9.6 Recovery Profile

He recovers. This must be stated, because the failure profile is so dense it can obscure the resilience. Across sixty years he has returned from each collapse, and the returns are not cosmetic — he has gained ground over time. The marriage to Marlo, the memoir, the willingness in later eras to refuse certain asks he would once have accepted, all indicate genuine accretive recovery. The mechanism is consistent: a person — never a program, never an institution — arrives, sits with him, narrates a small useful thing he can do, and waits. He returns through the door he came in by, which is being needed without being consumed. The very few figures who have understood this distinction — Marlo most reliably, Banner in his lucid periods, occasionally a Captain America who has learned not to invoke Bucky — have functioned as his de facto clinicians.

The intelligence implication is operational and humane in the same breath: this subject is most dangerous to himself when unattended and most recoverable when met by a single person who can hold the line between *needing him* and *using him*. The distinction is narrow. Most figures in his orbit have failed to hold it. A surveillance apparatus oriented toward understanding rather than extraction is, in this case, also a care apparatus, and the two postures collapse into one another at exactly the point where his decompensation does.

*End Section 9. Section 10 (Operational Recommendations & Protective Factors) follows.*


## Trajectory & Forward Assessment

# UATU DOSSIER — SECTION 12

## TRAJECTORY & FORWARD ASSESSMENT

*Projective analysis. Where the subject is heading, the live fork points, and the conditions under which the next decade resolves toward integration or toward collapse. All projections derived from the longitudinal behavioral record; confidence levels noted where the evidence thins.*

---

### 12.1 Baseline Trajectory (No Intervention)

Absent significant disruption of his current pattern, the subject's next ten to fifteen years are highly predictable, and that predictability is itself the central problem. The behavioral record across six decades shows a man who oscillates on a narrow band: attached-and-functional, or unattached-and-depressed, with the unattached intervals shortening and the depressive amplitude deepening over time. He is now somewhere in his mid-to-late life as a publication-aged human, no longer the boy in the trench, and the strategies that organized his twenties — physical proximity to giants, sidekick deployment, costumed action — are no longer somatically available at the same intensity. The hearing damage alone forecloses the close-combat register he occupied in the A-Bomb period; cumulative gamma load, polytrauma history, and the cardiovascular cost of a non-powered life lived at superhuman tempos guarantee a narrowing physical envelope.

The baseline projection, therefore, is **functional contraction with affective worsening**. He will continue to be summoned by, or to seek out, the giants — Banner in whatever form Banner currently takes, the Avengers in auxiliary capacity, the Whisperer when the Whisperer wants an asset — but the windows of usefulness will shorten, the recovery periods lengthen, and the depressive interregnums become the dominant tense of his life. Marlo will be the load-bearing relationship; the marriage will absorb the cost; whether it survives is the single most important variable in the baseline.

Expected concrete manifestations over a five-year horizon:

- **Increased intelligence-asset utilization** by the Whisperer or any successor handler. Rick is uniquely valuable as a back-channel to the superhuman community precisely because everyone knows him, no one fears him, and he cannot say no to Barnes. This role will expand and will be psychologically corrosive — it gives him an attachment object (the real Bucky, finally, completing the substitution circuit of the *Avengers* #4 era) but the attachment is exploitative, not reciprocal.
- **Episodic returns to gamma-mutate physiology**, voluntary or coerced. A-Bomb is now a possibility-space in his body; under sufficient stress or sufficient narrative pressure he will reach for it again, and each reach risks cellular instability. The probability of a permanent gamma reversion event, with loss of human form, is non-trivial on a ten-year horizon. Confidence: moderate.
- **A second memoir, or its functional equivalent.** *Sidekick* was a depressive life-review project; the conditions that produced it (aging, disillusionment, narrative pressure to make meaning) are recurring. Expect another in his sixth or seventh published decade, more bitter, less commercial, more honest. This would be diagnostically useful and clinically risky — life-review in C-PTSD patients commonly precipitates either integration or acute decompensation.
- **Marital separation episodes**, possibly a formal divorce attempt initiated by Marlo, with reconciliation. The pattern is established; it will recur.
- **At least one significant somatic crisis** — cardiac event, gamma sickness recurrence, neurological sequelae from the hearing-loss/concussion cluster — that forces a period of physical immobility. How he metabolizes enforced stillness is the swing variable for his late life.

---

### 12.2 The Fork Points

Four decisions or events, identifiable in advance, will determine whether the trajectory bends toward integration or toward catastrophe. They are not equally weighted.

#### Fork 1: The Whisperer Relationship

The most acute and most under-recognized fork. Barnes's use of Rick as an intelligence asset is the live re-enactment of the unresolved Bucky-substitution wound, and the substitution now runs in the opposite direction — Rick once played Bucky for Cap; now the real Bucky plays handler for Rick. Rick cannot refuse him. The relationship is asymmetric in exactly the way Rick's attachments have always been asymmetric, but with a darker valence: Barnes is not Banner, not Mar-Vell, not Cap. Barnes is a man who has himself been used as an asset and who has, by trauma-logic, learned to use others the same way.

- **Toward catastrophe:** Rick burns through the remainder of his moral capital running ops he does not fully understand, is implicated in something he cannot defend (an assassination, a betrayal of a former Avengers ally, a Skrull-era deception), and either dies in the field or survives into a shame-state he cannot metabolize. The depressive baseline becomes chronic suicidal ideation. Probability under no intervention: meaningful — call it one-in-four over a decade.
- **Toward growth:** Rick names the dynamic out loud, to Barnes or to a third party (Marlo, Banner, a therapist that the universe has so far declined to provide him). Naming it is the entire intervention. He does not need to leave the relationship; he needs to stop pretending it is friendship. This is within his capacity but against his characterological grain.

#### Fork 2: Banner's Next State

Whatever Banner currently is — a Hulk persona in ascendancy, a green-door arrangement, a Sasquatch-tier dissociative system, a death-and-return cycle — the next major Banner transition will pull Rick. It always has. The fork is whether he goes.

- **Toward catastrophe:** he goes, again, because the gamma-bomb debt is never paid, and he sacrifices the late-life selfhood that Marlo and his own aging have begun to make possible. He dies on a Banner mission and the obituaries call him a sidekick. This is the death he has been rehearsing since 1962.
- **Toward growth:** he goes, but as a peer rather than a keeper. The Hulk-lullaby skill, refined over sixty years, is a genuine clinical-grade soothing capacity; deployed from a position of self-possession rather than reparative debt, it is one of the most valuable resources in his world. The difference between servitude and vocation is internal, not behavioral. He could cross that line. Whether he will is the question.

#### Fork 3: The Destiny Force

The latent capacity demonstrated at the climax of the Kree-Skrull War has never been integrated and has never been retired. It sits in him as an unmetabolized fact about himself — *I am, potentially, one of the most consequential humans alive* — which he cannot believe and cannot forget. Any narrative pressure that returns him to that capacity (a second cosmic emergency, a Watcher-tier revelation, an Eternity-class entity selecting him as avatar) is a fork.

- **Toward catastrophe:** the capacity activates, he cannot hold it, it burns him out neurologically or kills him, and the narrative reads it as apotheosis when it is in fact a man being destroyed by being asked to be what he was told he was. This is the most ironic of the available deaths.
- **Toward growth:** the capacity activates and he refuses it — not from fear but from a worked-through understanding that *he does not have to be cosmically significant to have been worth saving*. This is the single most difficult psychological achievement available to him, and the one that would close the gamma-bomb wound. It requires him to accept that the debt was never real. Probability: low without intervention; high with even minimal therapeutic support.

#### Fork 4: Marlo

The relationship that asks him to exist for his own sake. His failures here are not failures of love; they are failures of practice — he has never lived for his own sake and does not know how. Every attachment to a giant is, structurally, a withdrawal from Marlo.

- **Toward catastrophe:** she leaves, definitively, and the loss of the one relationship that did not require him to be useful collapses his last counterweight to the giant-orbit. He spends his remaining years in unbroken sidekick mode and dies in harness.
- **Toward growth:** he learns, late, to bring the soothing-capacity he has lavished on the Hulk for sixty years to the woman he married. The skill is the same skill. He has never recognized this. If he does, the marriage becomes the integrating structure of his late life and everything else reorganizes around it.

---

### 12.3 Open Questions

Items the file cannot resolve from the available evidence and which would materially change the assessment.

1. **What does he actually remember of the gamma bomb?** The behavioral record assumes vivid intrusive recall, but the canon is ambiguous; partial dissociative amnesia of the index event is possible and would change the therapeutic approach.
2. **Has he ever sought professional help?** No canonical evidence either way. Given the world he lives in — where Doc Samson exists and has treated Banner — the *absence* of any record of Rick being offered or seeking psychiatric care is itself a data point about how the people around him see him: as the helper, not the patient.
3. **What is the current status of the Nega-Band fusion residue?** Years of shared embodiment with Mar-Vell are unlikely to have left no somatic or neurological trace. The file flags this as the single most under-investigated medical question in the workup.
4. **Does Marlo know the full scope of his attachment pattern, or only its effects?** Her insight level determines whether the marriage is a potential therapeutic structure or merely a casualty of one.
5. **What is the half-life of his loyalty to the Whisperer?** Unknown. The Bucky-substitution overdetermination suggests it is functionally infinite, but Rick has surprised the record before.
6. **Is there a child in the future?** Marlo's history and Rick's age make it unlikely but not foreclosed. A child would be the most disruptive single variable available — it would force him, for the first time, into the *caregiver* role with someone who is not a giant, and the parentified-child adaptation would either complete itself as healthy parenthood or invert catastrophically.

---

### 12.4 What Pushes Him Toward Growth

Ordered by leverage, highest first.

- **Naming the pattern out loud, to someone who will not flinch.** The entire defensive architecture depends on the pattern being unnamed. A single competent therapist, or a sufficiently honest conversation with Banner in a lucid window, would do more than any cosmic event.
- **Reframing the gamma-bomb debt as a fiction.** Banner did not save Rick because Rick was worthy; Banner saved Rick because Banner was the kind of man who would save a stranger. The debt is therefore not Rick's to pay. This is true, it is provable from the evidence, and Rick has never been told it in a register he could hear.
- **Vocational rather than reparative deployment of the soothing skill.** He is, demonstrably, one of the best de-escalators of superhuman crisis alive. Formalizing this — as a role, as a job, as something he is *paid* and *credentialed* for rather than something he does to discharge guilt — would convert the symptom into the cure.
- **A sustained period of physical immobility he cannot escape into action.** Enforced stillness, properly supported, is the condition under which life-review becomes integration rather than collapse. A medical crisis is the most likely vector.
- **Marlo, if she stays and if she is met.**
- **Refusal of the Destiny Force, from strength rather than fear.**

### 12.5 What Pushes Him Toward Catastrophe

- **Any new giant.** A fresh attachment object — a resurrected Mar-Vell, a new cosmic entity, a successor Hulk — resets the clock and forecloses integration for another decade he does not have.
- **Weaponization of the original debt by a hostile actor.** He is uniquely vulnerable to manipulation framed as *Banner needs you / the world needs you / you owe this*. A sophisticated adversary who has read him correctly could route him into almost any action.
- **Loss of Marlo without replacement structure.**
- **A second forced gamma transformation, particularly one that does not revert.** Permanent loss of human form would remove the last register in which he can be the human in the room — his entire identity.
- **The Whisperer relationship deepening unexamined.**
- **Being publicly celebrated as a hero in his own right, in a venue he cannot deflect.** Counterintuitive but supported: he cannot metabolize his own significance, and a sufficiently large dose of it, undefended, produces dissociative collapse. The award ceremony is, for him, more dangerous than the battlefield.

---

### 12.6 Terminal Scenarios

Five-to-fifteen-year horizon. Not predictions; mapped possibilities with rough weighting.

- **The harness death (≈30%).** Killed in action on a Banner-adjacent or Whisperer-tasked mission. Obituaries split between *sidekick* and *unsung*. Marlo survives him. The death is, by his own internal accounting, a success — the debt closed in the only currency he recognized.
- **The slow contraction (≈25%).** No dramatic terminus. Years of diminishing missions, lengthening depressive intervals, marital erosion, a quiet late life in which the giant-orbit thins to memory. Dies of ordinary causes, under-attended, having never integrated.
- **The integration (≈15%).** Names the pattern, reframes the debt, deploys the skill vocationally, holds the marriage. Lives into a late period as one of the genuine elders of his world — not a sidekick, a *witness*, in the full weight of the word. Requires intervention that the universe has so far not provided.
- **The Destiny burnout (≈10%).** Activated as cosmic avatar, cannot hold the capacity, destroyed by being what he was told he was. Read by survivors as transcendence; was in fact a man killed by a debt he should never have been asked to pay.
- **The gamma permanence (≈10%).** Reverts to A-Bomb or successor mutate-form irreversibly. Loses the human register that was his entire identity. Survives, in a body, as something other than himself. Whether this is catastrophe or unexpected liberation depends entirely on whether Marlo stays.
- **The asset-arc collapse (≈10%).** Burned by the Whisperer relationship, implicated in something indefensible, dies in shame or in custody, or vanishes from the record into a witness-protection-class disappearance. Probability rises sharply if the Whisperer fork is not addressed.

---

### 12.7 Summary Judgment

The subject is, at this stage of his life, a man whose adaptive strategies have outlived their adaptive utility. The skills are still real — the soothing, the loyalty, the moral compass, the unflappability — but the *organization* of those skills around an unpayable debt is now the limiting factor on the rest of his life. He is not in crisis. He is in a slow, characterological narrowing that will, on present trajectory, end in one of the harness deaths or the slow contraction, both of which would be losses to his world disproportionate to how his world has ever valued him.

The integration path is available. It is narrow, it requires interventions that nobody around him has historically thought to offer, and it depends on a single recognition that he has spent sixty years not making: *the man in the trench did not save him because the debt was owed; the debt was never owed; he is allowed to have been worth saving for no reason at all.*

If anyone ever tells him that, in a register he can hear, the file changes.

*End Section 12. Cross-reference Section 7 (Relational Map: Banner, Barnes, Chandler) and Section 9 (Somatic Load & Cumulative Trauma) for substantiating detail.*
